Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The Four Categories of Leftover Water (Su'r) in Hanafi Fiqh
Classifies leftover water into four categories with rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of su'r (leftover water) according to the Hanafi school and identify the ruling (tahir, najis, makruh, mashkuk) for each animal's leftover water.

Core Idea
Su'r ruling depends on the animal: pure from humans/horses, impure from dogs/pigs, disliked from cats, doubtful from donkeys.

This passage from Nur al-Idah classifies leftover water (su'r) from animals into four precise categories, each with a distinct legal ruling. Understanding this classification is essential for determining the validity of wudu and purification when using water that an animal has drunk from. We will break down each category, the animals it includes, and the legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify scope: Su'r applies only to little water
First, note that su'r rulings only apply to water that is 'little' (qalil), defined as less than 10 x 10 cubits and not flowing. Large or flowing water does not take the ruling of su'r.
Little water is any stagnant pool smaller than 10x10 cubits.
2
List the four categories and their defining animals
The passage divides su'r into four types: (1) pure and purifying (tahir mutahhir), (2) impure by consensus (najis), (3) disliked if other water is available (makruh tanzihan), and (4) doubtful (mashkuk). Identify which animals fall into each category.
Memorize the animals for each category: pure: human, horse, halal meat; impure: dog, pig, beasts of prey; disliked: cat, free-roaming hen, birds of prey, house-dwelling mice; doubtful: mule, donkey.
3
Note conditions and exceptions for each category
For humans, the leftover water is pure only if the mouth is free from impurity (e.g., from wine or vomit). For cats, only domestic cats are disliked; wild cats are impure. If an animal is a jallalah (eats filth), its su'r becomes disliked even if it normally is pure.
The ruling for cats is based on the 'illa of roaming around the house.
4
Understand the doubtful category (mashkuk)
For mules and donkeys, the water is doubtful: one must perform wudu with it and also do tayammum as a precaution, then pray. This is not because the ruling is unknown, but due to conflicting evidence; it ensures certainty of purification.
The term 'mashkuk' does not mean ignorance; it is a precautionary ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة
بيان أحكام السؤر
وكان راكدا قليلا - والقليل ما دون عشر في عشر – فينجس وإن لم يظهر أثرها [؟] وصلية نجاسة فيه، أو جاريا وظهر فيه أثرها، والأثر : طعم أو لون أو ريح، والخامس: ماء نجاسة فيكون نجساً أي طعم نجاسة أي لا في طهارته مشكوك في طهوريته، وهو ما شرب منه حمار أو بغل.
فصل في بيان أحكام السؤر ]
والماء القليل إذا شرب منه حيوان يكون على أربعة أقسام، ويسمى سؤرا: الأول: طاهر مطهر، وهو ما شرب منه آدمي أو فرس أو ما يؤكل لحمه، والثاني: نجس بالاتفاق لا يجوز استعماله، وهو ما شرب منه الكلب، أو الخنزير، أو شيء من سباع البهائم كالفهد والنمر والذئب. والثالث: مكروه استعماله مع وجود غيره، وهو سؤر الهرة، والدجاجة المخلاة، وسباع الطير كالصقر والشاهين والحدأة، وسواكن البُيُوتِ بتثليث الدال كالفأرة لا العقرب، والرابع مشكوك في طهوريته وهو سؤر البغل والحمار، فلا كراهة في سؤرها من أقسام الماء القليل فإن لم يجد غيره توضأ به ،وتيمم ثم صلى.
أطلقه آدمي وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يكن في فمه نجاسة، ولا فرق بين الكبير والصغير والمسلم والكافر، والحائض والجنب، وإذا تنجس فمه كأن شرب خمراً، أو أكل أو شرب نجساً، أو قاء ملء الفم، فشرب الماء من فوره تنجس، وإن كان بعد ما تردد البزاق في فمه مرات وألقاه أو ابتلعه قبل الشرب، فلا يكون سؤره نجساً عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف حمل، لكنه مكروه؛ لقول محمد سه بعدم طهارة النجاسة بالبزاق عنده. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٩] أو ما يؤكل إلخ ولا كراهة في سؤر ما يؤكل لحمه إن لم تكن جلالة - تأكل الجلة بالفتح، وهي في الأصل: البعرة، وقد يكنى بها عن العذرة - فإن كان جلالة فسؤرها من القسم الثالث مكروه. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٩] والثاني: من أقسام الماء القليل نجس في الكلام نوع إجمال، فاعلم أن سؤر الكلب والخنزير نجس نجاسة غليظة بالاتفاق، وأما سور غيرهما فنجاسة غليظة، وقيل: خفيفة. لا يجوز إلخ أي لا يصح التطهير به بحال، ولا يشربه إلا مضطر كالميتة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٩]
من سباع إلخ: احترز به عن سباع الطير والثالث من أقسام الماء القليل استعماله: أطلقه فشمل ما إذا استعمل في الطهارة، أو الشرب أو الطبخ مع وجود غيره احترز به عما إذا لم يجد الماء، فلا يجوز المصير إلى التيمم مع وجوده؛ لأنه طاهر. [ مراقي الفلاح: ٣٠]
الهرة أطلقها وهي مقيدة بالأهلية؛ لسقوط حكم النجاسة اتفاقا بعلة الطواف، وأما إذا كانت الهرة برية فسورها نجس لفقد علة الطواف فيها المخلاة التي تجول في القاذورات ولم يعلم طهارة منقارها من نجاسته، فكره سؤرها للشك، فإن لم يكن كذلك فلا كراهة فيه بأن حُبست فلا يصل منقارها لقذر. مراقي الفلاح: ۳۱] وسباع الطير : هي الطيور التي تصيد بمنقارها .
مشكلاً، وسواكن البيوت التي لا يوجد فيها دم سائل مشكوك قال ابن أمير :حاج هذه التسمية لم تُرو عن سلفنا أصلاً، وإنما وقعت لكثير مشكوكاً المتأخرين، فسماه بعضهم من وبعضهم و مرادهم بذلك: التوقف في كونه مزيل الحدث، فقالوا: يجب استعماله مع التيمم عند عدم الماء المطلق احتياطاً؛ ليخرج عن العهدة بيقين، وليس معناه الجهل بحكم الشرع، كما فهمه أبو طاهر الدباس فأنكر هذا التعبير ؛ لأن الحكم فيه معلوم، وهو ما ذكرنا، والقول بالتوقف في مثل هذا لتعارض الأدلة دليل العلم وغاية الورع [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٢] وتيمم [قال زفر ولا يجوز البداءة بالتيمم. (الزيلعي) عطف بالواو المفيدة لمطلق الاجتماع؛ ليفيد التخيير في التقديم، والأفضل تقديم الماء؛ ليخرج عن الخلاف والمراعاة وجود صورة الماء. الشلبي على تبيين الحقائق: ۱۱۳، حاشية الطحطاوي ثم إلخ أتى بـ "ثم" ليفيد أن الصلاة بعد فعلهما، وهو الأفضل، فلو صلى بعد كل طهارة الصلاة صح مع الكراهة ، ولا يلزم الكفر؛ لأنه لم يصل بغير طهارة من كل وجه، بل من وجه دون وجه حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٣]
The Book of Purification: Statement of the Rulings of Leftover Water. If it was stagnant and little - and little is what is less than ten by ten cubits - then it becomes impure even if its trace does not appear [؟] and a [؟] impurity in it, or flowing and its trace appears, and the trace is taste, color, or smell. Fifth: water [of] impurity becomes impure - meaning taste of impurity - meaning not in its purity, doubtful in its purifying quality, and it is water from which a donkey or mule drank. Section on the statement of rulings of leftover water. And little water, if an animal drinks from it, is of four types, called leftover water (su'r): First: pure and purifying, which is what a human or horse or animal whose meat is eaten drank from. Second: impure by consensus, it is not permissible to use it, and it is what a dog, pig, or any beast of prey like leopard, tiger, wolf drank from. Third: makruh to use when other water is available, which is leftover water of a cat, free-roaming hen, birds of prey like falcon, peregrine, kite, and house-dwelling animals (with three pronunciations) like mice but not scorpions. Fourth: doubtful in its purifying quality, which is leftover water of a mule and donkey; there is no dislike in their leftover water from the types of little water; if one finds no other water, he performs wudu with it and tayammum and then prays. He [the author] gave absolute [rule] for human, but it is conditioned by there being no impurity in his mouth; no distinction between adult and child, Muslim and disbeliever, menstruating and junub. If his mouth becomes impure, such as drinking wine, or eating or drinking impurity, or vomiting a mouthful, then drinking water immediately makes it impure. But if after saliva circulated in his mouth several times and he spat it out or swallowed it before drinking, then his leftover water is not impure according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf - [it is] makruh; due to Muhammad's statement that impurity is not removed by saliva according to him. [Maraqi al-Falah: 29] Or 'what is eaten' etc.: There is no dislike in leftover water of animals whose meat is eaten if it is not a jallalah - eating jallah (with fatha), which originally means dung, and may be euphemism for filth - if it is a jallalah, its leftover water is from the third category, makruh. [Maraqi al-Falah: 29] The second type of little water: impure. In the wording there is some conciseness. Know that the leftover water of dog and pig is severely impure by consensus, and as for leftover water of others, it is severely impure, and some say light. It is not permissible etc. i.e. purification with it is not valid at all, and it is not drunk except by necessity like carrion. [Maraqi al-Falah: 29] From 'beasts of prey' etc.: he excluded birds of prey. The third type of little water: its use [is makruh]. He gave absolute [rule], so it includes use for purification, or drinking, or cooking when other water is available; he excluded when one finds no water, for it is not permissible to resort to tayammum while it exists, because it is pure. [Maraqi al-Falah: 30] The cat - he gave absolute [rule] but it is restricted to domestic cats; because the ruling of impurity is dropped by consensus due to the reason of roaming around the house. As for wild cats, their leftover water is impure due to the absence of the reason of roaming. The free-roaming [hen] that goes about in filth and the purity of its beak is not known from impurity, so its leftover water is disliked due to doubt; if it is not so, i.e. it is confined such that its beak does not reach filth, then there is no dislike. [Maraqi al-Falah: 31] Birds of prey are those that hunt with their beaks. 'Doubtful', and house-dwelling animals that have no flowing blood - doubtful. Ibn Amir Haj said: This terminology is not reported from our earlier scholars at all, but only occurred to many later ones; some called it 'from' and some 'and' - what they mean by that is suspending judgement on whether it removes the state of impurity. So they said: It must be used along with tayammum when no absolute water is found, as a precaution, to ensure being free of responsibility with certainty. It does not mean ignorance of the legal ruling, as Abu Tahir al-Dabbas understood and thus objected to this expression, because the ruling is known - it is what we mentioned. The statement of suspending judgement in such a case due to conflicting evidences is a sign of knowledge and utmost piety. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 32] And tayammum [Zafar said: It is not permissible to begin with tayammum. (al-Zayla'i)] He conjoined with 'waw' which indicates absolute conjunction, to indicate choice in precedence; the better is to use water first, to avoid disagreement and to observe the existence of water in form. [Al-Shalabi on Tabyin al-Haqaiq: 113, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 33] Then he came with 'thumma' to indicate that prayer is after both actions, and that is the better; if one prays after each purification, the prayer is valid with dislike, and disbelief is not necessary, because he did not pray without any purification at all, but in some respect without purification. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 33]
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling statement from the matn of Nur al-Idah, with interlinear commentary from various sources. It defines the rulings of 'su'r' (leftover water) from animals. The author divides little water (less than 10x10 cubits and not flowing) into four categories based on what animal drinks from it. The first category is pure and purifying: water from humans (provided no impurity in mouth, regardless of age, religion, or state of purity), horses, and animals whose meat is eaten. The second is impure by consensus: from dogs, pigs, and beasts of prey (like leopards, tigers, wolves). The third is disliked (makruh tanzihan) when other water is available: from domestic cats, free-roaming hens, birds of prey (falcons, etc.), and house-dwelling animals like mice (but not scorpions). The fourth is doubtful in purifying quality: from mules and donkeys; if no other water is available, one must perform wudu with it and also do tayammum, then pray. The commentary clarifies nuances: for humans, if the mouth is impure (e.g., from wine, impurity, or vomit), drinking immediately makes the leftover water impure, but if saliva circulates and is spat or swallowed before drinking, then according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf the water is not impure but makruh; Muhammad considers it impure. For animals whose meat is eaten, if they are jallalah (feed on filth), their leftover water becomes disliked. For cats, only domestic cats have pure leftover water due to the reason of roaming; wild cats render it impure. For house-dwelling animals with no flowing blood (like mice), the water is doubtful: they require using it with tayammum as a precaution, not because the ruling is unknown but to ensure certainty of purification. The passage emphasizes that this classification is specific to little water.

Key Terms
السؤر (al-su'r): The leftover water in a vessel after an animal has drunk from it, specifically when the water is little (less than 10x10 cubits).
طاهر مطهر (tahir mutahhir): Pure in itself and purifying for others, i.e., can be used for wudu and ghusl without dislike.
مشكوك (mashkuk): Doubtful in its purifying quality; not that the ruling is unknown, but that one must exercise caution by using it and also performing tayammum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on leftover water from a domestic cat according to the Hanafi school?
A) Pure and purifying
B) Impure
C) Makruh tanzihan when other water is available
D) Doubtful

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of su'r is based on the animal's legal purity and the strength of evidence, leading to four distinct rulings: pure, impure, disliked, and doubtful.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
6 min
Rulings on Su'r of Cats, Birds, and Domestic Animals
Explanation of third and fourth su'r categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the su'r of cats, chickens, birds of prey, domestic animals, donkeys, and mules, and explain the precautionary wudu-and-tayammum requirement for mashkuk su'r.

Core Idea
Su'r of a domestic cat is makruh tanzihi; su'r of a donkey is mashkuk requiring wudu and tayammum.

This passage completes the Hanafi classification of su'r by explaining the third and fourth categories. The third includes animals whose su'r is disliked only when other water is available; the fourth involves water from donkeys and mules that requires a combination of wudu and tayammum due to doubt. Understanding these categories ensures correct purification when water is scarce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the third and fourth su'r categories
From the text, list which animals fall into each category: third includes cat, free-ranging chicken, birds of prey (falcon, kite, etc.), and domestic animals like mice; fourth includes donkey and mule.
Note that scorpions are excluded from the third category.
2
State the ruling for each category
Third category: makruh tanzihi when other water is available; otherwise pure. Fourth category: mashkuk (doubtful), requiring wudu then tayammum.
Mashkuk does not mean najis; it is a precaution due to conflicting evidence.
3
Explain conditions affecting the rulings
For cat su'r, the ruling depends on domestic vs. wild: domestic cats are exempted due to frequent roaming; wild cats' su'r is najis. For free-ranging chicken, the dislike is due to possible impurity on its beak.
If the chicken is confined and its beak doesn't reach filth, there is no karaha.
4
Describe the precautionary procedure for mashkuk su'r
If no other water is available, perform wudu with the su'r, then perform tayammum, then pray. The preferred order is to use water first, but both orders are valid.
The text uses 'waw' (and) to indicate conjunction, implying choice.
5
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Zufar holds that one should not begin with tayammum; the majority (Abu Hanifa and others) allow either order. The mufta bihi view is that both orders are valid, with water first being better.
This dispute does not affect the fundamental requirement to perform both acts.

Source Text

وهو ما شرب منه الكلب، أو الخنزير، أو شيء من سباع البهائم كالفهد كان أي حيوان النمر والذئب. والثالث: مكروه استعماله مع وجود غيره، وهو سؤر الهرة، كراهة تنزيهية مما لا كراهة فيه والدجاجة المخلاة، وسباع الطير كالصقر والشاهين والحدأة، وسواكن البُيُوتِ بتثليث الدال كالفأرة لا العقرب، والرابع مشكوك في طهوريته وهو سؤر البغل والحمار، فلا كراهة في سؤرها من أقسام الماء القليل فإن لم يجد غيره توضأ به ،وتيمم ثم صلى. المحدث أي الذي أمه أتان من سباع إلخ: احترز به عن سباع الطير والثالث من أقسام الماء القليل استعماله: أطلقه فشمل ما إذا استعمل في الطهارة، أو الشرب أو الطبخ مع وجود غيره احترز به عما إذا لم يجد الماء، فلا يجوز المصير إلى التيمم مع وجوده؛ لأنه طاهر. (الزيلعي) عطف بالواو المفيدة لمطلق الاجتماع؛ ليفيد التخيير في التقديم، والأفضل تقديم الماء؛ ليخرج عن الخلاف والمراعاة وجود صورة الماء. الشلبي على تبيين الحقائق: ۱۱۳، حاشية الطحطاوي ثم إلخ أتى بـ "ثم" ليفيد أن الصلاة بعد فعلهما، وهو الأفضل، فلو صلى بعد كل طهارة الصلاة صح مع الكراهة ، ولا يلزم الكفر؛ لأنه لم يصل بغير طهارة من كل وجه، بل من وجه دون وجه حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٣]
It is what a dog, or pig, or any beast of prey like leopard (any animal, tiger, wolf) drinks from. And the third: its use is makruh in the presence of other [water], and it is the su'r of a cat, a karaha tanzihiyya, and of the free-ranging chicken, and birds of prey like falcon, peregrine, kite, and domestic animals (with three pronunciations of the dal) like the mouse, not the scorpion. And the fourth: it is mashkuk in its tahuriyya, and it is the su'r of a mule and donkey, so there is no karaha in their su'r. It is from the categories of qalil water, and if he does not find other water, he performs wudu with it, and then performs tayammum, then prays. The water-waster: i.e. whose mother is a donkey. From beasts etc.: he excluded birds of prey. And the third of the categories of qalil water: he used it absolutely, so it includes if used for purification, or drinking or cooking in the presence of other [water]. He excluded the case when he does not find water, so it is not permissible to resort to tayammum while it exists, because it is pure. [Maraqi al-Falah: 30] He mentioned the cat absolutely and it is restricted to domestic, because the ruling of impurity falls by consensus due to the cause of [the cat] roaming around. And if the cat is wild, its su'r is najis due to the lack of the cause of roaming. The free-ranging [chicken] that roams in filth and whose beak's purity from impurity is not known, so its su'r is disliked due to doubt. If it is not so, then there is no karaha, such as if it is confined and its beak does not reach filth. [Maraqi al-Falah: 31] And birds of prey: they are the birds that hunt with their beaks. Problematic. And domestic animals that have no flowing blood are problematic. Ibn Amir said: This terminology is not narrated from our predecessors at all, and it occurred to many later scholars. Some called it min and some called it... and their meaning by that is hesitation in its being a remover of hadath, so they said: it must be used with tayammum when there is no absolute water, as a precaution, to fulfill the obligation with certainty. And it does not mean ignorance of the legal ruling, as Abu Tahir al-Dabbas understood, so he rejected this expression, because the ruling concerning it is known, and it is what we mentioned. And the statement of hesitation in such a matter due to conflicting evidences is a sign of knowledge and utmost piety. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 32] And tayammum: Zufar said: it is not permissible to begin with tayammum. (al-Zayla'i) He connected with waw which indicates absolute conjunction, to indicate the choice of precedence, and the best is to give precedence to water, to exit the disagreement and to observe the existence of the form of water. [al-Shilbi on Tabayin al-Haqa'iq: 113, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi] Then he came with 'thumma' to indicate that prayer is after both acts, and it is best. If he prays after each purification, the prayer is valid with karaha, and disbelief is not necessary, because he did not pray without purification from every aspect, but from one aspect without another. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 33]
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage discusses the third and fourth categories of su'r (leftover water) according to the Hanafi school. The third category is water drunk by cats, free-ranging chickens, birds of prey (like falcon, kite, etc.), and domestic animals like mice (but not scorpions). The ruling for this category is that it is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not sinful) to use when other water is available; if no other water exists, using it is allowed and it is considered pure. The reason for the cat is that domestic cats are exempted from impurity because they frequently roam around houses (by consensus), but wild cats' su'r is najis. For the free-ranging chicken, the dislike is due to doubt about its beak's purity. The fourth category is water drunk by donkeys and mules, which is considered mashkuk (doubtful) in its purifying ability. It is not disliked but requires combining with tayammum when no other water is available: one performs wudu with it, then tayammum, then prays. The commentary clarifies that the hesitation in this ruling is not ignorance but a precaution due to conflicting evidences. It also addresses a difference: Imam Zufar holds that one should not begin with tayammum, but the relied-upon view allows both orders, with preference for water first to avoid disagreement.

Key Terms
السؤر (al-su'r): Leftover water after an animal has drunk from it.
مشكوك (mashkuk): Doubtful: water whose purifying ability is uncertain due to conflicting evidence.
كراهة تنزيهية (karaha tanzihiyya): A disliked but not forbidden action; its omission is better but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for the su'r of a domestic cat when other water is available?
A) It is najis and cannot be used.
B) It is makruh tanzihi to use it.
C) It is pure and preferred.
D) It requires wudu and tayammum.

Key Takeaway
Su'r of domestic cats is makruh tanzihi; su'r of donkeys and mules is mashkuk requiring wudu and tayammum.

Taharri for Mixed Vessels and Clothes
Ruling on taharri for mixed vessels and clothes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on taharri (exerting effort) when pure and impure vessels or clothes are mixed, distinguish the criteria for vessels vs. clothes, and apply the rulings to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Taharri for vessels depends on majority; for clothes it always applies because there's no substitute.

Imagine you have several water containers, some pure and some impure, but you cannot tell which is which. How do you proceed? In this lesson, we learn the Hanafi ruling for such cases. The key insight is whether a substitute exists: for water, tayammum serves as a backup, but for clothes, there is no alternative, so investigation is always required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario: mixed vessels or clothes?
First determine if the mixed items are vessels (for water) or clothes. The rules differ.
Vessels include containers for water, drinks, etc.
2
For vessels, check the majority
If more than half are likely pure, you must perform taharri for wudu and drinking. If more than half are impure, you do not perform taharri for wudu (instead do tayammum), but you still do taharri for drinking (no substitute for water).
3
For clothes, always perform taharri
Regardless of the majority being pure or impure, you must perform taharri to find a pure garment. There is no substitute for clothing to cover the 'awra.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The rule is based on whether a valid substitute exists for the act (wudu/ghusl vs. covering).
Tayammum substitutes for wudu/ghusl, but nothing substitutes for clothing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في التحري في الأواني والثياب] لو اختلط أوانٍ أكثرها طاهر تحرى للتوضؤ ،والشرب، وإن كان أكثرها نجسا لا يتحرى الجملة نعت لـ"أوان" جواب لو والاغتسال إلا للشرب، وفي الثياب المختلطة يتحرى، سواء كان أكثرها طاهرا أو نجسا. أوان: مرفوع بالفاعلية، وعلامة رفعه ضمة مقدرة على الياء المحذوفة؛ لالتقاء الساكنين، وأصله "أواني" يفعل به كـ"جوار". [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٤ تحرى إلخ ماض من التحرّي، وهو تفريغ الوسع والجهد لتمييز الطاهر عن غيره. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۳۳] لا يتحرى بل يتيمم كمن عدم ا الماء. وفي الثياب إلخ أي إذا اختلطت الثياب، بعضها نجس وبعضها طاهر و لم تتميز فحكمه التحري، سواء كان أكثر منها نجساً أو طاهراً. يتحرى إلخ لأنه لا خلف للثوب في ستر العورة، والماء يخلفه التراب. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٤]
Chapter on investigation (taharri) regarding vessels and clothes: If vessels are mixed, the majority of which are pure, then he performs taharri for wudu and drinking. But if the majority are impure, he does not perform taharri (and instead does tayammum) except for drinking. And regarding mixed clothes, he performs taharri, whether the majority are pure or impure. 'Awan': in the nominative as subject, its nominative sign is a implied dhamma on the omitted ya due to two silent letters meeting; its origin is 'awani', patterned like 'jawari'. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 34] 'Tahara' etc. is past tense of 'taharri', which is expending effort and exertion to distinguish the pure from others. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 33] He does not perform taharri but does tayammum like one who has no water. 'And in clothes' etc.: i.e., if clothes are mixed, some impure and some pure, and they are not distinguishable, then its ruling is taharri, whether the majority are impure or pure. He performs taharri because there is no substitute for clothing in covering the 'awra, while water has earth as a substitute. [Maraqi al-Falah: 34]
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah deals with the ruling of taharri (seeking the best opinion) when pure and impure vessels or clothes are mixed together and cannot be distinguished. For vessels: if the majority of the vessels are pure, one must perform taharri to identify a pure vessel for wudu and drinking. If the majority are impure, then one does not perform taharri for wudu and ghusl; instead, he must resort to tayammum as if he had no water, because using a likely impure vessel would be risky. However, for drinking, he may still perform taharri even if the majority are impure, because there is no substitute for water for drinking. For clothes: the ruling is different. One always performs taharri, regardless of whether the majority are pure or impure. The reason given in the commentary is that unlike water, which has tayammum as a substitute, there is no substitute for clothing to cover the 'awra. Therefore, one must make an effort to identify a pure garment.

Key Terms
التحري (al-taharri): Exerting effort to distinguish the pure from the impure when faced with mixed items of unknown purity.
أوانٍ (awānin): Plural of inā' (vessel), referring to containers used for water or other liquids.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person has ten vessels for water; seven are likely impure and three are pure. For which act does the Hanafi school still require taharri?
A) Wudu
B) Ghusl
C) Drinking
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The obligation of taharri depends on the availability of a substitute: for water, tayammum can replace wudu/ghusl, so taharri is not required when risk is high; for clothes, no substitute exists, so taharri is always required.

Purification of Wells from Najasah
Ruling on causes of well impurity and required purification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the causes that make a small well impure, identify the exceptions (including the dog ruling), and explain the 200-bucket rule when full emptying is impossible.

Core Idea
A small well is impurified by liquid najasah, pig, or death of dog/sheep/human; solid droppings and a live dog that exits without mouth contact do not cause impurity.

This lesson covers the Hanafi rules on when a well becomes impure and how to purify it. It distinguishes between different types of impurities and animals, providing clear guidelines for a common scenario in daily life. The text includes both the core ruling and commentary that clarifies key distinctions between the dog and pig.

Guided Path
1
Identify the well type
Determine if the well is 'small' (less than 10x10 cubits) based on the commentary. This is a condition for the ruling.
Large wells have different rules not covered here.
2
List the impurities that cause impurity
Read the text: any liquid impurity (even a drop), a pig (even if alive), death of a dog/sheep/human inside, or swelling of an animal make the well impure.
Solid droppings (arwath) are an exception.
3
Note exceptions and special cases
Solid droppings do not cause impurity. A dog only causes impurity if it dies in the well, not if it falls in and exits alive. A very small lamb is treated like a cat.
Contrast with pig which is najis al-ayn.
4
Interpret the purification method
If full emptying is impossible (e.g., spring-fed well), remove 200 medium-sized buckets as a substitute.
This ruling from Imam Muhammad is based on Baghdad wells.
5
Understand the rationale
The dog is distinguished from the pig because the dog is not najis al-ayn (inherently impure) in the Hanafi school.
Shafi'i school differs on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل [ في أحكام الآبار وتطهيرها ] تنزح البئر الصغيرة بوقوع نجاسة وإن قلت من غير الأرواث كقطرة دم أو خمر، وصلية لنجاسة عينه وصلية بيان النجاسة مثال القلة و بوقوع خنزير ولو خرج حيا ولم يصب فمه الماء، وبموت كلب أو شاة أو آدمي فيها، وبانتفاخ حيوان ولو صغيرا، ومائتا دلو لو لم يمكن نزحها، دموي غير مائي وصلية أوان: مرفوع بالفاعلية، وعلامة رفعه ضمة مقدرة على الياء المحذوفة؛ لالتقاء الساكنين، وأصله "أواني" يفعل به كـ"جوار". [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٤ تحرى إلخ ماض من التحرّي، وهو تفريغ الوسع والجهد لتمييز الطاهر عن غيره. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۳۳] لا يتحرى بل يتيمم كمن عدم ا الماء. وفي الثياب إلخ أي إذا اختلطت الثياب، بعضها نجس وبعضها طاهر و لم تتميز فحكمه التحري، سواء كان أكثر منها نجساً أو طاهراً. يتحرى إلخ لأنه لا خلف للثوب في ستر العورة، والماء يخلفه التراب. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٤] تنزح البئر : أي ينزح ماؤها؛ لأنه من إسناد الفعل إلى البئر وإرادة الماء الحال بالبئر؛ قصداً للمبالغة في إخراج جميع الماء، فهو من إطلاق اسم المحل وإرادة الحال فيه مراقي الفلاح: ٣٦ وحاشية الطحطاوي] الصغيرة: وهي ما دون عشر في عشر مراقي الفلاح: ٣٦] وإن قلت إلخ لأن قليل النجاسة ينجس قليل الماء، وإن لم يظهر أثره فيه. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٦] بموت إلخ : قيد بموت الكلب في البئر ولم يقل: بوقوع الكلب، كما قال في الخنزير؛ لأن الكلب غير نجس العين على الصحيح، فإذا لم يمت وخرج حيًّا ولم يصل فمه الماء لا ينجس. [ مراقي الفلاح: ٣٦] بخلاف الخنزير ؛ لأنه نجس العين شاة أطلقها وهي مقيدة بما إذا كانت كبيرة في الجملة، أما إذا كان ولد الشاة صغيراً جداً كان حكمه حكم الهرة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٦] ومائتا دلو إلخ [أي الدلو المتوسط الذي يستعمل في البئر أكثر الأحيان أي إذا وجب نزح الجميع ولم يمكن فراغها؛ لكونها معيناً نزح مائنا دلو، وهو مروي عن محمد، أفتى بما شاهد في بغداد؛ لأن آبارها كثيرة الماء؛ لمجاورة دجلة تبيين الحقائق: ۱۰۱/۱]
Chapter [On rulings of wells and their purification]: The small well is emptied by the falling of an impurity even if little, except for droppings, like a drop of blood or wine, and something that is impure by its essence, and by the falling of a pig even if it exits alive and its mouth does not hit the water, and by the death of a dog or a sheep or a human in it, and by the swelling of an animal even if small, and two hundred buckets if it is not possible to empty it completely. 'Awan': ... [commentary] ... 'The well is emptied' means its water is emptied, because it is assigning the action to the well intending the water present in the well, for exaggeration in removing all water; it is from using the name of the place and intending what is in it. [Maraqi al-Falah: 36 and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi] 'The small well' is that which is less than ten by ten. [Maraqi al-Falah: 36] 'Even if little' because a small amount of impurity makes a small amount of water impure, even if its trace does not appear. [Maraqi al-Falah: 36] 'By the death etc.' He restricted to the death of the dog in the well and did not say 'by the falling of the dog' as he said for the pig, because the dog is not impure by its essence according to the correct view. So if it does not die and exits alive and its mouth does not reach the water, it does not become impure. [Maraqi al-Falah: 36] Contrary to the pig, because it is impure by its essence. 'Sheep' he mentioned absolutely, but it is restricted to a large sheep generally; as for a very small lamb, its ruling is like that of a cat. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 36] 'And two hundred buckets etc.' i.e., the medium-sized bucket that is used in the well most of the time; i.e., if emptying all is obligatory and it is not possible to empty it fully because it is a flowing well, then two hundred buckets are emptied. This is narrated from Muhammad, who gave a fatwa based on what he saw in Baghdad because its wells have abundant water due to proximity to the Tigris. [Tabayin al-Haqa'iq: 101/1]
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage outlines the causes that make a well impure and the required purification method. A small well (less than 10 cubits in circumference) becomes impure by the fall of any liquid impurity (like blood or wine), a pig (even if it exits alive), or the death of a dog, sheep, or human inside, or if an animal swells in it. Exceptions: solid animal droppings (arwath) do not make the well impure; a dog does not make it impure by merely falling in if it exits alive without its mouth touching water (since the dog is not najis al-ayn). If the well must be emptied but cannot be fully drained (due to being a spring), one must remove 200 medium-sized buckets. This ruling is attributed to Imam Muhammad based on his observation of wells in Baghdad near the Tigris. The commentary also explains the grammatical point that 'emptying the well' means removing its water, and that a very young lamb is treated like a cat (i.e., its death does not make the well impure because its blood is not flowing).

Key Terms
تنزح (tunzahu): The well is emptied of its water (by removing water).
الأرواث (al-arwāth): Solid droppings of animals; they do not make the well impure when they fall.
نجس العين (najis al-ʿayn): An object that is intrinsically impure, like a pig, regardless of contact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always, regardless of circumstances.
B) Only if the dog's mouth touches the water.
C) Only if the dog dies inside the well.
D) It never makes the well impure.

Key Takeaway
A small well becomes impure by liquid najasah, pig, or death of certain animals; solid droppings and a live dog that exits without wetting its mouth do not cause impurity; if full emptying is impossible, remove 200 buckets.

Well Purification: Bucket Counts and Exceptions
Continuation of well rulings with specific numbers and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required number of buckets for each animal and identify which objects do not pollute a well.

Core Idea
Not every dead animal pollutes a well; the ruling depends on blood flow, swelling, and type.

This lesson covers the specific rulings for purifying a well when various objects fall into it. You will learn the exact number of buckets required for small animals like chickens and mice, as well as important exceptions: dung, animals without flowing blood, and humans or edible animals that exit alive. These rules balance purification with practicality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is purifying a well (nazh) after an impurity falls into it. The ruling is wajib for the specified amounts.
2
List the mandatory bucket counts
For a chicken or cat: 40 buckets. For a mouse that is not swollen: 20 buckets. If the mouse is swollen, a different ruling applies (not covered here).
The purification also applies to the bucket, rope, and hand.
3
Recognize what does NOT pollute
Dung (camel, sheep, cow) does not pollute unless abundant. Bird droppings (pigeon, sparrow) do not spoil water. Animals without flowing blood (fish, frog, insects) do not pollute even if they die in the water.
Abundance is judged by the observer (relied-upon view).
4
Identify the condition for human/edible animal
If a human or an animal whose meat is eaten falls in and exits alive, the well is not polluted provided there is no impurity (e.g., najasah) on its body.
Impurity here means actual najasah, not mere possibility.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(مراقي الفلاح) والدلو: أناء يستقى به من البير. البئر ولا فرق بين آبار الأمصار والفلوات في الصحيح، ولا فرق بين الرطب واليابس، والصحيح والمنكسر في ظاهر الرواية. (مراقي الفلاح إلا إلخ : اعلم أن الأصل أن البئر لا تنجس بوقوع البعر وغيره إلا أن يكون الواقع كثيراً، واختلفوا في الفاصل بين القليل والكثير، فقيل: الثلاث كثير، وروي عن أبي حنيفة: أن الكثير ما يستكثره الناظر والقليل ما يستقله وعليه الاعتماد وقيل الكثير ما يغطي وجه الماء كله، وقيل: ما لا يخلو فيه كل دلو عن بعرة. (الزيلعي بحذف وزيادة بخرء حمام الحرء بالفتح واحد الخرء بالضم. ولا بموت أي ولا ينجس الماء ولا المائعات فيه أي في الماء أو المائع، وهو قيد اتفاقي، حتى لو مات خارجه وألقي فيه يكون الحكم كذلك مراقي الفلاح: ٤٠ ، حاشية الطحطاوي وضفدع [بالكسر ودال مهملة مكسورة] أطلقه وهو مقيد بالبحري، فإن كان الضفدع يفسد الماء إذا كان له دم سائل، وهو ما لا سترة له ، أصابعه وحيوان الماء الحد الفاصل بين المائي والبري أن المائي ما لا يعيش في غير الماء، والبري ما لا يعيش في غير البرّ، واختلف فيما يعيش فيهما، فقال قاضي خان في شرح الجامع الصغير: إنه يفسد. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٠] آدمي ولو جنباً، أو حائضاً، أو نفساء انقطع دمها، أو كافراً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤١] نجاسة: أراد بها نجاسة متيقنة، فلا ينظر إلى ظاهر اشتمال أبوالها على أفخاذها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١]
And if a chicken or cat or similar dies in it, it is necessary to draw forty buckets; and if a mouse dies in it and its corpse does not swell, it is necessary to draw twenty buckets; and that is purification for the well, the bucket, the rope, and the hand of the drawer, after removing what fell into it. Al-nazh (drawing) is considered only after removing the impurity that fell; drawing before that is of no benefit. The well is not polluted by camel dung, sheep/goat droppings, or cow dung, unless the onlooker considers it abundant, or that every bucket for horse, mule, and donkey is not free from a dung pellet. Water is not spoiled by the droppings of a pigeon or sparrow, nor by the death of an animal that has no flowing blood in it, such as fish (whether land or sea), frog, aquatic animal, bedbug, fly, wasp, or scorpion; nor by the falling of a human or an animal whose flesh is eaten if it comes out alive and there is no impurity on its body.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage continues the well rulings with specific quantities for smaller animals: a chicken or cat requires 40 buckets; a mouse requires 20 buckets if not swollen. The purification extends to the bucket, rope, and drawer's hand because their impurity was due to the water. The commentary emphasizes that the object must be removed first; drawing water before removal does not purify. The text then lists exceptions: animal droppings (bahr, rawth, khuthi) do not pollute unless abundant; the measure of abundance is what the observer deems much (relied-upon view from Abu Hanifa). Bird droppings (pigeon, sparrow) do not spoil water. Animals without flowing blood (fish, frog, insects) do not pollute even if they die in the water. A human or edible animal (e.g., sheep) that falls in and exits alive does not pollute provided no impurity on its body. The commentary clarifies that the distinction between aquatic and terrestrial animals is based on whether they live exclusively in one habitat; ambiguous cases may cause pollution per Qadikhan.

Key Terms
الرشاء (al-rishā'): The rope used to draw water from a well.
بَعْر (ba'r): Dung pellets of camels, sheep, and goats.
مَا لا دَمَ لَهُ (mā lā dama lahu): Animals without flowing blood, such as insects and fish; they do not cause impurity when they die in water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The well is polluted; 40 buckets must be drawn.
D) The well is polluted; all water must be drawn.

Key Takeaway
The well is not automatically polluted by every object; specific bucket counts apply for animals with blood, while dung, non-blood creatures, and live exits are exceptions.

Required Amounts of Nazh for Different Animals
States specific amounts for nazh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required number of buckets (nazh) for purifying a well when a chicken, cat, or mouse dies in it, and explain why the amounts differ.

Core Idea
Forty buckets for a chicken or cat; twenty for a mouse—each impurity has a prescribed remedy.

When an animal dies in a well, the water becomes impure and must be purified by drawing a specific number of buckets. This lesson focuses on the exact amounts required for common household animals as stated in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animals mentioned
Find the animals explicitly listed in the text: chicken (دجاجة), cat (هرة), mouse (فأرة), and the phrase 'or similar' (أو نحوهما).
2
Extract the required number of buckets
The text states 40 buckets for chicken/cat, 20 buckets for a mouse that is not bloated. Note the condition of bloating for the mouse.
The text does not specify the amount if the mouse is bloated; that is treated separately under the duration of impurity.
3
Understand the scope of purification
The purification covers not only the well but also the bucket, rope, and the hand of the drawer. This is because these items become impure by contact with the water.
4
Note the reason for the amounts
The amounts are based on transmitted rulings (zahir al-riwayah). The Hanafi school considers them wajib, not merely recommended.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام الآبار وتطهيرها
وإن مات فيها دجاجة أو هرة أو نحوهما الزم نزح أربعين دلوا، وإن مات فيها فأرة و لم تنتفخ الجثة بالهمز أو نحوها لزم نزح عشرين دلوا، وكان ذلك طهارة للبئر والدلو والرشاء ويد المستقي، كعصفور بعد إخراج ما وقع فيها النزوح بكسر الراء حبل الدلو من الاستقاء ولا تنجس البئر بالبعر والروث والخثي، إلا أن يستكثره الناظر، أو أن لا يخلو دلو للفرس والبغل والحمار وعليه الاعتماد صححه في المبسوط عن بعرة، ولا يفسد الماء بخرء حمام وعصفور، ولا بموت ما لا دم له فيه كسمك أي لا ينجس بريا كان أو بحرياً وضفدع وحيوان الماء وبق وذباب وزنبور وعقرب ولا بوقوع آدمي وما يؤكل أي مائي المولد الا الله لحمه إذا خرج حيا و لم يكن على بدنه نجاسة. أي ولا ينجس نزح إلخ والنزح إنما يعتبر بعد إخراج ما وقع فيها من النجاسة؛ فإن النزح قبله لا يفيد؛ لأنه سبب النجاسة، إلا إذا تعذر إخراجه كخشبة أو خرقة نجسة تعذر إخراجها أو تغيبت فينزح القدر الواجب، وتطهر الخشبة والخرقة تبعاً لطهارة البئر. [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ۳۸ مع تصرف أربعين وتستحب الزيادة إلى خمسين أوستين. (مراقي الفلاح) وكان ذلك إلخ لأن نجاسة هذه الأشياء كانت بنجاسة الماء، فتكون طهارتها بطهارته نفياً للحرج كطهارة دنّ الخمر بتخللها. (مراقي الفلاح) والدلو: أناء يستقى به من البير. البئر ولا فرق بين آبار الأمصار والفلوات في الصحيح، ولا فرق بين الرطب واليابس، والصحيح والمنكسر في ظاهر الرواية. [مراقي الفلاح: ۳۸] بالبعر : رجيع الإبل والغنم والغزال. والخثي: بكسر الخاء، واحد الأخثاء للبقر. (مراقي الفلاح إلا إلخ : اعلم أن الأصل أن البئر لا تنجس بوقوع البعر وغيره إلا أن يكون الواقع كثيراً، واختلفوا في الفاصل بين القليل والكثير، فقيل: الثلاث كثير، وروي عن أبي حنيفة: أن الكثير ما يستكثره الناظر والقليل ما يستقله وعليه الاعتماد وقيل الكثير ما يغطي وجه الماء كله، وقيل: ما لا يخلو فيه كل دلو عن بعرة. (الزيلعي بحذف وزيادة بخرء حمام الحرء بالفتح واحد الخرء بالضم. ولا بموت أي ولا ينجس الماء ولا المائعات فيه أي في الماء أو المائع، وهو قيد اتفاقي، حتى لو مات خارجه وألقي فيه يكون الحكم كذلك مراقي الفلاح: ٤٠ ، حاشية الطحطاوي وضفدع [بالكسر ودال مهملة مكسورة] أطلقه وهو مقيد بالبحري، فإن كان الضفدع يفسد الماء إذا كان له دم سائل، وهو ما لا سترة له ، أصابعه وحيوان الماء الحد الفاصل بين المائي والبري أن المائي ما لا يعيش في غير الماء، والبري ما لا يعيش في غير البرّ، واختلف فيما يعيش فيهما، فقال قاضي خان في شرح الجامع الصغير: إنه يفسد. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٠] آدمي ولو جنباً، أو حائضاً، أو نفساء انقطع دمها، أو كافراً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤١] نجاسة: أراد بها نجاسة متيقنة، فلا ينظر إلى ظاهر اشتمال أبوالها على أفخاذها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١]
ولا بوقوع بغل وحمار وسباع طير ووحش في الصحيح، وإن وصل لعاب الواقع إلى كسبع و قرد الماء أخذ حكمه ووجود حيوان ميت فيها ينجسها من يوم وليلة، ومنتفخ من ثلاثة مبتدأ دموي غير مائي أيام ولياليها إن لم يعلم وقت وقوعه.
Rulings on wells and their purification: If a chicken or cat or similar dies in it, the nuzh (removal) of forty buckets is required. If a mouse dies in it and its body is not bloated, the nuzh of twenty buckets is required. That is purification for the well, the bucket, the rope, and the hand of the drawer, like a sparrow after removing what fell into it. The well does not become impure by ba'r (camel dung), rawth (horse dung), or khuthy (cow dung), unless the observer considers it abundant, or every bucket does not come out free of a dung ball. Reliance is upon this, as confirmed in al-Mabsut. Water is not spoiled by the droppings of a pigeon or sparrow, nor by the death of something without flowing blood in it, such as fish, whether land or sea, frog, aquatic animals, bugs, flies, wasps, scorpions, nor by the falling of a human or what is permissible to eat that came out alive and had no impurity on its body. Nuzh is only considered after removing the impurity that fell into it; before removal it is of no benefit, because removal is the cause of purification, unless removal is not possible, like a piece of wood or a cloth that cannot be removed or is hidden, then the required amount is drawn, and the wood and cloth become pure due to the purity of the well. Forty is recommended to be increased to fifty or sixty. That is because the impurity of these things was due to the impurity of the water, so their purification is through its purification, to avoid hardship, like the purification of a wine jug by its fermentation. The bucket is the vessel used for drawing from the well. There is no difference between wells in cities and deserts in the correct view, nor between wet and dry, nor between sound and broken in the apparent narration. Ba'r is the dung of camels, sheep, and gazelles. Khuthy is the plural of khuthya for cows. Know that the original principle is that the well does not become impure by the falling of dung and such unless it is much. They differed on the line between little and much: some said three is much; it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that much is what the viewer considers abundant, and little is what he considers little, and reliance is upon this. Others said much is what covers the entire surface of the water, or what every bucket does not come out free of a dung ball. With the dropping of a pigeon, and death: water and other liquids are not impure when something without flowing blood dies in them or outside and is thrown in, according to the agreed restriction. Frog: it is restricted to sea frogs; a land frog spoils water if it has flowing blood, i.e., without webbed fingers. The dividing line between aquatic and land animals: aquatic animals cannot live out of water, land animals cannot live in water. There is disagreement on those that live in both: Qadi Khan in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir said they spoil the water. A human, even if junub, menstruating, or postpartum bleeding has stopped, or a disbeliever, is allowed. Impurity refers to confirmed impurity, not the apparent inclusion of urine on their thighs. The falling of a mule, donkey, predatory birds, and wild animals does not spoil the water in the correct view. If the saliva of the fallen animal reaches the water, its ruling applies. The presence of a dead animal in it makes the water impure from the day and night if not bloated, and from three days and nights if bloated, when the time of falling is unknown.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings (ahkam) on the purification of wells when impurities fall into them. The text begins by stating the required amount of water to be drawn (nazh) for different animals: forty buckets for a chicken or cat, twenty buckets for a mouse that is not bloated. The purification covers the well, bucket, rope, and the hand of the drawer. After removing the impurity, the actual nazh is performed. If the impurity cannot be removed (e.g., a submerged piece of wood), the required amount is drawn, and the item becomes pure along with the well. The text then discusses that the well does not become impure by animal droppings unless they are abundant, with the authoritative opinion being that abundance is judged by the observer's perception. Next, it states that water is not spoiled by the dropping of birds or by the death of animals without flowing blood (e.g., fish, frogs, insects). A human or a permissible-to-eat animal falling in does not spoil the water if it came out alive and was not carrying impurity. The text also clarifies the definition of aquatic vs. land animals and that a frog with flowing blood spoils the water. Finally, it rules that the falling of mules, donkeys, predatory birds, and wild animals does not spoil the water, but the presence of a dead animal does spoil it, with the duration of impurity calculated from the last day if unknown, and from three days if bloated. The commentary by Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi provides additional details and clarifications.

Key Terms
نزح (nazh): Removal of water from a well, usually by drawing buckets, to purify it.
دجاجة (dajajah): Chicken (hen).
فأرة (fa'rah): Mouse or rat.
دلو (dalw): Bucket used for drawing water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, how many buckets must be drawn if a mouse dies in a well and its body is not bloated?
A) 10 buckets
B) 20 buckets
C) 40 buckets
D) 50 buckets

Key Takeaway
The required nazh for a chicken or cat is 40 buckets; for a mouse (non-bloated) it is 20 buckets.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
4 min
The Process of Purification: Nazh Before and After Removal
Clarifies the correct sequence of purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the correct order of purification for a well (removal of impurity first, then nazh) and identify the exception when removal is impossible.

Core Idea
Nazh only purifies if the impurity is first removed; otherwise it is pointless.

Simply drawing water from a well does not purify it if the source of impurity remains. The text explicitly states that nazh is only effective after removing the fallen animal or object, with an exception for items that cannot be removed.

Guided Path
1
Locate the ruling on the order
Find the sentence: 'والنزح إنما يعتبر بعد إخراج ما وقع فيها من النجاسة' (Nazh is only considered after removing the impurity that fell into it).
2
Understand the reason
The text says 'لأن النزح قبله لا يفيد؛ لأنه سبب النجاسة' because before removal, the impurity remains and re-impurifies the water.
3
Identify the exception
When removal is impossible (e.g., a piece of wood or cloth hidden in the well), nazh the required amount suffices, and the hidden item becomes pure along with the water.
4
Apply the rule
In practice, always remove the dead animal or impurity first, then draw the required number of buckets.

إخراج (ikhraj): Removal of the impurity from the well.

What must be done before drawing the required buckets of water to purify a well after a dead animal falls in?

Impurity from Dung: The Rule of Abundance
Explains the impurity rules for animal dung

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a well does not become impure by animal dung unless it is abundant, and define what constitutes abundance according to the relied-upon opinion.

Core Idea
A well is not impure by dung unless the observer deems it abundant.

The text addresses a common scenario: animal droppings falling into a well. The Hanafi school takes a lenient view, stating that the well does not become impure unless the dung is abundant. This lesson unpacks the definition of abundance and the different opinions within the school.

Guided Path
1
Find the ruling on dung
The text says: 'ولا تنجس البئر بالبعر والروث والخثي' (The well does not become impure by camel dung, horse dung, or cow dung) except if abundant.
2
Identify the condition
The exception is 'إلا أن يستكثره الناظر' (unless the observer considers it abundant) or 'أو أن لا يخلو دلو عن بعرة' (or every bucket does not come out free of a dung ball). The relied-upon opinion is the observer's perception.
3
Understand the different definitions of abundance
The text mentions variant opinions: some said three dung pellets is abundant; others said covering the water surface; others said every bucket contains some. The chosen view is the observer's judgment.
4
Apply the rule
In practice, if a few dung pellets fall in, the water remains pure. Only when the amount appears significant to a reasonable observer does it become impure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام الآبار وتطهيرها
وإن مات فيها دجاجة أو هرة أو نحوهما الزم نزح أربعين دلوا، وإن مات فيها فأرة و لم تنتفخ الجثة بالهمز أو نحوها لزم نزح عشرين دلوا، وكان ذلك طهارة للبئر والدلو والرشاء ويد المستقي، كعصفور بعد إخراج ما وقع فيها النزوح بكسر الراء حبل الدلو من الاستقاء ولا تنجس البئر بالبعر والروث والخثي، إلا أن يستكثره الناظر، أو أن لا يخلو دلو للفرس والبغل والحمار وعليه الاعتماد صححه في المبسوط عن بعرة، ولا يفسد الماء بخرء حمام وعصفور، ولا بموت ما لا دم له فيه كسمك أي لا ينجس بريا كان أو بحرياً وضفدع وحيوان الماء وبق وذباب وزنبور وعقرب ولا بوقوع آدمي وما يؤكل أي مائي المولد الا الله لحمه إذا خرج حيا و لم يكن على بدنه نجاسة. أي ولا ينجس نزح إلخ والنزح إنما يعتبر بعد إخراج ما وقع فيها من النجاسة؛ فإن النزح قبله لا يفيد؛ لأنه سبب النجاسة، إلا إذا تعذر إخراجه كخشبة أو خرقة نجسة تعذر إخراجها أو تغيبت فينزح القدر الواجب، وتطهر الخشبة والخرقة تبعاً لطهارة البئر. [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ۳۸ مع تصرف أربعين وتستحب الزيادة إلى خمسين أوستين. (مراقي الفلاح) وكان ذلك إلخ لأن نجاسة هذه الأشياء كانت بنجاسة الماء، فتكون طهارتها بطهارته نفياً للحرج كطهارة دنّ الخمر بتخللها. (مراقي الفلاح) والدلو: أناء يستقى به من البير. البئر ولا فرق بين آبار الأمصار والفلوات في الصحيح، ولا فرق بين الرطب واليابس، والصحيح والمنكسر في ظاهر الرواية. [مراقي الفلاح: ۳۸] بالبعر : رجيع الإبل والغنم والغزال. والخثي: بكسر الخاء، واحد الأخثاء للبقر. (مراقي الفلاح إلا إلخ : اعلم أن الأصل أن البئر لا تنجس بوقوع البعر وغيره إلا أن يكون الواقع كثيراً، واختلفوا في الفاصل بين القليل والكثير، فقيل: الثلاث كثير، وروي عن أبي حنيفة: أن الكثير ما يستكثره الناظر والقليل ما يستقله وعليه الاعتماد وقيل الكثير ما يغطي وجه الماء كله، وقيل: ما لا يخلو فيه كل دلو عن بعرة. (الزيلعي بحذف وزيادة بخرء حمام الحرء بالفتح واحد الخرء بالضم. ولا بموت أي ولا ينجس الماء ولا المائعات فيه أي في الماء أو المائع، وهو قيد اتفاقي، حتى لو مات خارجه وألقي فيه يكون الحكم كذلك مراقي الفلاح: ٤٠ ، حاشية الطحطاوي وضفدع [بالكسر ودال مهملة مكسورة] أطلقه وهو مقيد بالبحري، فإن كان الضفدع يفسد الماء إذا كان له دم سائل، وهو ما لا سترة له ، أصابعه وحيوان الماء الحد الفاصل بين المائي والبري أن المائي ما لا يعيش في غير الماء، والبري ما لا يعيش في غير البرّ، واختلف فيما يعيش فيهما، فقال قاضي خان في شرح الجامع الصغير: إنه يفسد. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٠] آدمي ولو جنباً، أو حائضاً، أو نفساء انقطع دمها، أو كافراً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤١] نجاسة: أراد بها نجاسة متيقنة، فلا ينظر إلى ظاهر اشتمال أبوالها على أفخاذها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١]
ولا بوقوع بغل وحمار وسباع طير ووحش في الصحيح، وإن وصل لعاب الواقع إلى كسبع و قرد الماء أخذ حكمه ووجود حيوان ميت فيها ينجسها من يوم وليلة، ومنتفخ من ثلاثة مبتدأ دموي غير مائي أيام ولياليها إن لم يعلم وقت وقوعه.
Rulings on wells and their purification: If a chicken or cat or similar dies in it, the nuzh (removal) of forty buckets is required. If a mouse dies in it and its body is not bloated, the nuzh of twenty buckets is required. That is purification for the well, the bucket, the rope, and the hand of the drawer, like a sparrow after removing what fell into it. The well does not become impure by ba'r (camel dung), rawth (horse dung), or khuthy (cow dung), unless the observer considers it abundant, or every bucket does not come out free of a dung ball. Reliance is upon this, as confirmed in al-Mabsut. Water is not spoiled by the droppings of a pigeon or sparrow, nor by the death of something without flowing blood in it, such as fish, whether land or sea, frog, aquatic animals, bugs, flies, wasps, scorpions, nor by the falling of a human or what is permissible to eat that came out alive and had no impurity on its body. Nuzh is only considered after removing the impurity that fell into it; before removal it is of no benefit, because removal is the cause of purification, unless removal is not possible, like a piece of wood or a cloth that cannot be removed or is hidden, then the required amount is drawn, and the wood and cloth become pure due to the purity of the well. Forty is recommended to be increased to fifty or sixty. That is because the impurity of these things was due to the impurity of the water, so their purification is through its purification, to avoid hardship, like the purification of a wine jug by its fermentation. The bucket is the vessel used for drawing from the well. There is no difference between wells in cities and deserts in the correct view, nor between wet and dry, nor between sound and broken in the apparent narration. Ba'r is the dung of camels, sheep, and gazelles. Khuthy is the plural of khuthya for cows. Know that the original principle is that the well does not become impure by the falling of dung and such unless it is much. They differed on the line between little and much: some said three is much; it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that much is what the viewer considers abundant, and little is what he considers little, and reliance is upon this. Others said much is what covers the entire surface of the water, or what every bucket does not come out free of a dung ball. With the dropping of a pigeon, and death: water and other liquids are not impure when something without flowing blood dies in them or outside and is thrown in, according to the agreed restriction. Frog: it is restricted to sea frogs; a land frog spoils water if it has flowing blood, i.e., without webbed fingers. The dividing line between aquatic and land animals: aquatic animals cannot live out of water, land animals cannot live in water. There is disagreement on those that live in both: Qadi Khan in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir said they spoil the water. A human, even if junub, menstruating, or postpartum bleeding has stopped, or a disbeliever, is allowed. Impurity refers to confirmed impurity, not the apparent inclusion of urine on their thighs. The falling of a mule, donkey, predatory birds, and wild animals does not spoil the water in the correct view. If the saliva of the fallen animal reaches the water, its ruling applies. The presence of a dead animal in it makes the water impure from the day and night if not bloated, and from three days and nights if bloated, when the time of falling is unknown.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings (ahkam) on the purification of wells when impurities fall into them. The text begins by stating the required amount of water to be drawn (nazh) for different animals: forty buckets for a chicken or cat, twenty buckets for a mouse that is not bloated. The purification covers the well, bucket, rope, and the hand of the drawer. After removing the impurity, the actual nazh is performed. If the impurity cannot be removed (e.g., a submerged piece of wood), the required amount is drawn, and the item becomes pure along with the well. The text then discusses that the well does not become impure by animal droppings unless they are abundant, with the authoritative opinion being that abundance is judged by the observer's perception. Next, it states that water is not spoiled by the dropping of birds or by the death of animals without flowing blood (e.g., fish, frogs, insects). A human or a permissible-to-eat animal falling in does not spoil the water if it came out alive and was not carrying impurity. The text also clarifies the definition of aquatic vs. land animals and that a frog with flowing blood spoils the water. Finally, it rules that the falling of mules, donkeys, predatory birds, and wild animals does not spoil the water, but the presence of a dead animal does spoil it, with the duration of impurity calculated from the last day if unknown, and from three days if bloated. The commentary by Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi provides additional details and clarifications.

Key Terms
بعر (ba'r): Dung of camels, sheep, and gazelles.
روث (rawth): Dung of horses, mules, and donkeys.
خثي (khuthy): Dung of cows.
ناظر (nazir): The observer or viewer who judges abundance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon criterion for determining whether dung is abundant enough to spoil the well?
A) A fixed number of three pellets.
B) The entire surface of the water is covered.
C) The observer's personal judgment that it is abundant.
D) Whether the dung floats or sinks.

Key Takeaway
A well does not become impure by animal dung unless the observer considers it abundant.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
5 min
Animals Without Flowing Blood and Their Droppings
Identifies animals that do not spoil water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which animals and birds' droppings and deaths do not spoil well water according to the Hanafi school, and explain the distinction between aquatic and land animals.

Core Idea
Animals without flowing blood do not spoil water when they die in it.

Not all animals that die in a well render the water impure. The text lists several creatures that, due to the absence of flowing blood, do not affect the water's purity. This lesson covers those animals, including birds' droppings and the special case of frogs.

Guided Path
1
List the animals explicitly mentioned
The text says water is not spoiled by: fish, frog (sea frog), aquatic animals, bugs, flies, wasps, scorpions, and the droppings of pigeon and sparrow.
2
Understand the underlying principle
The common factor is that these animals do not have flowing blood (دم سائل). Their death does not cause ritual impurity (najasa).
This is based on the hadith that the blood of a martyr is not najis, but the principle here is general.
3
Distinguish between aquatic and land animals
The text defines aquatic animals as those that cannot live out of water; land animals as those that cannot live in water. Animals that live in both (e.g., some frogs) are disputed: Qadi Khan says they spoil the water.
4
Note the exception for frogs
A frog with webbed fingers (sea frog) is considered aquatic; if it has webbed toes and lives in water, it does not spoil water. A land frog (without webbing) has flowing blood and spoils water.

Source Text

(مراقي الفلاح إلا إلخ : اعلم أن الأصل أن البئر لا تنجس بوقوع البعر وغيره إلا أن يكون الواقع كثيراً، واختلفوا في الفاصل بين القليل والكثير، فقيل: الثلاث كثير، وروي عن أبي حنيفة: أن الكثير ما يستكثره الناظر والقليل ما يستقله وعليه الاعتماد وقيل الكثير ما يغطي وجه الماء كله، وقيل: ما لا يخلو فيه كل دلو عن بعرة. Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings (ahkam) on the purification of wells when impurities fall into them. The text begins by stating the required amount of water to be drawn (nazh) for different animals: forty buckets for a chicken or cat, twenty buckets for a mouse that is not bloated. If the impurity cannot be removed (e.g., a submerged piece of wood), the required amount is drawn, and the item becomes pure along with the well. The text then discusses that the well does not become impure by animal droppings unless they are abundant, with the authoritative opinion being that abundance is judged by the observer's perception. Next, it states that water is not spoiled by the dropping of birds or by the death of animals without flowing blood (e.g., fish, frogs, insects). A human or a permissible-to-eat animal falling in does not spoil the water if it came out alive and was not carrying impurity. Finally, it rules that the falling of mules, donkeys, predatory birds, and wild animals does not spoil the water, but the presence of a dead animal does spoil it, with the duration of impurity calculated from the last day if unknown, and from three days if bloated. Key Terms
دم سائل (dam sa'il): Flowing blood; animals that have blood that flows when wounded.
ضفدع بحري (dafda' bahri): Sea frog; an aquatic frog with webbed toes.
خرء (khar'): Droppings of birds (pigeon, sparrow).

Which of the following, if it dies in a well, does NOT spoil the water according to the text?
A) A mouse

D) A cat

Key Takeaway
Animals without flowing blood (e.g., fish, insects, sea frogs) do not spoil water when they die in it; their droppings also do not spoil water.

Taharah — Purification

Falling of Humans, Edible Animals, and Duration of Impurity
Covers additional cases and retroactive impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings when a human or an edible animal falls into a well alive, and calculate the duration of impurity when a dead animal is found with unknown time of death.

Core Idea
A human or edible animal falling alive and clean does not spoil water; a dead animal found makes water impure retroactively.

The passage concludes with several important rulings: the falling of a human (even in a state of major impurity) does not spoil the water, provided they are not carrying a confirmed impurity. Similarly, animals whose meat is permissible to eat do not spoil water if they fall in alive and exit alive without impurity. The final section covers the retroactive duration of impurity when a dead animal is found in the well with an unknown time of death.

Guided Path
1
Ruling on humans falling in
The text says: 'ولا بوقوع آدمي' – the falling of a human does not spoil the water. This includes a person who is junub, menstruating, or postpartum (after bleeding stops), or a disbeliever. The key is that the person must not be carrying a confirmed impurity on their body.
The impurity referred to is confirmed physical najasa (like blood or urine), not the state of janabah.
2
Ruling on permissible meat animals
The text says: 'وما يؤكل لحمه إذا خرج حيا و لم يكن على بدنه نجاسة' – an animal whose meat is halal, if it falls in alive and comes out alive, and has no impurity on its body, does not spoil the water.
This implies that if the animal dies in the well, it does spoil the water (like a chicken).
3
Ruling on mules, donkeys, predatory birds, and wild animals
The text says: 'ولا بوقوع بغل وحمار وسباع طير ووحش في الصحيح' – the falling of these animals does not spoil the water. Their saliva, however, if it contacts the water, may change the ruling (saliva of a dog-like animal?).
There is a nuance: if the saliva of the fallen animal reaches the water, its ruling applies (implying that the animal's mouth may be impure).
4
Duration of impurity for an unobserved dead animal
If a dead animal is found in the well and the time of its falling is unknown, the water is considered impure for the past day and night if the body is not bloated, and for the past three days and nights if it is bloated.
This is a practical ruling to determine retroactive impurity for actions performed with the water.

Source Text

أحكام الآبار وتطهيرها
وإن مات فيها دجاجة أو هرة أو نحوهما الزم نزح أربعين دلوا، وإن مات فيها فأرة و لم تنتفخ الجثة بالهمز أو نحوها لزم نزح عشرين دلوا، وكان ذلك طهارة للبئر والدلو والرشاء ويد المستقي، كعصفور بعد إخراج ما وقع فيها النزوح بكسر الراء حبل الدلو من الاستقاء ولا تنجس البئر بالبعر والروث والخثي، إلا أن يستكثره الناظر، أو أن لا يخلو دلو للفرس والبغل والحمار وعليه الاعتماد صححه في المبسوط عن بعرة، ولا يفسد الماء بخرء حمام وعصفور، ولا بموت ما لا دم له فيه كسمك أي لا ينجس بريا كان أو بحرياً وضفدع وحيوان الماء وبق وذباب وزنبور وعقرب ولا بوقوع آدمي وما يؤكل أي مائي المولد الا الله لحمه إذا خرج حيا و لم يكن على بدنه نجاسة. أي ولا ينجس نزح إلخ والنزح إنما يعتبر بعد إخراج ما وقع فيها من النجاسة؛ فإن النزح قبله لا يفيد؛ لأنه سبب النجاسة، إلا إذا تعذر إخراجه كخشبة أو خرقة نجسة تعذر إخراجها أو تغيبت فينزح القدر الواجب، وتطهر الخشبة والخرقة تبعاً لطهارة البئر. [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ۳۸ مع تصرف أربعين وتستحب الزيادة إلى خمسين أوستين. (مراقي الفلاح) وكان ذلك إلخ لأن نجاسة هذه الأشياء كانت بنجاسة الماء، فتكون طهارتها بطهارته نفياً للحرج كطهارة دنّ الخمر بتخللها. (مراقي الفلاح) والدلو: أناء يستقى به من البير. البئر ولا فرق بين آبار الأمصار والفلوات في الصحيح، ولا فرق بين الرطب واليابس، والصحيح والمنكسر في ظاهر الرواية. [مراقي الفلاح: ۳۸] بالبعر : رجيع الإبل والغنم والغزال. والخثي: بكسر الخاء، واحد الأخثاء للبقر. (مراقي الفلاح إلا إلخ : اعلم أن الأصل أن البئر لا تنجس بوقوع البعر وغيره إلا أن يكون الواقع كثيراً، واختلفوا في الفاصل بين القليل والكثير، فقيل: الثلاث كثير، وروي عن أبي حنيفة: أن الكثير ما يستكثره الناظر والقليل ما يستقله وعليه الاعتماد وقيل الكثير ما يغطي وجه الماء كله، وقيل: ما لا يخلو فيه كل دلو عن بعرة. (الزيلعي بحذف وزيادة بخرء حمام الحرء بالفتح واحد الخرء بالضم. ولا بموت أي ولا ينجس الماء ولا المائعات فيه أي في الماء أو المائع، وهو قيد اتفاقي، حتى لو مات خارجه وألقي فيه يكون الحكم كذلك مراقي الفلاح: ٤٠ ، حاشية الطحطاوي وضفدع [بالكسر ودال مهملة مكسورة] أطلقه وهو مقيد بالبحري، فإن كان الضفدع يفسد الماء إذا كان له دم سائل، وهو ما لا سترة له ، أصابعه وحيوان الماء الحد الفاصل بين المائي والبري أن المائي ما لا يعيش في غير الماء، والبري ما لا يعيش في غير البرّ، واختلف فيما يعيش فيهما، فقال قاضي خان في شرح الجامع الصغير: إنه يفسد. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٠] آدمي ولو جنباً، أو حائضاً، أو نفساء انقطع دمها، أو كافراً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤١] نجاسة: أراد بها نجاسة متيقنة، فلا ينظر إلى ظاهر اشتمال أبوالها على أفخاذها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١]
ولا بوقوع بغل وحمار وسباع طير ووحش في الصحيح، وإن وصل لعاب الواقع إلى كسبع و قرد الماء أخذ حكمه ووجود حيوان ميت فيها ينجسها من يوم وليلة، ومنتفخ من ثلاثة مبتدأ دموي غير مائي أيام ولياليها إن لم يعلم وقت وقوعه.
Rulings on wells and their purification: If a chicken or cat or similar dies in it, the nuzh (removal) of forty buckets is required. If a mouse dies in it and its body is not bloated, the nuzh of twenty buckets is required. That is purification for the well, the bucket, the rope, and the hand of the drawer, like a sparrow after removing what fell into it. The well does not become impure by ba'r (camel dung), rawth (horse dung), or khuthy (cow dung), unless the observer considers it abundant, or every bucket does not come out free of a dung ball. Reliance is upon this, as confirmed in al-Mabsut. Water is not spoiled by the droppings of a pigeon or sparrow, nor by the death of something without flowing blood in it, such as fish, whether land or sea, frog, aquatic animals, bugs, flies, wasps, scorpions, nor by the falling of a human or what is permissible to eat that came out alive and had no impurity on its body. Nuzh is only considered after removing the impurity that fell into it; before removal it is of no benefit, because removal is the cause of purification, unless removal is not possible, like a piece of wood or a cloth that cannot be removed or is hidden, then the required amount is drawn, and the wood and cloth become pure due to the purity of the well. Forty is recommended to be increased to fifty or sixty. That is because the impurity of these things was due to the impurity of the water, so their purification is through its purification, to avoid hardship, like the purification of a wine jug by its fermentation. The bucket is the vessel used for drawing from the well. There is no difference between wells in cities and deserts in the correct view, nor between wet and dry, nor between sound and broken in the apparent narration. Ba'r is the dung of camels, sheep, and gazelles. Khuthy is the plural of khuthya for cows. Know that the original principle is that the well does not become impure by the falling of dung and such unless it is much. They differed on the line between little and much: some said three is much; it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that much is what the viewer considers abundant, and little is what he considers little, and reliance is upon this. Others said much is what covers the entire surface of the water, or what every bucket does not come out free of a dung ball. With the dropping of a pigeon, and death: water and other liquids are not impure when something without flowing blood dies in them or outside and is thrown in, according to the agreed restriction. Frog: it is restricted to sea frogs; a land frog spoils water if it has flowing blood, i.e., without webbed fingers. The dividing line between aquatic and land animals: aquatic animals cannot live out of water, land animals cannot live in water. There is disagreement on those that live in both: Qadi Khan in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir said they spoil the water. A human, even if junub, menstruating, or postpartum bleeding has stopped, or a disbeliever, is allowed. Impurity refers to confirmed impurity, not the apparent inclusion of urine on their thighs. The falling of a mule, donkey, predatory birds, and wild animals does not spoil the water in the correct view. If the saliva of the fallen animal reaches the water, its ruling applies. The presence of a dead animal in it makes the water impure from the day and night if not bloated, and from three days and nights if bloated, when the time of falling is unknown.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings (ahkam) on the purification of wells when impurities fall into them. The text begins by stating the required amount of water to be drawn (nazh) for different animals: forty buckets for a chicken or cat, twenty buckets for a mouse that is not bloated. The purification covers the well, bucket, rope, and the hand of the drawer. After removing the impurity, the actual nazh is performed. If the impurity cannot be removed (e.g., a submerged piece of wood), the required amount is drawn, and the item becomes pure along with the well. The text then discusses that the well does not become impure by animal droppings unless they are abundant, with the authoritative opinion being that abundance is judged by the observer's perception. Next, it states that water is not spoiled by the dropping of birds or by the death of animals without flowing blood (e.g., fish, frogs, insects). A human or a permissible-to-eat animal falling in does not spoil the water if it came out alive and was not carrying impurity. The text also clarifies the definition of aquatic vs. land animals and that a frog with flowing blood spoils the water. Finally, it rules that the falling of mules, donkeys, predatory birds, and wild animals does not spoil the water, but the presence of a dead animal does spoil it, with the duration of impurity calculated from the last day if unknown, and from three days if bloated. The commentary by Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi provides additional details and clarifications.

Key Terms
آدمي (adami): Human being.
مأكول اللحم (ma'kul al-lahm): Animal whose meat is permissible to eat (e.g., sheep, cow).
منتفخ (muntafikh): Bloated (swollen due to decomposition).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a dead, non-bloated animal is found in a well with an unknown time of death, for how long is the water considered impure retroactively?
A) One day and night
B) Three days and nights
C) Seven days
D) Until the water is changed

Key Takeaway
A human or edible animal falling alive does not spoil water; a dead animal found unknown time spoils water retroactively for 1 day (non-bloated) or 3 days (bloated).
