The Ruling of Istinja: A Strong Sunnah with the Force of Obligation
Defines istinja and states its ruling, with gender difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of istinja and distinguish between the obligations for men and women.

Core Idea
Istinja is a strong sunnah; deliberate omission invalidates prayer and is a major sin.

Istinja – cleansing after relieving oneself – is a daily practice for every Muslim. This passage from Nur al-Idah defines it and clarifies its legal weight. While technically a sunnah, the author emphasizes its necessity: neglecting it deliberately renders prayer invalid and incurs major sin. The passage also highlights a gender difference in the prerequisites for proper cleansing.

Guided Path
1
State the definition of istinja
What is the linguistic and technical meaning? The text defines it as removal of impurity from the private parts using water or stones.
Istinja is from 'najw' meaning what exits from the stomach.
2
Identify the hukm level
Is it fard, wajib, sunnah? The text calls it 'min aqwa sunnat al-wudu' and uses the term 'lazim' to emphasize its strength. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah with the consequence that deliberate omission invalidates prayer.
Lazim is used because omission affects validity, unlike regular sunnah.
3
Understand the consequence of omission
What happens if someone leaves it out deliberately? The text says validity of prayer is lost and it is from the major sins.
4
Distinguish between men and women
What extra step does a man need? Istibra (ensuring no urine remains). Why does a woman not need istibra? Due to the width and shortness of her private part.
Women wait a little before performing istinja.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الاستنجاء

الاستنجاء هو من أقوى سنة الوضوء (حاشية الطحطاوي)] هو قلع النجاسة بنحو الماء، ومثل القلع التقليل بنحو الحجر. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢] وهو في اللغة: مسح موضع النجو أو غسله مطلقاً والنجو: ما يخرج من البطن. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٢] يلزم عبر باللازم؛ لأنه أقوى من الواجب؛ لفوات الصحة بفواته، لا بفوات الواجب حتى كان تركه من الكبائر. مراقي الفلاح: ٤٣ ، حاشية الطحطاوي الرجل ولا تحتاج المرأة إلى الاستبراء يعني المذكور في الرجل؛ لاتساع محلها وقصره، بل تصبر قليلاً ثم تستنجي. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٣، حاشية الطحطاوي]
Chapter on Istinja. Istinja is one of the strongest sunnahs of wudu. It is the removal of impurity by means such as water, and like removal is reduction by means such as stone. In language, it is wiping the place of najw or washing it absolutely; najw is what comes out of the stomach. The expression 'lazim' is used because it is stronger than wajib, since the validity is lost by its omission, not by omission of wajib, to the extent that leaving it is from the major sins. For a man, and a woman does not need istibra (the istibra mentioned for men) due to the width and shortness of her place; rather, she waits a little and then performs istinja.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling on istinja, the cleansing after relieving oneself. The text states that istinja is one of the strongest sunnahs of wudu, meaning it is highly emphasized. However, the commentary clarifies that the term 'lazim' (necessary) is used instead of 'wajib' because the validity of the prayer is lost if istinja is omitted, whereas omission of a regular sunnah does not invalidate. In fact, leaving it deliberately is considered among the major sins. The linguistic definition is provided: it is wiping or washing the place of najw (excrement). The act can be done with water or by using stones (dry cleansing). The passage then distinguishes between men and women: men are required to perform istibra (ensuring no urine remains by moving or coughing) before istinja, but women do not need istibra due to the anatomy of their private part. Instead, a woman should wait a little after urination to ensure it stops, then perform istinja.

Key Terms
استنجاء (istinja): Removal of impurity from the private parts after relieving oneself, using water or stones.
استبراء (istibra): For men, ensuring no urine remains by moving or coughing; women do not need it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because she does not urinate
B) Due to the width and shortness of her private part
C) Because she always uses water
D) Because it is not required for anyone

Key Takeaway
Istinja is a necessary purification act; its deliberate omission invalidates prayer and is a major sin, with men requiring istibra before cleansing.

Rulings on Animals Falling into Wells
Ruling on wells when animals fall in, including saliva and dead animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on water purity when a mule, donkey, or other specified animal falls into a well, and apply the retroactive impurity timeline when a dead animal is found with an unknown time of death.

Core Idea
Water remains pure when certain animals fall in because their bodies are pure; only death causes impurity.

A common concern in traditional settings is the purity of well water after an animal falls in. The Hanafi school provides detailed rules distinguishing between the fall of clean-bodied animals and the discovery of a dead animal. This lesson explains the correct position (al-sahih) and the retroactive impurity calculation for unknown death times.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animals mentioned
The text lists mule, donkey, birds of prey, and wild animals. These are considered to have pure bodies when alive, so their fall does not spoil the water.
The ruling is specific to these animals; other animals may differ.
2
Understand the reasoning
The purity of the body is based on the creation of these animals for human use (utility in riding, etc.). Only death renders them impure.
This is a qiyas (analogical) reasoning from the principle of original purity.
3
Analyze the minority view
Some scholars analogize the animal's moisture to its saliva, requiring draining of all water. The correct (sahih) view rejects this, maintaining purity.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf resolved by tarjih.
4
Apply the saliva ruling
If saliva reaches the water, the water takes the ruling of the saliva: pure if the animal's saliva is pure, impure if impure, disliked if disliked.
This is based on the previous chapter on wells.
5
Apply the dead animal rule
If a dead animal is found and the time of death unknown, the well is considered impure retroactively: from one day and night if not bloated, three days and nights if bloated. This is a precaution (ihtiyat) by Imam Abu Hanifa.
Applies only to bloody land animals, not aquatic or non-bloody.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بوقوع بغل وحمار وسباع طير ووحش في الصحيح، وإن وصل لعاب الواقع إلى كسبع و قرد الحيوان الساقط الماء أخذ حكمه ووجود حيوان ميت فيها ينجسها من يوم وليلة، ومنتفخ من ثلاثة مبتدأ دموي غير مائي أيام ولياليها إن لم يعلم وقت وقوعه. يلزم الرجل مفعول البئر خبر فصل في الاستنجاء ولا إلخ أي لا يفسد الماء بوقوع بغل وحمار فيه، ولا يصير مشكوكاً؛ لأن بدن هذه الحيوانات طاهر؛ لأنها مخلوقة لنا استعمالاً، وإنما تصير نجسة بالموت [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤١] الصحيح: [بسبب طهارة أبدانها ] وقيل: يجب نزح كل الماء؛ إلحاقاً لرطوبتها بلعابها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١] أخذ حكمه: [طهارة ونجاسةً وكراهة أي يكون الماء في حكم اللعاب، فإن كان لعاب الواقع طاهراً فالماء طاهر، وإن كان نجساً فالماء نجس، وإن كان اللعاب مكروهاً فالماء مكروه، وقد علمته في الفصل السابق للآبار. ووجود حيوان إلخ: أي إن وجد حيوان ميت في البئر، ولم يعلم وقت موته، فيحكم بنجاسة البئر مذ يوم وليلة إن لم ينتفخ، ومذ ثلاثة أيام ولياليها إن انتفخ وهذا عند الإمام احتياطاً قيد بـ"الحيوان"؛ لأن غيره من النجاسات لا يتأتى فيه التفصيل ولا الخلاف بل يحكم بنجاسة البئر من وقت الوجدان فقط، والمراد: الحيوان الدموي غير المائي، وقيد بـ "عدم العلم"؛ لأنه إن علم أو ظن فلا إشكال، ويعتبر الحكم من وقته بلا خلاف. واعلم أن قوله ينجسها يعني به في حق الوضوء، حتى يلزمهم إعادة الصلاة إذا توضؤوا منها، وأما في حق غيره فإنه يحكم بنجاستها في الحال من غير إسناد؛ لأنه من باب وجود النجاسة في الثوب حتى إذا كانوا غسلوا الثياب بمائها لا يلزمهم إلا غسلها على الصحيح. من يوم إلخ : فيلزم إعادة صلوات تلك المدة إذا توضؤوا منها وهم محدثون أو اغتسلوا من جنابة، و إن كانوا متوضئين أو غسلوا الثياب لا عن نجاسة، فلا إعادة إجماعاً [ مراقي الفلاح: ٤١] وقوعه: الأولى أن يقول: وقت موته" بدل "وقت وقوعه"
And [the water] is not spoiled by the fall of a mule, donkey, birds of prey, and wild animals, according to the correct [position]. And if the saliva of the falling [animal] reaches the water, it takes its ruling. And the presence of a dead animal in it [the well] renders it impure from a day and a night, and if bloated then from three days and their nights, if the time of its fall is unknown. It obligates the man... the object of 'well' the predicate... Section on Istinja': 'And not etc.' meaning the water is not spoiled by the fall of a mule and donkey in it, nor does it become doubtful, because the body of these animals is pure, for they are created for our use, and they only become impure by death. The correct [view]: [due to purity of their bodies]. And it was said: it is obligatory to drain all the water, by analogizing its moisture to its saliva. It takes its ruling: [purity, impurity, and dislike], meaning the water is subject to the ruling of the saliva: if the saliva of the falling is pure, then the water is pure; if impure, then the water is impure; if disliked, then the water is disliked, as you learned in the previous chapter on wells. And 'the presence of an animal etc.': meaning if a dead animal is found in the well and the time of its death is unknown, then the well is ruled impure from a day and a night if not bloated, and from three days and nights if bloated. This is by Imam [Abu Hanifa] as a precaution. He restricted it to 'animal' because other impurities do not admit such detail nor difference, but the well is ruled impure from the moment of finding only. And the intended [animal] is the bloody, non-aquatic animal. And he restricted it with 'lack of knowledge' because if known or thought, there is no problem, and the ruling is considered from its time without disagreement. Know that his statement 'it renders it impure' means with respect to wudu, so that they must repeat prayer if they performed wudu from it. As for other than that, then it is ruled impure immediately without attribution, because it is of the chapter of impurity on the garment, so that if they washed clothes with its water, they are only obligated to wash them [again] according to the correct view. 'From a day etc.': so they must repeat prayers of that period if they performed wudu from it while in a state of hadath or performed ghusl from janabah. But if they were already in a state of wudu or washed clothes without impurity, there is no repetition by consensus. 'Its fall': it is better to say 'time of its death' instead of 'time of its fall'.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding wells when animals fall into them. The text first states the ruling: according to the correct position (al-sahih), the water is not spoiled by the fall of a mule, donkey, birds of prey, or wild animals. This is because the bodies of these animals are considered pure (tahir) since they are created for human use. They only become impure upon death. There is a minority view that all water must be drained, reasoning that the animal's moisture is analogous to its saliva. The text then addresses two additional scenarios: first, if the saliva of the falling animal reaches the water, the water takes the ruling of that saliva—if the saliva is pure, the water is pure; if impure, impure; if disliked, disliked. Second, if a dead animal is found in the well and the time of its death is unknown, the well is considered impretroactively: from a day and night if not bloated, three days and nights if bloated. This is a precaution (ihtiyat) from Imam Abu Hanifa. The commentary specifies that this applies only to bloody land animals, not aquatic ones, and only when the time is unknown. The impurity ruling applies specifically to wudu (ablution), requiring repetition of prayers performed with that water. For washing clothes, only the clothes need rewashing.

Key Terms
الصحيح (al-sahih): The correct or preferred position in the madhhab
نجاسة (najasah): Impurity, specifically the state of being ritually impure
احتياط (ihtiyat): Precautionary measure, especially in matters of worship

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi position, if a dead, bloated cat is found in a well and the time of death is unknown, from when is the well considered impure?
A) From the moment of finding.
B) From one day and night before finding.
C) From three days and nights before finding.
D) From one week before finding.

Key Takeaway
Water remains pure when certain animals fall in because their bodies are pure; only death or specific saliva contaminates, with retroactive impurity for unknown death times.

Rulings on Istinja' and Istibra'
Definition and ruling of istinja' with conditions on impurity amount and istibra'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of istinja' based on the amount of impurity and distinguish between istinja', istibra', and istinqa'.

Core Idea
Istinja' is sunnah for small impurity, wajib for dirham-sized, and fard for larger; istibra' is essential for men to ensure purity.

This passage from Nur al-Idah explains the rulings of istinja' (cleansing after using the toilet) in detail. It clarifies that istinja' is not always obligatory—its ruling depends on the amount of impurity. The passage also introduces istibra' (ensuring urine flow has ceased) and distinguishes it from istinja' and istinqa' (polishing). Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correct purification before wudu and salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general category
Istinja' is the removal of impurity from the private parts using water or stones. It is a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) when the impurity does not exceed the exit opening.
2
Determine the ruling based on impurity amount
If the impurity equals a dirham in size, removal with water becomes wajib. If it exceeds a dirham, washing with water or any liquid becomes fard (obligatory). The dirham is defined either by weight (20 qirats) for solid impurity or by area (palm width) for liquid impurity.
The Hanafi position reconciles the two narrations: weight for solids, area for liquids.
3
Meet the prerequisite: istibra' for men
Men must perform istibra' (actions to ensure complete cessation of urine) before istinja'. Methods include walking, coughing, or lying down until one is certain no drips remain. Women do not need istibra'.
Starting wudu before certainty of istibra' is not permissible.
4
Distinguish between istinja', istibra', and istinqa'
Istinja' is the removal using stones or water. Istibra' is moving the feet or other actions to ensure urine has stopped. Istinqa' is polishing to remove smell, using stones or fingers.
These terms are often confused but have distinct meanings and rulings.
5
Apply the definition of dirham
The dirham measurement is crucial for determining the ruling. The correct view is: weight (20 qirats) for solid impurity, area (palm width) for liquid. This affects whether istinja' is sunnah, wajib, or fard.
Al-Sarakhsi considered the dirham of his time by weight.

Source Text

فصل: لا يخفى حسن تقديمه على الوضوء. (حاشية الطحطاوي) الاستنجاء هو من أقوى سنة الوضوء (حاشية الطحطاوي)] هو قلع النجاسة بنحو الماء، ومثل القلع التقليل بنحو الحجر. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢] وهو في اللغة: مسح موضع النجو أو غسله مطلقاً والنجو: ما يخرج من البطن. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٢] يلزم عبر باللازم؛ لأنه أقوى من الواجب؛ لفوات الصحة بفواته، لا بفوات الواجب حتى كان تركه من الكبائر. مراقي الفلاح: ٤٣ ، حاشية الطحطاوي الرجل ولا تحتاج المرأة إلى الاستبراء يعني المذكور في الرجل؛ لاتساع محلها وقصره، بل تصبر قليلاً ثم تستنجي. [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٣] :يزول بزوال البلل، أي لا يظهر على الحجر بوضعه على المخرج. البول خصه؛ لأن الغالب أن يتأخر البول، وإلا فالغائط كذلك؛ إذ لا فرق [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٣] ويطمئن قال في "المضمرات": ومتى وقع في قلبه أنه صار طاهراً جاز له أن يستنجي؛ لأن كل أحدٍ أعلم بحاله. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٣] أو التنحنح بفتح الأول والثاني وسكون الحاء المهملة، وضم النون الثانية، ترديد الصوت في الحلق لتنقيته. أو الاضطجاع وضع الجنب على الأرض ونحوها. أو غيره بنقل أقدام وركض وعصر ذكر برفق. سنة : أطلقه فشمل الرجال والنساء، وما إذا كان في القبل أو الدبر، وقيل: يستحب في القبل. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٥] من نجس إلخ قيد به؛ لأن الريح طاهر على الصحيح، وقوله: "يخرج إلخ" جرى على الغالب؛ إذ لو أصاب المخرج نجاسة من غيره يطهر بالاستنجاء كالخارج، وخرج به حدث من غير السبيلين كالنوم؛ فإن الاستنجاء من هذه الأحداث كلها بدعة كما في "القهستاني"، وقوله: "ما لم يتجاوز المخرج" قيد لتسميته استنجاء ولكونه مسنوناً، لا لأصل الغسل. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٤] الدرهم اختلفت الرواية في الدرهم فقيل: يعتبر بالوزن وهو أن يكون وزنه قدر الدرهم الكبير المثقال وهو عشرون قيراطاً، والقيراط خمس شعيرات، وقيل: بالمساحة وهو قدر عرض الكف، ووفق أبو جعفر بين الروايتين فقال: أراد محمد بذكر العرض تقدير النجاسة المائعة، وبذكر الوزن تقدير النجاسة المتجسدة، وهذا هو الصحيح، وقال السرخسي يعتبر بدرهم .زمانه تبيين الحقائق: ۲۰۰] وجب إزالته إلخ لأنه من باب إزالة النجاسة، فلا يكفي مسحه بالحجر، والتقييد بالماء اتفاقي وإلا فيصح إزالته بالمائع أيضا. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٤]
Section: It is not hidden the excellence of its precedence over wudu. Istinja' is from the strongest sunnah of wudu. It is the removal of impurity by means of water, and like removal is reduction by means of stones. [It means] in language: wiping the place of excrement or washing it absolutely, and 'najw' is what exits from the belly. He used 'obligatory' [lazim] because it is stronger than wajib, for soundness is lost by its omission, not by omission of wajib, so its abandonment is from the major sins. [Istinja' is obligatory for] the man, and the woman does not need istibra', meaning that which is mentioned for the man, because of the width and shortness of her place, but she waits a little then performs istinja'. Istibra': until the trace of urine disappears, and his heart is at rest according to his habit, either by walking, or clearing the throat, or lying down, or other than that. And it is not permissible for him to begin wudu until he is certain of the cessation of urine drip. And istinja' is sunnah from impurity that exits from the two passages as long as it does not exceed the exit; and if it exceeds and is the amount of a dirham, its removal with water becomes obligatory; and if it exceeds a dirham, its washing becomes fard (obligatory) with water or liquid. Istibra': Know that the difference between istinja', istibra', and istinqa' is as stated in al-Muqaddimah al-Ghaznawiyyah: istinja' is the use of stone or water; istibra' is moving the feet and kicking with them and the like until one is certain of the cessation of the trace of urine; istinqa' is purification, which is to rub with stones during istijmar, or with fingers during istinja' with water until the foul smell goes away. 'Disappears with disappearance of moisture': i.e., it does not appear on the stone when placed on the exit. He specified urine because generally urine is delayed; otherwise feces is likewise, as there is no difference. 'And his heart is at rest': It is stated in al-Mudmarat: whenever it occurs in his heart that he has become pure, it is permissible for him to perform istinja', because everyone knows his own condition best. 'Or clearing the throat': with fatha on first and second, sukun on the important ha, and dhamma on the second nun, producing sound in the throat to clear it. 'Or lying down': placing the side on the ground and the like. 'Or other': by moving feet, kicking, and gently squeezing the penis. 'Sunnah': he mentioned it absolutely, including men and women, and whether it is from front or back; and it was said it is recommended for the front. 'From impurity etc.': he restricted it because wind is pure according to the correct view. And his statement 'exits etc.' follows the usual case; for if impurity from other than the exit reaches the place, it is purified by istinja' like the exit. And it excludes hadath from other than the two passages, like sleep, for istinja' from all such events is bid'ah as in al-Qahastani. And his statement 'as long as it does not exceed the exit' restricts its being called istinja' and its being sunnah, not the obligation of washing itself. The dirham: narrations differed regarding the dirham. It was said it is considered by weight: its weight is equal to the large dirham (mithqal), which is twenty qirats, and a qirat is five barley grains. And it was said it is by area: the width of the palm. Abu Ja'far reconciled the two narrations, saying: Muhammad intended by mentioning width the estimation of liquid impurity, and by mentioning weight the estimation of solid impurity, and this is correct. Al-Sarakhsi said it is considered by the dirham of his time. [It is] obligated to remove it etc. because it is from the chapter of removing impurity, so wiping with a stone is not sufficient. The restriction to water is incidental; otherwise it is valid to remove it with any liquid.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings related to istinja' (cleansing after using the toilet). It begins by emphasizing that istinja' is one of the strongest sunnah acts of wudu, and its omission is considered a major sin. The text defines istinja' linguistically as wiping or washing the place of excrement. It then discusses istibra' (ensuring the complete cessation of urine flow), which is obligatory for men but not for women due to anatomical differences. Methods of istibra' include walking, coughing, lying down, etc. The ruling on istinja' itself depends on the amount of impurity: if it does not exceed the exit opening, it is sunnah; if it equals the size of a dirham, removal with water is wajib; if larger, it is fard to wash with water or any liquid. The text then distinguishes between istinja', istibra', and istinqa' (polishing). Finally, it discusses the definition of a dirham for measuring impurity: there is a difference of opinion between weight (20 qirats) and area (width of palm), with a reconciliation that weight is for solid impurity and area for liquid. The relied-upon position is that removal is obligatory, and any liquid (not just water) suffices.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinja'): Removal of impurity from the two passages using water or stones
الاستبراء (al-istibra'): Actions to ensure complete cessation of urine flow
الدرهم (al-dirham): A unit of measurement for impurity: either weight (20 qirats) or area (width of palm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if the impurity from the two passages is the size of a dirham?
A) It is sunnah to remove it with water.
B) It is wajib to remove it with water.
C) It is fard to wash it with water or any liquid.
D) It is permissible to use stones only.

Key Takeaway
The ruling of istinja' is graded: sunnah for small amounts, wajib for dirham-sized, and fard for larger; istibra' is essential for men to ensure complete purity before wudu.

Istibra, Istinja, and Istinqa: Definitions and the Sunnah Ruling of Istinja
Defining three related terms and stating the ruling of istinja as sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between istibra, istinja, and istinqa and state the Hanafi ruling on istinja as sunnah muakkadah, including when it becomes wajib or fard based on the size of impurity.

Core Idea
Istinja is sunnah for impurities within the outlet; only when impurity exceeds a dirham does washing become obligatory.

Cleansing oneself after using the toilet involves three distinct steps: istibra (ensuring the flow stops), istinja (washing or wiping), and istinqa (polishing to remove odor). The Hanafi school holds that istinja itself is a stressed sunnah, not a duty, as long as the impurity remains within the immediate exit. But when the impurity spreads beyond, the ruling changes based on its size. This passage from Nur al-Idah lays out these foundational definitions and the precise conditions that shift the ruling from sunnah to wajib to fard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three terms and their definitions
Locate the definitions of istibra, istinja, and istinqa in the text. Note the actions each involves: istibra (moving feet, clearing throat, etc.), istinja (use of stone or water), istinqa (rubbing to remove odor).
The passage quotes Al-Muqaddimat al-Ghaznaviyyah for these definitions.
2
Pinpoint the default ruling of istinja
Find the statement 'والاستنجاء سنة من نجس يخرج من السبيلين' and note that it applies to any impurity from the two passages as long as it does not exceed the outlet. Also note that this ruling is general for men and women.
The word 'سنة' is absolute, covering both gender and both passages.
3
Trace the threshold conditions
Understand the condition 'ما لم يتجاوز المخرج' and the escalation: if impurity exceeds the outlet and is the size of a dirham or less, washing becomes wajib; if more than a dirham, it becomes fard.
The dirham is a measure of impurity; its exact size is defined in fiqh texts.
4
Note important exceptions and clarifications
The text clarifies that wind (ريح) is pure, so no istinja is needed. Also, events from other than the two passages (like sleep) do not require istinja; doing so would be an innovation.
This prevents misconceived practices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة أحكام الاستنجاء الاستبراء حتى يزول أثر البول، ويطمئن قلبه على حسب عادته، إما بالمشي أو التنحنح أو الاضطجاع أو غيره، ولا يجوز له الشروع في الوضوء حتى يطمئن أي يطمئن بزوال رشح البول. والاستنجاء سنة من نجس يخرج من السبيلين ما لم يتجاوز المخرج، وإن تجاوز وكان قدر الدرهم وجب إزالته بالماء، وإن زاد على الدرهم افترض غسله بالماء أو المائع الاستبراء: اعلم أن الفرق بين الاستنجاء والاستبراء والاستنقاء ما قاله في المقدمة الغزنوية من أن الاستنجاء استعمال الحجر أو الماء، والاستبراء نقل الأقدام والركض بها ونحو ذلك حتى يستيقن بزوال أثر البول، والاستنقاء هو النقاوة، وهو أن يدلك بالأحجار حال الاستجمار، أو بالأصابع حال الاستنجاء بالماء حتى تذهب الرائحة الكريهة. يزول بزوال البلل، أي لا يظهر على الحجر بوضعه على المخرج. ويطمئن قال في المضمرات: ومتى وقع في قلبه أنه صار طاهراً جاز له أن يستنجي؛ لأن كل أحدٍ أعلم بحاله. أو التنحنح بفتح الأول والثاني وسكون الحاء المهملة، وضم النون الثانية، ترديد الصوت في الحلق لتنقيته. أو الاضطجاع وضع الجنب على الأرض ونحوها. أو غيره بنقل أقدام وركض وعصر ذكر برفق. سنة : أطلقه فشمل الرجال والنساء، وما إذا كان في القبل أو الدبر، وقيل: يستحب في القبل. من نجس إلخ قيد به؛ لأن الريح طاهر على الصحيح، وقوله: يخرج إلخ جرى على الغالب؛ إذ لو أصاب المخرج نجاسة من غيره يطهر بالاستنجاء كالخارج، وخرج به حدث من غير السبيلين كالنوم؛ فإن الاستنجاء من هذه الأحداث كلها بدعة كما في القهستاني، وقوله: ما لم يتجاوز المخرج قيد لتسميته استنجاء ولكونه مسنوناً، لا لأصل الغسل.
The Book of Purity. Rulings of Istinja: Istibra until the trace of urine disappears, and his heart is at ease according to his custom, either by walking, or clearing the throat, or lying down, or other. He is not permitted to begin ablution until he is at ease by the cessation of the drip of urine. And istinja is a sunnah for impurity that exits from the two passages as long as it does not exceed the outlet. If it exceeds and is the size of a dirham, its removal with water becomes wajib; if it exceeds a dirham, washing it with water or liquid becomes obligatory. Istibra: Know that the difference between istinja, istibra, and istinqa is what was said in Al-Muqaddimat al-Ghaznaviyyah: Istinja is the use of stone or water; istibra is moving the feet and kicking with them and the like until one is certain of the disappearance of the trace of urine; istinqa is cleanliness, which is to rub with stones during istijmar, or with fingers during istinja with water until the foul smell disappears. It disappears with the disappearance of moisture, i.e., it does not appear on the stone when placed on the outlet. He is at ease: He said in Al-Mudmarat: Whenever it occurs in his heart that he has become pure, it is permissible for him to perform istinja, because everyone knows his own state best. Or clearing the throat: with fatha of the first and second, sukun of the important ha, and damm of the second nun, repeating the sound in the throat to clear it. Or lying down: placing the side on the ground or similar. Or other: by moving feet, kicking, and gently squeezing the penis. Sunnah: It is general, including men and women, whether it is from the front or the back, and it is said it is recommended for the front. Condition: 'of impurity', to restrict it because wind is pure according to the correct view. His statement 'exits etc.' follows the general case; if impurity from other than the exit touches the outlet, it is purified by istinja like the exiting impurity. Events from other than the two passages such as sleep are excluded; istinja from all these events is an innovation as in Al-Qahistani. His statement: 'as long as it does not exceed the outlet' is a condition for calling it istinja and for its being sunnah, not for the basis of washing.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage provides foundational definitions and the primary ruling on istinja. It first describes istibra—the process of ensuring no more urine will drip after urination—using walking, coughing, or lying down. This is necessary before starting wudu. Then it defines istinja (using stone or water to cleanse the private parts) as sunnah for any impurity (najis) that exits from the front or back, provided the impurity does not spread beyond the immediate exit area. If it does spread and is the size of a dirham or less, washing it with water becomes wajib (obligatory); if more than a dirham, it becomes fard (obligatory) to wash with water or any purifying liquid. The passage then clarifies the terminology: istibra is the active effort to stop the flow, istinja is the cleansing, and istinqa is polishing to remove odor. It specifies that wind is pure, so istinja is not needed for it. The sunnah applies to both genders and both passages, though some recommend istinja only for the front. Importantly, istinja from sleep or other events not originating from the two passages is considered an innovation. The condition 'as long as it does not exceed the outlet' defines the scope of the sunnah ruling, not the general obligation of washing the impurity.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinja): Cleansing the private parts with stone or water after relieving oneself.
الاستبراء (al-istibra): Moving the feet or other actions to ensure no more urine emerges before istinja.
الاستنقاء (al-istinqa): Polishing the area after istinja to remove any remaining trace or odor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on istinja for impurity that exits from the private parts and does not exceed the outlet?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Fard
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Istinja is a sunnah act for impurities within the outlet; only when impurity exceeds a dirham does washing become obligatory.

The Dirham Measure and Obligation of Impurity Removal
Ruling on impurity size and obligation of removal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi measures of a dirham (weight vs area) and apply the ruling that impurity exceeding a dirham requires washing with water (fard) while a dirham's size requires wajib washing.

Core Idea
The dirham measure defines the threshold between sunnah, wajib, and fard in impurity removal.

This passage opens with a fundamental question: how much impurity triggers a legal obligation beyond mere sunnah? The Hanafi school establishes a precise measure based on the dirham coin, with two methods for solids and liquids. The ruling then extends to ghusl, where washing the outlet is obligatory even if the impurity is small.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two narrations on the dirham measure
Note that some scholars define it by weight (20 qirat) and others by area (width of palm). Understand the reconciliation by Abu Ja'far: weight for solid impurity, area for liquid impurity.
Al-Sarakhsi later considered the dirham of his time.
2
Apply the dirham measure to impurity removal
Impurity less than a dirham: istinja is sunnah. Exactly a dirham: removal is wajib. More than a dirham: removal is fard. Wiping with stone is insufficient for wajib/fard; water (or liquid) is required.
The restriction to water is incidental; other liquids work.
3
Understand the obligation during ghusl
Washing the private part (including inside the outlet) is obligatory during ghusl from janabah, haid, and nifas, even if the impurity is small. This contradicts the common belief that istinja is only sunnah.
The sunnah is the preceding of istinja, not the washing itself.
4
Distinguish the levels of obligation
Sunnah (less than dirham) vs wajib (dirham) vs fard (exceeding dirham). The different levels are based on the strength of evidence and the dirham measure.
The Shafi'i school does not use this measure; they require removal of any impurity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدرهم اختلفت الرواية في الدرهم فقيل: يعتبر بالوزن وهو أن يكون وزنه قدر الدرهم الكبير المثقال وهو عشرون قيراطاً، والقيراط خمس شعيرات، وقيل: بالمساحة وهو قدر عرض الكف، ووفق أبو جعفر بين الروايتين فقال: أراد محمد بذكر العرض تقدير النجاسة المائعة، وبذكر الوزن تقدير النجاسة المتجسدة، وهذا هو الصحيح، وقال السرخسي يعتبر بدرهم زمانه. وجب إزالته إلخ لأنه من باب إزالة النجاسة، فلا يكفي مسحه بالحجر، والتقييد بالماء اتفاقي وإلا فيصح إزالته بالمائع أيضا. ويفترض غسل ما في المخرج عند الاغتسال من الجنابة والحيض والنفاس وإن كان ما في المخرج قليلا وأن يستنجي بحجر منق ونحوه، والغسل بالماء أحب، والأفضل الجمع بين الماء والحجر، فيمسح ثم يغسل ويجوز أن يقتصر على الماء أو الحجر فقط، والسنة إنقاء المحل، والعدد في الأحجار مندوب لا سنة مؤكدة، فيستنجي بثلاثة أحجار ندبا إن حصل التنظيف بما دونها. وكيفية الاستنجاء أن يمسح بالحجر الأول من جهة المقدم إلى خلف، وبالثاني من خلف إلى قدام، وبالثالث من قدام إلى خلف إذا كانت الخصية مدلاة، وإن كانت غير مدلاة يبتدئ من خلف إلى قدام والمرأة تبتدئ من قدام إلى خلف خشية تلويث فرجها، ويفترض: لأن غسل سائر الجسد فرض في الغسل، فلو لم يغسل ما في المخرج قليلاً كان أو كثيراً، بقي ما عليه النجاسة من غير غسل، فلا يصح الغسل. فإن قلت: هذا ينافي ما اشتهر بأن الاستنجاء من سنن الغسل قلت المسنون هو تقديم الاستنجاء لا نفسه غسل أي إزالة ما في المخرج بغسله بالماء المطلق. وأن يستنجي بحجر منق بأن لا يكون خشناً كالآجر، ولا أملس كالعقيق. أحب: لحصول الطهارة المتفق عليها، وإقامة السنة على الوجه الأكمل؛ لأن الحجر مقلل والمائع غير الماء مختلف في تطهيره. والأفضل: أطلقه فأفاد الأفضلية في كل زمان وقيل: الجمع إنما هو سنة في زماننا، أما في الزمان الأول فأدب؛ لأنهم كانوا يبعرون. يقتصر إلخ والاقتصار على الماء فقط أقرب في الفضل من الاقتصار على الحجر، فإنه دونهما، ولكن يحصل السنة وإن تفاوت الفضل. إنقاء إلخ لأنه المقصود، فلو لم يحصل الإنقاء بثلاث يزاد عليها إجماعا؛ لكونه هو المقصود، ولو حصل الإنقاء بواحد واقتصر عليه جاز كما ذكر. لا سنة مؤكدة: لما ورد من التخيير؛ لقوله : 'من استجمر فليوتر، من فعل فقد أحسن، ومن لا فلا حرج، فإنه لا يحتمل التأويل، فيدل على نفي وجوب الاستنجاء، وعلى نفي وجوب العدد فيه'. كانت: يفيد عموم الأزمنة صيفاً وشتاءً. يبتدئ: لكونه أبلغ في التنظيف.
The dirham: Narrations differ about the dirham. Some say it is considered by weight: its weight should be the weight of the large dirham of mithqal, which is twenty qirats, and a qirat is five barley grains. Others say by area: the width of the palm. Abu Ja'far reconciled the two narrations: He said Muhammad intended by 'width' the estimation of liquid impurity, and by 'weight' the estimation of solid impurity, and this is correct. Al-Sarakhsi said it is considered by the dirham of his time. Washing it becomes obligatory because it is from the chapter of removing impurity; wiping it with stone is not sufficient, and the restriction to water is incidental, otherwise removing it with a liquid is also correct. And it is obligatory to wash what is in the outlet during ghusl from janabah, haid, and nifas, even if what is in the outlet is small. And that one should perform istinja with a smooth stone or similar, and washing with water is more beloved, and the best is to combine water and stone: wipe then wash. It is permissible to limit to water only or stone only. The sunnah is to cleanse the area, and the number of stones is recommended (mandub), not an emphatic sunnah. So one performs istinja with three stones as a recommendation if cleansing is achieved with less. The method of istinja is to wipe with the first stone from the front backward, with the second from back to front, and with the third from front to back if the testicles are pendulous; if not pendulous, he starts from back to front. The woman starts from front to back for fear of soiling her vulva. And it is obligatory because washing the rest of the body is obligatory in ghusl; if one does not wash what is in the outlet, small or large, impurity remains unwashed, so ghusl is not valid. If you say: This contradicts what is well-known that istinja is from the sunan of ghusl, I say: The sunnah is the preceding of istinja, not the washing itself, i.e., removing what is in the outlet by washing it with absolute water. And that he perform istinja with a smooth stone: it should not be rough like brick nor smooth like agate. More beloved: because of achieving agreed-upon purity and performing the sunnah in the most complete manner; because the stone reduces and liquids other than water are disputed in their purifying ability. The best: It is general, indicating preference in every time; it is said that combining is sunnah in our time, but in earlier times it was adab because they would use dung. He said 'limit etc.': limiting to water only is closer in virtue than limiting to stone only, for it is inferior to the two, but the sunnah is achieved even if virtue differs. Cleansing etc. because it is the objective; if cleansing is not achieved with three, more are added by consensus because it is the objective; if cleansing is achieved with one and one limits to it, it is permissible as mentioned. Not an emphatic sunnah: because of the reported option; due to his saying: 'Whoever performs istijmar (cleansing with stones) should do so with an odd number; whoever does so has done well, and whoever does not is not sinful.' This cannot be interpreted figuratively, so it indicates the negation of the obligation of istinja and the negation of obligation of number in it. 'Were': indicates generality of times, summer and winter. 'She begins': because it is more effective in cleaning.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage expands on the rulings introduced earlier. It begins with a crucial discussion on the measure of a dirham—the threshold distinguishing wajib from fard in removing impurity. There are two narrations: by weight (20 qirat, each qirat = 5 barley grains) and by area (width of palm). Abu Ja'far reconciles: weight for solid impurity, area for liquid impurity. Al-Sarakhsi favors the dirham of his time. If impurity reaches a dirham, removal with water is wajib; if more, it is fard. The obligation (fard) is stressed: mere wiping with stone is insufficient; water (or any liquid) is required. Next, the passage addresses ghusl: washing the private part (including within the outlet) is obligatory during ghusl from major impurity, even if the impurity is small—contradicting a common understanding that istinja is only sunnah. The commentary clarifies: it is the preceding of istinja that is sunnah, not the washing itself. Then, the preferred method of istinja: using a smooth stone (not rough or too smooth), with water being superior, and combining water and stone being the best. However, using only water or only stone is permissible and fulfills the sunnah. The number of stones is mandub (recommended), not sunnah muakkadah, based on the hadith: 'من استجمر فليوتر...' (whoever uses stones should use an odd number; doing good is fine, not doing is no sin)—this proves no obligation. The method differs by gender and anatomy: a man with pendulous testicles wipes front-to-back first, then back-to-front, then front-to-back; a woman always wipes front-to-back to avoid soiling. The objective is cleanliness (inaqa); if not achieved with three stones, more are added; if achieved with one, it suffices.

Key Terms
الدرهم (al-dirham): A silver coin used as a measure for the minimum amount of impurity that triggers wajib/fard washing; approximately the size of a large dirham (20 qirat) or the width of the palm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on impurity that is exactly the size of a dirham?
A) Sunnah to remove
B) Wajib to wash with water
C) Fard to wash with water
D) Haram to leave unwashed

Key Takeaway
The dirham measure is the Hanafi tool for grading impurity removal: less than dirham = sunnah, exactly dirham = wajib, more = fard; and during ghusl, washing the outlet is fard regardless.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
The Method of Istinja: Stones, Water, and Gender Differences
Method of istinja including materials, number, and gender differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the method of istinja using stones or water, state that the number of stones is recommended (mandub) not obligatory, and apply the gender-specific wiping directions.

Core Idea
The objective of istinja is cleanliness (ināqa); the number of stones is recommended, not obligatory.

This passage details the practical method of cleansing after using the toilet. It covers the preferred materials (smooth stone or water), the number of stones, and the specific wiping directions for men and women. A key point is that the number three is recommended (mandub) based on the hadith that allows an odd number without obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended materials for istinja
The passage recommends a smooth stone (not rough nor too smooth) and prefers water, with the best being to combine both: wipe then wash. However, using only water or only stone is permissible.
Water is more beloved because it achieves agreed-upon purity.
2
Understand the number of stones
The sunnah is to cleanse the area (ināqa). Using three stones is recommended (mandub), not an emphatic sunnah. The hadith 'من استجمر فليوتر' shows the odd number is optional.
If cleansing is achieved with one stone, it suffices; if not achieved with three, more stones are added.
3
Apply the gender-specific wiping method
For a man with pendulous testicles: wipe front-to-back, then back-to-front, then front-to-back. If testicles are not pendulous: start back-to-front. A woman always wipes front-to-back to avoid soiling the vulva.
The method ensures thorough cleaning and prevents spreading impurity.
4
Distinguish between sunnah and mandub
The act of istinja itself is not wajib; the sunnah is the cleansing. The number of stones is mandub (recommended), not sunnah muakkadah, based on the hadith's explicit permission to omit odd number.
This reinforces the Hanafi position that the dirham measure determines obligation, not the number of stones.

Source Text

الدرهم اختلفت الرواية في الدرهم فقيل: يعتبر بالوزن وهو أن يكون وزنه قدر الدرهم الكبير المثقال وهو عشرون قيراطاً، والقيراط خمس شعيرات، وقيل: بالمساحة وهو قدر عرض الكف، ووفق أبو جعفر بين الروايتين فقال: الاستجمار (al-istijmar): Cleansing the private parts using stones or similar dry objects after relieving oneself.
الإنقاء (al-inaqa): Complete cleansing of the area until no impurity or odor remains.

beginner
6 min
The Obligation of Washing the Exit (Makhraj) During Ghusl
Focuses on the fard of washing the exit during ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that washing the private parts (makhraj) during ghusl from janabah, menstruation, or postnatal bleeding is fard, and explain why it is considered fard based on the general obligation of washing the entire body.

Core Idea
Washing the exit during ghusl is fard; leaving it unwashed invalidates the ghusl.

This lesson focuses on the first part of the passage: the ruling on washing the private parts during the ritual bath (ghusl). Many assume istinja (cleaning after toilet) is the same as washing during ghusl, but the text clarifies that washing the exit during ghusl is a distinct obligation (fard). The reasoning is that since the entire body must be washed, any remaining impurity—however small—invalidates the ghusl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage explicitly states: 'ويفترض غسل ما في المخرج عند الاغتسال من الجنابة والحيض والنفاس' – it is obligatory (fard) to wash whatever is in the exit during ghusl from janabah, menstruation, and postnatal bleeding.
The ruling is unconditional: even if the impurity is little.
2
Locate the proof for the obligation
The proof is not a separate dalil but a logical deduction (qiyas): since washing the rest of the body is fard, failing to wash the exit leaves impurity, which invalidates the ghusl. The passage states: 'لأن غسل سائر الجسد فرض في الغسل' – because washing the rest of the body is fard in ghusl.
The proof is based on the general fard of ghusl (Quran 5:6).
3
Address the potential objection
The passage anticipates a common objection: if istinja is sunnah of ghusl, then washing the exit would be sunnah, not fard. The response clarifies that the sunnah is the preceding of istinja (i.e., doing it before ghusl), not the washing itself. The actual washing during ghusl is fard.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the Hanafi position.
4
Note the consequence of omission
If the exit is not washed during ghusl, the impurity remains, and the ghusl is invalid (batil). Therefore, one must repeat the ghusl.
This elevates the ruling to a fard 'ayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة
أحكام الاستنجاء
ويفترض غسل ما في المخرج عند الاغتسال من الجنابة والحيض والنفاس وإن كان ما في المخرج قليلا وأن يستنجي بحجر منق ونحوه، والغسل بالماء أحب، والأفضل التنقية أي التنظيف المطلق الجمع بين الماء والحجر، فيمسح ثم يغسل ويجوز أن يقتصر على الماء أو الحجر، مع الترتيب فقط أي يصح والسنة إنقاء المحل، والعدد في الأحجار مندوب لا سنة مؤكدة، فيستنجي بثلاثة أحجار ندبا إن حصل التنظيف بما دونها. أي التطهير

ويفترض: لأن غسل سائر الجسد فرض في الغسل، فلو لم يغسل ما في المخرج قليلاً كان أو كثيراً، بقي ما عليه النجاسة من غير غسل، فلا الغسل. فإن قلت: هذا ينافي ما اشتهر في ما أن الاستنجاء بينهم من من سنن الغسل قلت المسنون هو تقديم الاستنجاء لا نفسه غسل أي إزالة ما في المخرج بغسله بالماء المطلق. [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح منق: بأن لا يكون خشناً كالآجر، ولا أملس كالعقيق [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٥] أحب: [أي من الحجر وحدة] لحصول الطهارة المتفق عليها، وإقامة السنة على الوجه الأكمل؛ لأن الحجر مقلل والمائع غير الماء مختلف في تطهيره. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٥] والأفضل : أطلقه فأفاد الأفضلية في كل زمان وقيل: الجمع إنما هو سنة في زماننا، أما في الزمان الأول فأدب؛ لأنهم كانوا يبعرون. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٥] يقتصر إلخ والاقتصار على الماء فقط أقرب في الفضل في استعمال الماء والحجر من الاقتصار على الحجر، فإنه دونهما، ولكن يحصل السنة وإن تفاوت الفضل.
إنقاء إلخ لأنه المقصود، فلو لم يحصل الإنقاء بثلاث يزاد عليها إجماعا؛ لكونه هو المقصود، ولو حصل الإنقاء بواحد واقتصر عليه جاز كما ذكر ومراقي الفلاح ،٤٦ ، حاشية الطحطاوي] لا سنة مؤكدة: لما ورد من التخيير؛ لقوله : "من استجمر فليوتر، من فعل فقد أحسن، ومن لا فلا حرج، فإنه لا يحتمل التأويل، فيدل على نفي وجوب الاستنجاء، وعلى نفي وجوب العدد فيه الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ٤٦] كانت: يفيد عموم الأزمنة صيفاً وشتاءً. يبتدئ: لكونه أبلغ في التنظيف.

وكيفية الاستنجاء أن. يمسح بالحجر الأول من جهة المقدم إلى خلف، وبالثاني من خلف للرجل بادياً القبل الوراء إلى قدام، وبالثالث من قدام إلى خلف إذا كانت الخصية ،مدلاة، وإن كانت غير مدلاة مرسلة يبتدئ من خلف إلى قدام والمرأة تبتدئ من قدام إلى خلف خشية تلويث فرجها، يصح تلطيخ بسكون الراء المهملة

ثم يغسل يده أولا بالماء، ثم يدلك المحل بالماء بباطن إصبع أو إصبعين أو ثلاث إلى الرسغين
The Book of Purity. Rulings on Istinja. It is obligatory to wash what is in the exit during the ritual bath from janabah, menstruation, and postnatal bleeding, even if what is in the exit is little. And he should perform istinja with a clean stone or similar. Washing with water is more beloved, and the best is combination, i.e., absolute cleansing, of water and stone: he wipes then washes. It is permissible to limit to water or stone only with order. And the sunnah is to purify the place, and the number of stones is recommended, not an emphasized sunnah. So he performs istinja with three stones as a recommendation if cleansing is achieved with fewer. That is purification. The obligation: because washing the rest of the body is fard in ghusl, so if he does not wash what is in the exit, little or much, the impurity remains without washing, so the ghusl is invalid. If you say: this contradicts what is famous that istinja is among the sunan of ghusl, I say: the sunnah is the preceding of istinja, not the istinja itself, i.e., removal of what is in the exit by washing with absolute water. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah: that it should not be rough like brick nor smooth like agate] [Maraqi al-Falah: 45] Beloved: i.e., more than stone alone, because it achieves agreed-upon purification and establishes the sunnah in the most complete manner; because stone is minimal and liquid other than water is disputed in its purifying effect. [Maraqi al-Falah: 45] The best: it is absolute, so it indicates preference in every time. It is said: combination is sunnah in our time, while in the first time it was etiquett; because they used to use dry dung. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 45] To limit etc.: Limiting to water alone is closer in virtue than limiting to stone, for it is inferior to both, but the sunnah is obtained even if virtue varies. Purification etc. because it is the objective, so if purification is not achieved with three, more are added by consensus because it is the objective. If purification is achieved with one and one confines to it, it is permissible as mentioned. [Maraqi al-Falah 46, Hashiyah al-Tahtawi] Not an emphasized sunnah: because of the reported choice; due to his saying: "Whoever uses stones, let him use an odd number. Whoever does so has done well, and whoever does not, there is no harm." This cannot be interpreted, so it indicates negation of obligation of istinja and negation of obligation of number in it. [Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah: 46] It was: indicates generality of times, summer and winter. He begins: because it is more thorough in cleansing. And the method of istinja: He wipes with the first stone from the front direction to the back, and with the second from the back for the man, starting from the front? Actually from back to front, and with the third from front to back if the testicles are hanging. If not hanging, he begins from back to front. The woman begins from front to back for fear of soiling her vulva. It is valid to soil with a silent ra. Then he washes his hand first with water, then rubs the place with water with the inside of one, two, or three fingers up to the wrists.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a combination of matn and hashiyah from Nur al-Idah. It opens with the obligation of washing the exit during ghusl from major impurities. The reasoning is that since the entire body must be washed, any remaining impurity invalidates the ghusl. This does not contradict the famous view that istinja is a sunnah of ghusl, because the sunnah is to perform it before ghusl, not the washing itself. The text then moves to istinja after using the toilet. It states that one should use a clean stone or absorbent material. Water is more beloved, and the best is to combine stone and water. The sunnah is to clean the area thoroughly, and using three stones is recommended (mandub) not an emphasized sunnah. The hadith 'whoever uses stones, let him use an odd number...there is no harm' proves that istinja is not obligatory and that odd numbers are recommended. The method: men wipe from front to back, then back to front, etc., depending on the position of the testicles. Women wipe from front to back to avoid soiling. Finally, the passage describes washing the hand and rubbing the area with fingers.

Key Terms
يفترض (yuftarad): It is fard (obligatory). The act is required and omission is sinful.
المخرج (al-makhraj): The exit, i.e., the private parts (front and rear) from which impurity exits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence of not washing the exit (makhraj) during ghusl for janabah?
A) The ghusl is valid but makruh
B) The ghusl is invalid because impurity remains
C) The ghusl is valid and no penalty
D) The ghusl is valid but one must repeat it

Key Takeaway
Washing the private parts during ghusl is fard; leaving them unwashed invalidates the ghusl regardless of prior istinja.

Taharah — Purification

The Sunnah of Istinja: Method and Rulings
Explains rulings on istinja: sunnah, method, and number of stones

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules of istinja: identify its status as sunnah muakkadah, state the recommended method using three stones or water, and explain why using an odd number is mandub (recommended) not wajib.

Core Idea
Istinja is sunnah muakkadah, using water is best, combination is optimal, and three stones are recommended not obligatory.

This lesson covers the rules of istinja (cleaning after using the toilet) as detailed in the passage. The text establishes that istinja is a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation. It explains the types of materials (clean stones or water), the recommended order, and the distinction between sunnah and mandub in the number of stones. The method of wiping for men and women is also provided.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling level of istinja
The passage states: 'والسنة إنقاء المحل' – the sunnah is to purify the place. Istinja itself is sunnah muakkadah, not fard. The hadith 'من استجمر فليوتر... لا حرج' proves non-obligation.
Sunnah muakkadah means highly recommended but not sinful to omit.
2
Determine the status of using stones and number
The text says: 'والعدد في الأحجار مندوب لا سنة مؤكدة' – the number of stones is mandub (recommended), not an emphasized sunnah. The proof is the hadith allowing choice.
Mandub is a lower level than sunnah muakkadah.
3
Learn the preferred methods: water vs. stone
The passage ranks methods: water alone is 'أحب' (more beloved) than stone alone; combination of water and stone is 'الأفضل' (best). The commentary explains reasons.
Water is preferred because it is agreed upon as purifying, while stone based purification can be disputed.
4
Study the method of wiping for men and women
The text provides specific directions: for a man with hanging testicles, wipe first from front to back, then back to front, then front to back. For a woman, always front to back.
The goal is thorough cleaning and avoiding soiling.

Source Text

كتاب الطهارة
أحكام الاستنجاء
ويفترض غسل ما في المخرج عند الاغتسال من الجنابة والحيض والنفاس وإن كان ما في المخرج قليلا وأن يستنجي بحجر منق ونحوه، والغسل بالماء أحب، والأفضل التنقية أي التنظيف المطلق الجمع بين الماء والحجر، فيمسح ثم يغسل ويجوز أن يقتصر على الماء أو الحجر، مع الترتيب فقط أي يصح والسنة إنقاء المحل، والعدد في الأحجار مندوب لا سنة مؤكدة، فيستنجي بثلاثة أحجار ندبا إن حصل التنظيف بما دونها. أي التطهير

ويفترض: لأن غسل سائر الجسد فرض في الغسل، فلو لم يغسل ما في المخرج قليلاً كان أو كثيراً، بقي ما عليه النجاسة من غير غسل، فلا الغسل. فإن قلت: هذا ينافي ما اشتهر في ما أن الاستنجاء بينهم من من سنن الغسل قلت المسنون هو تقديم الاستنجاء لا نفسه غسل أي إزالة ما في المخرج بغسله بالماء المطلق. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٥] يقتصر إلخ والاقتصار على الماء فقط أقرب في الفضل في استعمال الماء والحجر من الاقتصار على الحجر، فإنه دونهما، ولكن يحصل السنة وإن تفاوت الفضل.
إنقاء إلخ لأنه المقصود، فلو لم يحصل الإنقاء بثلاث يزاد عليها إجماعا؛ لكونه هو المقصود، ولو حصل الإنقاء بواحد واقتصر عليه جاز كما ذكر ومراقي الفلاح ،٤٦ ، حاشية الطحطاوي] لا سنة مؤكدة: لما ورد من التخيير؛ لقوله : "من استجمر فليوتر، من فعل فقد أحسن، ومن لا فلا حرج، فإنه لا يحتمل التأويل، فيدل على نفي وجوب الاستنجاء، وعلى نفي وجوب العدد فيه الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ٤٦] كانت: يفيد عموم الأزمنة صيفاً وشتاءً. يبتدئ: لكونه أبلغ في التنظيف.

Key Terms
مستنجى (mustanja): The place of istinja, i.e., the private parts after elimination.
منق (munqqan): A stone or object that is clean, absorbent, and not too rough or smooth, such as clay or brick.
مندوب (mandub): Recommended; an act whose performance is rewarded but leaving it is not sinful.

Method of Istinja: Fingers and Removing Smell
Rulings on the method of istinja

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on how many fingers to use for istinja, whether to raise the middle finger, and the obligation to remove foul smell.

Core Idea
Istinja requires three fingers maximum, no finger raising, and complete removal of smell.

This lesson covers the basic method of istinja according to the Hanafi school. It answers practical questions: how many fingers should I use? Should I raise one finger? What about the smell? These details ensure purification is valid and complete.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
We are discussing istinja (cleaning after defecation). The Hanafi school provides specific guidelines for its performance.
Istinja is sunnah muakkadah, not fard.
2
Determine the number of fingers
The text states that if one needs three fingers, it is permissible, but one should not increase beyond three unnecessarily. This is because necessity is met by three, and soiling pure parts without need is not permissible.
Three fingers: index, middle, ring.
3
Resolve the confusion on raising the middle finger
Some scholars recommend raising the middle finger so that dirty water flows down without spreading. However, the majority of Hanafi scholars hold that one should not raise any finger but lift all fingers together.
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is to lift all fingers together.
4
Address removing foul smell
The text emphasizes that the foul smell must be removed from both the place and the finger used for istinja, because the smell is a trace of impurity. Purification is not complete with its presence unless removing it is difficult.
If difficult, it is excused; people are often heedless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في ما يجوز به الاستنجاء، وما يكره به، وما يكره فعله
لا يجوز
عن زيادة
إن احتاج [أي احتاج إلى ثلاث أصابع في الاستنجاء. (مراقي الفلاح) وإن لم يحتج فلا تحرزاً . التلويث، ولا يزيد على الثلاث؛ لأن الضرورة تندفع بها، وتنجيس الطاهر بغير ضرورة لا يجوز كما في "المحيط". حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٧] ويصعد وذلك لينحدر الماء النجس من غير شيوع على جسده. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٧] وهي طريقة لبعض المشايخ والذي عليه عامتهم أنه لا يصعد بل يرفعها جملة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٧] إصبعه الوسطى هي من الأصابع من بين البنصر والسبابة بنصره: ما بين الوسطى والخنصر. يقطع الرائحة إلخ : أي عن المحل وعن إصبعه التي استنجى بها؛ لأن الرائحة أثر النجاسة، فلا طهارة مع بقائها إلا أن يشق، والناس عنه غافلون [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٨] ، و لم يقدر بعدد؛ لأن الصحيح تفويضه إلى الرأي حتى يطمئن القلب بالطهارة بيقين أو غلبة الظن، وقيل: يقدر في حق الموسوس بسبع أو ثلاث، وقيل: في الإحليل بثلاث، وفي المقعدة بخمس، وقيل: بتسع، وقيل: بعشر [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨] وفي إرخاء إلخ: إنما يبالغ في إرخاء المعقدة؛ ليزيل ما في الشرج بقدر الإمكان. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨] إن لم يكن إلخ وإن كان صائما لا يبالغ في إرخاء المقعدة؛ حفظاً للصوم عن الفساد. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨] ونشف الئلا تجذب مقعدته شيئا من الماء أي بخرقة أو بيده اليسرى مرة بعد أخرى إن لم تكن خرقة. حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ٤٨] لا يجوز: قال الكمال: إنما يستنجي بالماء إذا وجد مكاناً يستتر فيه، ولو كان على شط نهر ليس فيه سترة لو استنجى بالماء، قالوا يفسق وكثيراً ما يفعله عوام المصلين في الميضأة فضلاً. شاطئ النيل. (شلبي)
عن
Section on what is permissible for istinja, what is disliked, and what is prohibited to do. It is not permissible for increase. If needed [i.e., needed three fingers for istinja (Maraqi al-Falah)] and if not needed, then do not [unclear] soiling. And he should not increase beyond three, because necessity is met by them, and soiling a pure thing without necessity is not permissible as in al-Muhit. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 47] And he raises (the middle finger) so that the dirty water flows without spreading over his body. [Maraqi al-Falah: 47] This is the method of some teachers, but the majority hold that he does not raise but lifts them together. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 47] His middle finger: it is between the ring and index; his ring finger: between middle and little. He should remove the foul smell, i.e., from the place and from his finger with which he performed istinja, because smell is a trace of impurity; so there is no purification with its presence unless it is difficult, and people are heedless of this. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 48] And it is not quantified with a number, because the correct view is to refer it to opinion until the heart is satisfied with purification with certainty or dominant probability. It is said: for the obsessive, it is quantified with seven or three; for the urethra with three, for the anus with five, or nine, or ten. [Maraqi al-Falah: 48] And in relaxing the anus: he only emphasizes relaxing the anus to remove what is in the rectum as much as possible. [Maraqi al-Falah: 48] If he is not... if he is fasting, he does not emphasize relaxing the anus to preserve the fast from nullification. [Maraqi al-Falah: 48] And drying his anus so that his anus does not attract any water, i.e., with a cloth or with his left hand repeatedly if there is no cloth. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah: 48] It is not permissible: al-Kamal said: one only performs istinja with water if he finds a place to conceal himself; if he is on a riverbank without a screen and performs istinja with water, they said he commits sin, and many common worshipers do this in the wudu area, let alone the Nile bank. (Shalabi) About.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This section deals with the details of istinja: how many fingers to use, the issue of raising fingers, removing smell, and the recommended number of washes. It also discusses the ruling on performing istinja with water in public places. The text states that if one needs three fingers, he may use them, but should not exceed three unnecessarily. There is a difference of opinion on whether to raise the middle finger or not. The majority hold that one should not raise but lift all fingers together. Removing the foul smell is important because it indicates remaining impurity, but if difficult, it is excused. The number of washes is not fixed; it is left to one's certainty or dominant probability. For obsessive individuals, limits are set. The text also notes that a fasting person should not emphasize relaxing the anus to avoid nullifying the fast. Finally, it warns that performing istinja with water in an exposed area is sinful.

Key Terms
إرخاء المقعدة (irkha' al-maq'adah): Relaxing the anal sphincter to allow complete expulsion of feces.
موسوس (muwaswis): A person afflicted with obsessive doubts about purification, requiring a quantified limit for istinja.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, what is the Hanafi ruling on the number of fingers used for istinja?
A) Always use three fingers.
B) Use three fingers if needed, but do not exceed unnecessarily.
C) Use any number up to five.
D) Use only one finger.

Key Takeaway
Use up to three fingers, lift them together, and remove any foul smell to complete istinja.

Number of Istinja Washes and the Ruling for the Obsessive
Rulings on the number of istinja washes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule on the number of istinja washes and apply the exception for obsessive individuals.

Core Idea
Istinja washes are not fixed by number; they are left to certainty, except for the obsessive who is limited.

How many times should you wash after using the toilet? The Hanafi school does not prescribe a specific number, but rather requires that one be certain of purity. However, for those with obsessive doubts (muwaswis), limits are set to prevent hardship. This lesson examines these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Understand the default rule on number of washes
The text states that the number of washes is not fixed (لم يقدر بعدد). The correct view is to refer it to personal judgment until the heart is satisfied with purity by certainty or dominant probability.
This is based on the principle that purification is achieved by removal of impurity, not by a set count.
2
Identify the exception for the obsessive (muwaswis)
For a person prone to obsessive doubts (muwaswis), the number is quantified to prevent endless washing. Several opinions are cited: seven or three; for urethra: three; for anus: five, nine, or ten.
The common view is three or seven total washes.
3
Apply the rule to practical cases
A normal person washes until he is sure; an obsessive person stops at the prescribed number even if he still doubts.
This prevents hardship and waswasah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لا يجوز
عن زيادة
إن احتاج [أي احتاج إلى ثلاث أصابع في الاستنجاء. (مراقي الفلاح) وإن لم يحتج فلا تحرزاً . التلويث، ولا يزيد على الثلاث؛ لأن الضرورة تندفع بها، وتنجيس الطاهر بغير ضرورة لا يجوز كما في "المحيط". حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٧] ويصعد وذلك لينحدر الماء النجس من غير شيوع على جسده. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٧] وهي طريقة لبعض المشايخ والذي عليه عامتهم أنه لا يصعد بل يرفعها جملة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٧] إصبعه الوسطى هي من الأصابع من بين البنصر والسبابة بنصره: ما بين الوسطى والخنصر. يقطع الرائحة إلخ : أي عن المحل وعن إصبعه التي استنجى بها؛ لأن الرائحة أثر النجاسة، فلا طهارة مع بقائها إلا أن يشق، والناس عنه غافلون [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٨] ، و لم يقدر بعدد؛ لأن الصحيح تفويضه إلى الرأي حتى يطمئن القلب بالطهارة بيقين أو غلبة الظن، وقيل: يقدر في حق الموسوس بسبع أو ثلاث، وقيل: في الإحليل بثلاث، وفي المقعدة بخمس، وقيل: بتسع، وقيل: بعشر [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨] وفي إرخاء إلخ: إنما يبالغ في إرخاء المعقدة؛ ليزيل ما في الشرج بقدر الإمكان. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨] إن لم يكن إلخ وإن كان صائما لا يبالغ في إرخاء المقعدة؛ حفظاً للصوم عن الفساد. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨] ونشف الئلا تجذب مقعدته شيئا من الماء أي بخرقة أو بيده اليسرى مرة بعد أخرى إن لم تكن خرقة. حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ٤٨] لا يجوز: قال الكمال: إنما يستنجي بالماء إذا وجد مكاناً يستتر فيه، ولو كان على شط نهر ليس فيه سترة لو استنجى بالماء، قالوا يفسق وكثيراً ما يفعله عوام المصلين في الميضأة فضلاً. شاطئ النيل. (شلبي)
عن
Section on what is permissible for istinja, what is disliked, and what is prohibited to do. It is not permissible for increase. If needed [i.e., needed three fingers for istinja (Maraqi al-Falah)] and if not needed, then do not [unclear] soiling. And he should not increase beyond three, because necessity is met by them, and soiling a pure thing without necessity is not permissible as in al-Muhit. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 47] And he raises (the middle finger) so that the dirty water flows without spreading over his body. [Maraqi al-Falah: 47] This is the method of some teachers, but the majority hold that he does not raise but lifts them together. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 47] His middle finger: it is between the ring and index; his ring finger: between middle and little. He should remove the foul smell, i.e., from the place and from his finger with which he performed istinja, because smell is a trace of impurity; so there is no purification with its presence unless it is difficult, and people are heedless of this. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 48] And it is not quantified with a number, because the correct view is to refer it to opinion until the heart is satisfied with purification with certainty or dominant probability. It is said: for the obsessive, it is quantified with seven or three; for the urethra with three, for the anus with five, or nine, or ten. [Maraqi al-Falah: 48] And in relaxing the anus: he only emphasizes relaxing the anus to remove what is in the rectum as much as possible. [Maraqi al-Falah: 48] If he is not... if he is fasting, he does not emphasize relaxing the anus to preserve the fast from nullification. [Maraqi al-Falah: 48] And drying his anus so that his anus does not attract any water, i.e., with a cloth or with his left hand repeatedly if there is no cloth. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah: 48] It is not permissible: al-Kamal said: one only performs istinja with water if he finds a place to conceal himself; if he is on a riverbank without a screen and performs istinja with water, they said he commits sin, and many common worshipers do this in the wudu area, let alone the Nile bank. (Shalabi) About.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This section deals with the details of istinja: how many fingers to use, the issue of raising fingers, removing smell, and the recommended number of washes. It also discusses the ruling on performing istinja with water in public places. The text states that if one needs three fingers, he may use them, but should not exceed three unnecessarily. There is a difference of opinion on whether to raise the middle finger or not. The majority hold that one should not raise but lift all fingers together. Removing the foul smell is important because it indicates remaining impurity, but if difficult, it is excused. The number of washes is not fixed; it is left to one's certainty or dominant probability. For obsessive individuals, limits are set. The text also notes that a fasting person should not emphasize relaxing the anus to avoid nullifying the fast. Finally, it warns that performing istinja with water in an exposed area is sinful.

Key Terms
موسوس (muwaswis): A person afflicted with obsessive doubts about purification, requiring a quantified limit for istinja.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the number of istinja washes for a person who is not obsessive?
A) Must wash exactly three times.
B) Must wash until certain or highly probable of purity.
C) Must wash seven times.
D) Must wash once.

Key Takeaway
Normal persons wash until certain; obsessive persons wash a set number (three or seven) to avoid hardship.

Etiquettes of Istinja: Relaxing, Drying, and Public Places
Rulings on additional etiquettes of istinja

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the etiquettes of relaxing the anus, drying, and the ruling on performing istinja in public places.

Core Idea
Relax the anus during istinja (except when fasting), dry afterward, and never perform istinja with water in exposed areas.

Istinja has additional etiquettes that affect its validity and religious propriety. These include relaxing the anal sphincter to ensure complete cleaning, drying to prevent attracting moisture, and the important ruling that performing istinja with water in an exposed place is sinful. This lesson covers these practical rules.

Guided Path
1
Understand the recommendation to relax the anus
The text recommends relaxing the anal sphincter (irkha' al-maq'adah) to expel any remaining feces. However, if one is fasting, he should not over-relax to prevent water from entering the body, which could nullify the fast.
Relaxing is recommended but not obligatory.
2
Learn the practice of drying
After istinja with water, one should dry the area with a cloth or the left hand repeatedly to prevent the anus from attracting moisture, which could be considered impurity.
Drying is part of cleanliness.
3
Apply the ruling on public istinja
The text strongly warns against performing istinja with water in a place without cover, even on a riverbank. Doing so is considered sinful (fisq) because it involves exposing one's private parts and soiling the public area.
Many worshipers are heedless of this in wudu areas.

beginner
