Method of Istinja (Cleansing) – Recommended Acts
Procedural description of istinja with gender-specific sunan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the recommended method of istinja and identify the sunan acts for men and women.

Core Idea
Istinja follows a specific method: use water, left hand, middle finger first for men, ring and middle for women, and dry for a fasting person.

This part of the text details the physical manner of performing istinja after relieving oneself. It outlines the recommended steps, highlighting the differences between men and women and special considerations for a fasting person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the essential actions
Recognize that washing the hand first is a sunnah, then rubbing with fingers up to the wrists.
2
Distinguish by gender
Men start with the middle finger, then ring finger; women use ring and middle together from the beginning. The reason given is to avoid pleasure.
The text explicitly states the reason for the difference.
3
Include thoroughness
The command to remove the foul odor implies complete cleansing until the odor is eliminated.
4
Note the fasting exception
Relaxing the anus is allowed only if not fasting; a fasting person must dry the anus before standing to prevent backflow.
This shows the integration of fasting rules with tahara.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يغسل يده أولا بالماء، ثم يدلك المحل بالماء بباطن إصبع أو إصبعين أو ثلاث إلى الرسغين إن احتاج، ويصعد الرجل إصبعه الوسطى على غيرها في ابتداء الاستنجاء، ثم يصعد بنصره ولا يقتصر على إصبع واحدة والمرأة تصعد بنصرها وأوسط أصابعها معا ابتداء؛ خشية حصول اللذة، ويبالغ في التنظيف حتى يقطع الرائحة الكريهة، وفي إرخاء المقعدة إن لم يكن صائما، فإذا فرغ غسل يده ثانيا ونشف مقعدته قبل القيام إن كان صائما. فصل في ما يجوز به الاستنجاء، وما يكره به، وما يكره فعله ] لا يجوز كشف العورة للاستنجاء، وإن تجاوزت النجاسة مخرجها وزاد المتجاوز على قدر الدرهم لا تصح الصلاة إذا وجد ما يزيله ويحتال لإزالته من غير كشف من كشف العورة للاستنجاء: قال العلامة نوح: المستنجي لا يكشف عورته عند أحد للاستنجاء، فإن كشفها صار فاسقاً؛ لأن كشف العورة حرام، ومرتكب الحرام فاسق، سواء كان النجس مجاوزاً للمخرج أو لا، وسواء زاد على الدرهم أو لا، ومن فهم من عبارتهم غير هذا فقد سها. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٩] ومع وزاد إلخ المعتبر في منع الصلاة ما جاوز المخرج من النجاسة، حتى إذا كان المجاوز عن المخرج قدر الدرهم، الذي في المخرج يزيد عليه لا يمنع الصلاة ولا يجب غسله؛ لأن ما على المخرج ساقط العبرة، ولهذا لا يكره تركه ولا يضم إلى ما في جسده من النجاسة، فبقيت العبرة للمجاوز فقط، فإن كان أكثر من قدر الدرهم منع وإلا فلا وهذا عند أبي حنيفة له وأبي يوسف له، وعند محمد به: يعتبر مع موضع الاستنجاء، حتى إذا كان المجموع أكثر قدر الدرهم منع عنده ووجب غسله وكذا يضم ما في المخرج إلى ما في جسده من النجاسة عنده فحاصله : أن المخرج كالباطن عندهما لا يعتبر تبيين الحقائق: ۲۱۱/۱] من حتى ما فيه النجاسة أصلاً، من وعنده كالخارج. قدر الدرهم وزناً في المتجسدة، ومساحة في المائعة (مراقي الفلاح) وإذا لم يزد إلا بالضم لما في المخرج فلا يضر تركه؛ لأن ما في المخرج ساقط الاعتبار مراقي الفلاح: ٤٩] لا تصح إلخ: لأنه يجب الاستنجاء بالماء إذا جاوزت النجاسة المخرج؛ لأن ما على المخرج من النجاسة إنما اكتفي فيه بغير الماء للضرورة، ولا ضرورة في المتجاوز فيجب غسله، وكذا إذا لم يجاوز وكان جنباً يجب الاستنجاء بالماء؛ لوجوب غسل المقعدة لأجل الجنابة، وكذا الحائض والنفساء لما ذكرنا تبيين الحقائق: ۲۱۱/۱] مع إذا وجد إلخ : أي عدم صحة الصلاة مشروط بشرطين: الأول: وجود مزيل النجاسة المتجاوز على قدر الدرهم، والثاني: إمكان إزالته من غير كشف العورة عند أحد، أما الأول؛ فلأنه عند عدم وجود المزيل تصح صلاته النجس، ولا يعيد الصلاة التي صلاها مع النجس بعد ما وجد الماء؛ لعدم القدرة على المزيل، وأما الثاني؛ فلأن كشف العورة حرام يعذر به في ترك طهارة النجاسة، إذا لم يمكن إزالتها من غير كشف. ويحتال احتيال بالكسر : اختيار الحيلة من يراه أطلقه . وهو مقيد بمن يحرم عليه جماعه، ولو أمته المجوسية والتي زوجها للغير؛ لأنه لما حرم عليه وطؤهما حرم عليه نظره إلى عورتهما؛ وكذا نظرهما إليه؛ إذ متى حرم الوطء حرمت الدواعي، إلا ما استثني كامرأته الحائض والنفساء [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٩]
Then he washes his hand first with water, then he rubs the place with water using the inner side of one, two, or three fingers up to the wrists if needed. The man raises his middle finger over others at the beginning of istinja, then he raises his ring finger and does not suffice with one finger. The woman raises her ring finger and her middle finger together at the beginning, fearing attainment of pleasure. He exerts in cleaning until he removes the foul odor. And in relaxing the anus if he is not fasting. Then when he finishes, he washes his hand a second time and dries his anus before standing if he is fasting. A chapter on what is permissible for istinja, what is disliked, and what is disliked to do. It is not permissible to expose the private parts for istinja. And if the impurity exceeds the exit and the excess exceeds the measure of a dirham, the prayer is not valid if he finds what removes it and he can contrive to remove it without exposing. From exposing the private parts for istinja: The scholar Nuh said: The person doing istinja does not expose his private parts to anyone for istinja, for if he exposes them he becomes a sinner because exposing the private parts is forbidden, and the committer of a forbidden act is a sinner, whether the impurity is beyond the exit or not, and whether it exceeds a dirham or not. Whoever understands from their expression other than this has erred. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 49] And with 'and the excess' etc.: The consideration in preventing prayer is what exceeds the exit of impurity, so that if the excess beyond the exit is the measure of a dirham, what is in the exit increases it, it does not prevent prayer nor is washing it obligatory because what is on the exit is disregarded. Therefore not leaving it is not disliked and it is not added to what is on his body from impurity. So the consideration remains only for the excess. If it is more than the measure of a dirham, it prevents, otherwise no. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad: he considers it together with the place of istinja, so if the total is more than the measure of a dirham, it prevents according to him and washing it becomes obligatory. Similarly, he adds what is in the exit to what is on his body from impurity. The upshot is that the exit is like the interior according to them two, not considered. [Tibyan al-Haqa'iq: 1/211] According to him it is like the exterior. The measure of a dirham is by weight for solid impurity and by area for liquid impurity (Maraqi al-Falah). And if it does not increase except by adding what is in the exit, then leaving it does not harm because what is in the exit is disregarded. [Maraqi al-Falah: 49] 'Is not valid' etc.: Because istinja with water is obligatory if the impurity exceeds the exit, since the impurity on the exit is only sufficed with other than water due to necessity, and there is no necessity for the excess, so washing it is obligatory. Similarly, if it does not exceed and he is in a state of janaba, istinja with water is obligatory due to the obligation of washing the anus for janaba, and similarly for the menstruating woman and the woman with postpartum bleeding for what we mentioned. [Tibyan al-Haqa'iq: 1/211] With 'if he finds' etc.: That is, the invalidity of prayer is conditioned by two conditions: first, the existence of a remover of the impurity exceeding the measure of a dirham; second, the possibility of removing it without exposing the private parts to anyone. As for the first, because in the absence of a remover his prayer with impurity is valid, and he does not repeat the prayer he prayed with impurity after finding water due to inability to remove. As for the second, because exposing the private parts is forbidden, and he is excused in leaving the purification of impurity if it cannot be removed without exposure. 'And he contrives' i.e., choosing the means. 'From one who sees him' is absolute, and it is restricted to one whom it is forbidden to have intercourse with, even his Magian slave woman and the one whose husband is other, because when intercourse with them is forbidden, looking at their private parts is forbidden, and similarly their looking at him, since when intercourse is forbidden, its incitements are forbidden, except what is exempted like his menstruating wife and the one with postpartum bleeding. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 49]
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage combines two major sections from Nur al-Idah: the method of istinja and the rulings on what is allowed and what invalidates prayer. The text first details the recommended way to perform istinja with water, including the number of fingers, the order for men and women, and the importance of thorough cleaning and drying, especially for a fasting person. It then transitions to a chapter on the permissibility of istinja materials and explicitly states that exposing the private parts (awrah) for istinja is not permissible, regardless of the amount of impurity. The commentary, drawn from Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, and Tibyan al-Haqa'iq, expands the ruling: exposing awrah is a sin (fisq) and invalidates prayer if it can be avoided. The passage also addresses the critical legal issue of how much impurity beyond the exit affects prayer validity. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, only the impurity that has left the exit is considered; the impurity still inside the exit is disregarded. If the external impurity is less than a dirham (about 60 grams in weight or the area of a dirham coin), prayer is valid; if more, prayer is invalid unless the person cannot remove it without exposing awrah. Imam Muhammad holds a stricter view, totaling the internal and external impurity. The measure is applied by weight for solid impurity and by area for liquid impurity. The conditions for prayer invalidity are: (1) the impurity exceeds a dirham, (2) there is a means to remove it, and (3) it can be removed without exposing awrah. If any condition fails, the prayer is valid. The passage concludes with the ruling that contrivance (hila) to avoid exposure is required only when the onlooker is someone whom the person cannot legally marry (mahram or spouse), not for strangers.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinja): Cleansing of the private parts after urination or defecation using water, stones, or other clean absorbent materials.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Index finger
B) Middle finger
C) Ring finger
D) Little finger

Key Takeaway
The recommended istinja method includes specific finger usage for men and women and drying for the fasting person.

Rulings on Exposing 'Awra and the Dirham Measure for Impurity
Exposition of rulings on awrah exposure and impurity threshold for prayer validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why exposing the private parts for istinja is forbidden, and determine when a person's prayer is invalid due to impurity based on the dirham measure and the ability to remove it without exposure.

Core Idea
Exposing the private parts for istinja is sinful regardless of impurity amount; prayer is invalid only if excess impurity exceeds a dirham and can be removed without exposure.

This part of the passage deals with the legal rulings concerning istinja: the prohibition of exposing the private parts, and the conditions under which excess impurity invalidates prayer. It also clarifies the internal debate among Hanafi imams about counting impurity inside the exit.

Guided Path
1
State the rule on exposure
Identify that exposing the private parts for istinja is not permissible; it is haram and makes one a fasiq.
The text quotes scholar Nuh to emphasize this.
2
Identify the dirham measure
Note that only impurity that has exited the body is considered; internal impurity is disregarded.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
3
Apply the conditions for prayer invalidity
Prayer is invalid only if: (a) external impurity exceeds a dirham, (b) there is a means to remove it, and (c) removal is possible without exposing awrah.
If any condition fails, prayer is valid with impurity.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Understand that Imam Muhammad counts internal impurity, but the relied-upon position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) does not.
The mufta bihi is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Then he washes his hand first with water, then he rubs the place with water using the inner side of one, two, or three fingers up to the wrists if needed. The man raises his middle finger over others at the beginning of istinja, then he raises his ring finger and does not suffice with one finger. The woman raises her ring finger and her middle finger together at the beginning, fearing attainment of pleasure. He exerts in cleaning until he removes the foul odor. Whoever understands from their expression other than this has erred. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 49] And with 'and the excess' etc.: The consideration in preventing prayer is what exceeds the exit of impurity, so that if the excess beyond the exit is the measure of a dirham, what is in the exit increases it, it does not prevent prayer nor is washing it obligatory because what is on the exit is disregarded. Similarly, he adds what is in the exit to what is on his body from impurity. The upshot is that the exit is like the interior according to them two, not considered. [Tibyan al-Haqa'iq: 1/211] With 'if he finds' etc.: That is, the invalidity of prayer is conditioned by two conditions: first, the existence of a remover of the impurity exceeding the measure of a dirham; second, the possibility of removing it without exposing the private parts to anyone. As for the first, because in the absence of a remover his prayer with impurity is valid, and he does not repeat the prayer he prayed with impurity after finding water due to inability to remove. As for the second, because exposing the private parts is forbidden, and he is excused in leaving the purification of impurity if it cannot be removed without exposure. 'And he contrives' i.e., choosing the means. 'From one who sees him' is absolute, and it is restricted to one whom it is forbidden to have intercourse with, even his Magian slave woman and the one whose husband is other, because when intercourse with them is forbidden, looking at their private parts is forbidden, and similarly their looking at him, since when intercourse is forbidden, its incitements are forbidden, except what is exempted like his menstruating wife and the one with postpartum bleeding. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 49]

Commentary
This passage combines two major sections from Nur al-Idah: the method of istinja and the rulings on what is allowed and what invalidates prayer. The text first details the recommended way to perform istinja with water, including the number of fingers, the order for men and women, and the importance of thorough cleaning and drying, especially for a fasting person. It then transitions to a chapter on the permissibility of istinja materials and explicitly states that exposing the private parts (awrah) for istinja is not permissible, regardless of the amount of impurity. The commentary, drawn from Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, and Tibyan al-Haqa'iq, expands the ruling: exposing awrah is a sin (fisq) and invalidates prayer if it can be avoided. The passage also addresses the critical legal issue of how much impurity beyond the exit affects prayer validity. If the external impurity is less than a dirham (about 60 grams in weight or the area of a dirham coin), prayer is valid; if more, prayer is invalid unless the person cannot remove it without exposing awrah. If any condition fails, the prayer is valid. The passage concludes with the ruling that contrivance (hila) to avoid exposure is required only when the onlooker is someone whom the person cannot legally marry (mahram or spouse), not for strangers.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinja): Cleansing of the private parts after urination or defecation using water, stones, or other clean absorbent materials.
درهم (dirham): A silver coin used as a measure; approximately the size of a circular coin or 60 grams in weight for solid impurity, or area for liquid impurity.
كشف العورة (kashf al-awrah): Uncovering the private parts, which is generally forbidden except for necessity like medical treatment or under specific circumstances like with spouse.

The Prohibition of Uncovering ‘Awrah for Istinja’ and the Dirham Threshold
Explains prohibition of kashf al-'awrah and dirham condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on uncovering the ‘awrah during istinja’ and identify the condition under which impurity beyond a dirham invalidates prayer.

Core Idea
Uncovering the ‘awrah for istinja’ is haram and makes one a fasiq; impurity only invalidates prayer if removal is possible without kashf.

This lesson from Nur al-Idah deals with a key conflict in purification: the obligation to remove impurity (wajib) versus the obligation to cover the ‘awrah (wajib). The Hanafi position prioritizes covering, making it impermissible to uncover even for istinja’. The passage also clarifies that impurity exceeding a dirham invalidates prayer only when it can be removed without uncovering the ‘awrah in front of others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts and their rulings
The act of kashf al-‘awrah (uncovering the private parts) is ruled haram. The act of praying with impurity beyond dirham is ruled batil if removal is possible without kashf. Identify these as separate rulings.
The hashya adds that kashf makes one a fasiq regardless of impurity amount.
2
Locate the condition linking impurity to prayer invalidity
The text states: '...if the impurity exceeds the exit and the excess is the size of a dirham, the prayer is invalid if one finds something to remove it and can contrive to remove it without uncovering the private parts in front of someone who sees him.' Break down the condition: impurity > dirham, and ability to remove without kashf.
The condition of being seen is crucial: if alone, removal without kashf is possible; if in public, it may be impossible.
3
Apply the hashya clarification
The commentator Nooh emphasizes that kashf is always haram, and that the rule about impurity does not affect its prohibition. Understand that even if impurity is massive, one must not uncover the ‘awrah.
This overrides any potential misconception that impurity amount could justify kashf.
4
Note the disliked materials for istinja’
The passage lists bone, food, brick, and dung as makruh for istinja’. This is a secondary ruling; the main focus is the kashf prohibition.
These materials are either disrespectful (food) or ineffective (bone, brick, dung).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة ما يجوز به الاستنجاء كشف العورة للاستنجاء، وإن تجاوزت النجاسة مخرجها وزاد المتجاوز على قدر الدرهم لا تصح الصلاة إذا وجد ما يزيله ويحتال لإزالته من غير كشف العورة عند من يراه ويكره الاستنجاء بعظم وطعام لآدمي أو بهيمة، وآجر، والروث أيضا قال العلامة نوح: المستنجي لا يكشف عورته عند أحد للاستنجاء، فإن كشفها صار فاسقاً؛ لأن كشف العورة حرام، ومرتكب الحرام فاسق، سواء كان النجس مجاوزاً للمخرج أو لا، وسواء زاد على الدرهم أو لا، ومن فهم من عبارتهم غير هذا فقد سها.
Book of Purification: What is permissible for cleansing. Uncovering the private parts for cleansing, and if the impurity exceeds the exit and the excess is the size of a dirham, the prayer is invalid if one finds something to remove it and can contrive to remove it without uncovering the private parts in front of someone who sees him. And it is disliked to cleanse with bone, food for human or animal, brick, and dung. The scholar Nooh said: The one performing cleansing should not uncover his private parts in front of anyone for cleansing; if he uncovers them, he becomes a transgressor, because uncovering the private parts is prohibited, and one who commits a prohibited act is a transgressor, whether the impurity is beyond the exit or not, and whether it exceeds a dirham or not. Whoever understands from their expression other than this has erred.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah outlines two crucial rules for istinja'. First, it is impermissible to deliberately uncover one's 'awrah for istinja', even if it means the impurity remains. The commentator, 'Allamah Nooh, strongly emphasizes that doing so makes one a fasiq because kashf al-'awrah is haram. This ruling applies regardless of the amount of impurity. Second, the presence of impurity exceeding a dirham on the body or clothing outside the exit invalidates prayer only if there is a means to remove it and one can do so without uncovering the 'awrah in front of someone. The text also lists materials disliked for istinja' (bone, food, brick, dung) due to disrespect or ineffectiveness.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinjā’): Cleansing the private parts after relieving oneself
العورة (al-‘awrah): The private parts that must be covered; for males from navel to knee, for females entire body except face, hands, and feet in prayer.
الدرهم (al-dirham): A silver coin used as measure; threshold for excusable impurity.

Key Takeaway

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Inner vs Outer Impurity
Resolves disagreement among Hanafi imams on counting inner impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding counting inner impurity and apply the majority view to determine prayer validity.

Core Idea
The inner impurity at the exit is disregarded; only external impurity counts for the dirham threshold.

This lesson examines a subtle but practically important disagreement within the Hanafi school: should the impurity that remains inside the anus or urethra be added to external impurity when determining whether prayer is prevented? The three senior imams differ, and the answer affects when washing becomes obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Heirs
First, understand the parties: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that internal impurity is disregarded (like the inside of the body). Imam Muhammad holds it is considered like external impurity.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Trace the Ruling Difference
If external impurity is less than a dirham but internal impurity brings the total over a dirham, the two imams say prayer is valid; Muhammad says it is invalid and washing becomes wajib.
The practical difference is clear: one dirham threshold.
3
Apply the Measurement Rule
The passage specifies: solid impurities measured by weight, liquid by area. Understand that the dirham is a standard unit.
This applies to both external and internal impurity amounts.
4
Identify the Reason (Ta'lil)
Why is internal impurity disregarded? Because the exit is like the inside (batin). The necessity for using water does not apply to internal impurity; only external excess requires water.
The basis is ta'lil (reasoning) based on necessity and the nature of the exit.
5
Note the Special Case of Janabah
Even if impurity does not exceed the exit, a junub (or menstruating woman) must wash with water because washing the private parts is obligatory due to janabah.
This is an exception: the ruling changes due to the state of major impurity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعتبر في منع الصلاة ما جاوز المخرج من النجاسة، حتى إذا كان المجاوز عن المخرج قدر الدرهم، الذي في المخرج يزيد عليه لا يمنع الصلاة ولا يجب غسله؛ لأن ما على المخرج ساقط العبرة، ولهذا لا يكره تركه ولا يضم إلى ما في جسده من النجاسة، فبقيت العبرة للمجاوز فقط، فإن كان أكثر من قدر الدرهم منع وإلا فلا وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وعند محمد: يعتبر مع موضع الاستنجاء، حتى إذا كان المجموع أكثر قدر الدرهم منع عنده ووجب غسله وكذا يضم ما في المخرج إلى ما في جسده من النجاسة عنده فحاصله: أن المخرج كالباطن عندهما لا يعتبر أصلاً، وعنده كالخارج. قدر الدرهم وزناً في المتجسدة، ومساحة في المائعة. وإذا لم يزد إلا بالضم لما في المخرج فلا يضر تركه؛ لأن ما في المخرج ساقط الاعتبار. لأنه يجب الاستنجاء بالماء إذا جاوزت النجاسة المخرج؛ لأن ما على المخرج من النجاسة إنما اكتفي فيه بغير الماء للضرورة، ولا ضرورة في المتجاوز فيجب غسله، وكذا إذا لم يجاوز وكان جنباً يجب الاستنجاء بالماء؛ لوجوب غسل المقعدة لأجل الجنابة، وكذا الحائض والنفساء.
The consideration in preventing prayer is the impurity that goes beyond the exit. If the excess beyond the exit is a dirham, and the impurity inside the exit adds to it, it does not prevent prayer nor must it be washed, because what is at the exit is disregarded. Hence leaving it is not disliked, nor is it added to the impurity on his body, so the consideration is only for the excess. If it is more than a dirham, it prevents; otherwise not. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, it is considered together with the place of cleansing, so if the total is more than a dirham, it prevents and must be washed. Likewise, he adds the impurity at the exit to the impurity on his body. So the result: The exit is like the inside according to them and is not considered at all; according to him, it is like the outside. The dirham is measured by weight for solid impurities and by area for liquid impurities. And if the excess does not exceed except by adding what is at the exit, then leaving it does not harm, because what is at the exit is disregarded. Because it is obligatory to perform istinja' with water if the impurity exceeds the exit; because what is at the exit is only excused with something other than water due to necessity, but there is no necessity for the excess, so it must be washed. Likewise, if it does not exceed and one is in a state of janabah, it is obligatory to perform istinja' with water because washing the private parts is obligatory due to janabah. Similarly, for a menstruating woman and a woman in postpartum bleeding.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between the three leading imams. The issue is whether impurity inside the exit (internal) should be added to external impurity to determine if the total exceeds the excusable dirham. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider the inside like the interior of the body (batin) — it is disregarded entirely; only external impurity counts. Thus, if external impurity is less than a dirham, prayer is valid even if internal impurity brings the total over. Imam Muhammad considers the exit like the exterior (kharij), so both internal and external are combined; if the total exceeds a dirham, prayer is prevented and washing is required. The passage then clarifies the dirham measurement (weight for solid, area for liquid) and adds that if impurity exceeds the exit, water must be used for istinja', and a person in major ritual impurity (junub) must use water even if impurity does not exceed.

Key Terms
المخرج (al-makhraj): The exit of waste; the anus or urethra
المجاوز (al-mujāwiz): The impurity that has spread beyond the external exit
قدر الدرهم (qadr al-dirham): The size/weight of a dirham coin, used as a threshold for impurity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if external impurity is half a dirham and internal impurity is half, the prayer is:
A) Invalid
B) Valid
C) Valid only if washed
D) Invalid unless water is used

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school disregards internal impurity at the exit; only external impurity exceeding a dirham prevents prayer and requires washing.

Two Conditions for Prayer Invalidation Due to Impurity
Identifies two conditions for prayer to be invalid due to impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions that must both be present for a prayer to be invalid due to impurity, and apply them to scenarios.

Core Idea
Prayer with impurity is valid unless both a remover is available and removal doesn't expose the 'awrah.

This lesson clarifies a nuanced ruling: not every prayer performed with impurity beyond the excusable limit is invalid. The author of Nur al-Idah specifies two conditions that must both exist for the prayer to be batil. Understanding these conditions balances the obligation to purify with the prohibition of exposing the 'awrah, and the limitation of being without a remover.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The default ruling is that prayer with impurity exceeding a dirham is sahih (valid) unless stated otherwise. Recognise that the passage sets conditions for invalidity, not validity.
2
State the first condition
The existence of a remover (muzil) of the impurity. If no remover is available, the prayer remains valid and need not be repeated later.
Remover includes water or solid that can remove impurity.
3
State the second condition
The possibility of removing the impurity without uncovering the 'awrah in front of someone. If removal would require kashf al-'awrah, the person is excused and prayer is valid.
Uncovering the 'awrah is haram, so it takes precedence over removing impurity.
4
Combine conditions for invalidity
Only when both conditions are present does the prayer become invalid (batil). If either is absent, the prayer is sahih.
Consequence: if both conditions exist, the prayer must be repeated with purification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عدم صحة الصلاة مشروط بشرطين: الأول: وجود مزيل النجاسة المتجاوز على قدر الدرهم، والثاني: إمكان إزالته من غير كشف العورة عند أحد، أما الأول؛ فلأنه عند عدم وجود المزيل تصح صلاته مع النجس، ولا يعيد الصلاة التي صلاها مع النجس بعد ما وجد الماء؛ لعدم القدرة على المزيل، وأما الثاني؛ فلأن كشف العورة حرام يعذر به في ترك طهارة النجاسة، إذا لم يمكن إزالتها من غير كشف.
The invalidity of prayer is conditional upon two conditions: Firstly, the existence of a remover of the impurity that exceeds a dirham. Secondly, the possibility of removing it without uncovering the private parts in the presence of someone who sees him. As for the first: because if there is no remover, his prayer with impurity is valid, and he does not repeat the prayer he performed with impurity after he finds water, due to the inability to remove it. As for the second: because uncovering the private parts is forbidden, so he is excused in leaving the purification of the impurity if it cannot be removed without uncovering.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage clarifies that the invalidity of prayer due to impurity beyond the excusable amount is not absolute. Two conditions must both be met: (1) the person must have access to a remover (water or solid); if he lacks any, his prayer is valid even with impurity, and he does not need to repeat it later when he finds water. (2) Removal must be possible without uncovering the 'awrah in front of someone; since kashf al-'awrah is haram, if removal would require it, he is excused and his prayer is valid. This balances the command to purify with the prohibition of uncovering private parts.

Key Terms
مزيل (muzīl): A substance that removes impurity, such as water or a solid remover
كشف العورة (kashf al-'awrah): Uncovering the private parts, which is haram in front of others

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is a person excused from removing impurity that exceeds a dirham?
A) When he does not have water
B) When removal would require uncovering his 'awrah
C) Both A and B
D) When the impurity is from urine

Key Takeaway
Prayer with impurity is only invalid if both a remover is available and removal is possible without exposing the 'awrah.

Using a Trick to Avoid Uncovering 'Awrah
Talil of hila restriction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain when a hila (legal stratagem) is required to avoid kashf al-'awrah and identify the legal reasoning (talil) that links the prohibition of intercourse to the prohibition of looking.

Core Idea
A stratagem to avoid uncovering is only required when the onlooker is one with whom intercourse is forbidden.

The passage addresses a practical concern: after relieving oneself, if someone is watching, should one devise a trick to avoid exposing the private parts? The answer depends on who the onlooker is. The ruling ties the permissibility of uncovering to the prohibition of sexual intercourse, using a talil (legal cause) that extends the prohibition to its means.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on using a hila
The passage states that one may use a trick (hila) to avoid uncovering the 'awrah. This ruling is mubah (permissible) in itself, but becomes recommended or even necessary when it is the only way to avoid a haram act.
2
Recognize the restriction on the onlooker
The hila is not required for any onlooker; it is specifically for a person whose sexual intercourse with you is prohibited (non-mahram). This includes even a Magian slave-girl or a woman married to someone else.
The phrase 'from one who sees him' is interpreted absolutely, but then restricted by this condition.
3
Understand the legal cause (talil)
The reasoning is: whenever intercourse is prohibited, looking at the 'awrah is also prohibited as a means. This is based on the legal principle that the prohibition of an act includes prohibition of its means (sadd al-dhara'i').
4
Note the exception
An exception is made for one's wife during menstruation or postpartum bleeding. Although intercourse is temporarily prohibited, looking is allowed. So no hila is needed when the onlooker is one's own wife in this state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويحتال احتيال بالكسر: اختيار الحيلة من يراه أطلقه. وهو مقيد بمن يحرم عليه جماعه، ولو أمته المجوسية والتي زوجها للغير؛ لأنه لما حرم عليه وطؤهما حرم عليه نظره إلى عورتهما؛ وكذا نظرهما إليه؛ إذ متى حرم الوطء حرمت الدواعي، إلا ما استثني كامرأته الحائض والنفساء.
And he may use a trick (hila) - 'hila' with a kasra: choosing the trick. The phrase 'from one who sees him' is used absolutely. And it is restricted to someone whose intercourse with him is prohibited, even his Magian slave-girl and the one whose marriage is to another; because when intercourse is prohibited for him, looking at their private parts is also prohibited, and similarly their looking at his private parts; because whenever intercourse is prohibited, the means to it are also prohibited, except what is excluded, like his menstruating or postpartum wife.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage explains the concept of hila (legal stratagem) in istinja'. The earlier ruling required avoiding kashf al-'awrah in front of 'anyone who sees him', but this is restricted to people with whom sexual intercourse is forbidden (non-mahram). The hila is to find a way to remove impurity without uncovering; this is required only if the onlooker is one to whom looking at the 'awrah is forbidden. The reasoning: when intercourse is prohibited, looking at private parts is also prohibited as a means. Exceptions include one's wife during menstruation or postpartum bleeding, where looking is allowed despite intercourse being temporarily prohibited.

Key Terms
الحيلة (al-ḥīlah): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible end while avoiding a prohibition

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, for whom should one use a trick to avoid uncovering the 'awrah?
A) For any person looking
B) For a person with whom intercourse is forbidden
C) For one's own wife in menstruation
D) For a child

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on hila ties the prohibition of looking at 'awrah to the prohibition of sexual intercourse, with a specific exception for a menstruating/postpartum wife.

Permissible Materials and Adab for Entering and Exiting the Toilet
Lists allowed cleaning materials and bathroom etiquettes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the permissible materials for istinja', state the ruling on using the right hand, and describe the sunnah actions for entering and exiting the toilet.

Core Idea
Istinja' requires specific materials and prescribed manners to maintain purity and reverence.

In this passage, Imam al-Quduri outlines the permissible materials that can be used for istinja'—such as pottery, charcoal, glass—and the etiquette for entering and exiting the toilet. These rulings ensure that even in a routine act, the believer maintains modesty and follows the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the permissible materials
The passage lists pottery, charcoal, glass, gypsum, and any clean, non-respectable object like a piece of cloth. Note that valuable items (e.g., silk brocade) are avoided.
2
Ruling on using the right hand
It is recommended to use the right hand for cleaning unless there is an excuse like paralysis; otherwise, the left hand is used.
3
Entering the toilet
Enter with the left foot, recite the isti'adha (seeking refuge) before entering if the place is prepared, sit leaning on the left leg, and do not speak unless necessary.
The du'a is said before entering if the place is prepared; otherwise at the time of starting to uncover.
4
Exiting the toilet
Exit with the right foot, then say the prescribed du'a thanking Allah for removing harm and granting well-being.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخزف، وفحم وزجاج وجص، وشيء محترم كخرقة ديباج وقطن، وباليد اليمنى إلا من عذر، ويدخل الخلاء برجله اليسرى، ويستعيذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم قبل دخوله ويجلس معتمدا على يساره ولا يتكلم إلا لضرورة، ويكره تحريما استقبال القبلة واستدبارها ولو في البنيان، واستقبال عين الشمس والقمر ومهب الريح، ويكره أن يبول أو يتغوط في الماء، والظل، والجحر، والطريق، وتحت شجرة مثمرة، والبول قائما إلا من عذر ويخرج من الخلاء برجله اليمنى، ثم يقول: الحمد لله الذي أذهب عني الأذى وعافاني. إلا من عذر أي لا يستنجي إلا بعذر في اليسار كالشلل وغيره، ولو استنجى بهذه الأشياء جاز. الخلاء ممدوداً، والمراد به بيت التغوط. قبل دخوله: أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا كان المكان معداً لذلك، وإن كان غير معدّ له كالصحراء فيستعيذ عند أوان الشروع كتشمير الثياب مثلاً قبل كشف العورة، وإن نسي ذلك أتى به في نفسه لا بلسانه. ويجلس لأنه أسهل لخروج الخارج، ويوسع فيما بين رجليه. ويكره: ويستثنى من المنع ما لو كانت الريح تهب عن يمين القبلة أو شمالها، فإن الاستقبال والاستدبار لا يكرهان للضرورة، وإذا اضطر إلى أحدهما ينبغي أن يختار الاستدبار؛ لأن الاستقبال أقبح، فتركه أدل على التعظيم. عين قيد بالعين إشارةً إلى أنه لو كان في مكان مستو، ولم تكن عينهما مرأى منه لا يكره بخلاف القبلة، وذكره الاستقبال يفيد أنه لا يكره استدبارهما. والظل أي يكره أن يبول أو يتغوط في الظل، أراد به الظل الذي يجلس فيه الناس والكراهة مقيدة بما إذا كان موضع الظل مباحاً، وأما إذا كان مملوكاً فيحرم فيه قضاء الحاجة بغير إذن مالكه، وإنما أردنا بالظل: الظل الذي يجلس فيه الناس؛ لأنه لا كراهة فيما لا حاجة إليه والجحر بضم الجيم وإسكان الحاء: الخرق في الأرض والجدار. والطريق وأفاد بإطلاقه أن البول في الطريق مكروه مطلقاً، ولو كان في ناحية منها. الأذى: أي بخروج الفضلات الممرضة بحبسها. وعافاني: أي بإبقاء خاصية الغذاء الذي لو أمسك كله أو خرج لكان مظنة الهلاك.
And [it is permissible to use] pottery, charcoal, glass, gypsum, and a respectable thing like a piece of silk brocade or cotton, and [to use] the right hand except for an excuse. And one enters the toilet with the left foot, and seeks refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan before entering, and sits leaning on the left leg, and does not speak except out of necessity. And it is prohibitively disliked to face or turn the back to the qiblah, even in a building, and to face the sun or moon directly, and [to face] the direction of the wind. And it is disliked to urinate or defecate in water, in the shade, in a hole, on a road, under a fruit-bearing tree, and to urinate standing except for an excuse. And one exits the toilet with the right foot, then says: 'Praise be to Allah who removed from me harm and granted me well-being.' 'Except for an excuse' means one does not use the left hand except if there is an excuse like paralysis, etc. And if one performs cleansing with these things, it is permitted. 'Al-khala' (toilet) is with a long vowel, meaning the house of defecation. 'Before entering' is unrestricted but it is restricted to when the place is prepared for that; if it is not prepared, like the desert, one seeks refuge at the time of beginning, like gathering one's clothes before uncovering the private parts; and if one forgets, he says it in his heart not with his tongue. 'And sits' because it is easier for the excretion to come out, and he spreads his legs apart. 'And it is disliked': there is an exception when the wind is blowing from the right or left of the qiblah; then facing or turning the back is not disliked out of necessity; and if forced to choose one, he should choose turning the back because facing is worse, leaving it is more indicative of reverence. 'The sun and moon' is qualified by 'eyeing' (seeing directly); if one is on level ground and the sun or moon is not in sight, it is not disliked, unlike the qiblah. The mention of facing implies that turning the back to the sun or moon is not disliked. 'The shade' means one should not urinate or defecate in the shade that people sit in, and the dislike is conditioned on the shade being in a permissible place; if it is owned, it is forbidden without the owner's permission. We mean by shade: the shade that people sit in; there is no dislike where there is no need. 'Al-juhur' (hole) is with a damma on the jim and sukun on the ha: a hole in the ground or wall. 'The road' indicates that urinating on the road is disliked absolutely, even on its side. 'Al-adha' (harm) means the excretion of harmful waste that was retained. 'Wa 'afani' (and granted me well-being) means preserving the property of food which if entirely retained or expelled would cause destruction.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This lengthy passage is a comprehensive list of rulings related to istinja' and bathroom etiquette. It covers: (1) materials permissible for istinja'—pottery, charcoal, glass, gypsum, and any clean, absorbent, non-respectable object; using the right hand is recommended unless excused. (2) Adab—entering with left foot, reciting du'a, sitting leaning on left, not speaking unless necessary, exiting with right foot and saying a du'a. (3) Prohibited/disliked actions—facing or turning back to qiblah (makruh tahrimi even in a building), facing sun/moon directly, facing wind, urinating/defecating in water, shade, holes, roads, under fruit trees, and standing urination without excuse. The commentary provides exceptions: for qiblah, if wind forces, no dislike; for sun/moon, only if directly seen; for shade, only if it is a public sitting place; for roads, disliked absolutely. The aim is to maintain purity, respect, and avoid disrespectful acts.

Key Terms
الخلاء (al-khalā’): The place designated for relieving oneself; toilet
يستعيذ (yasta'idhu): He seeks refuge (with Allah from Shaytan)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a permissible material for istinja'?
A) Silk brocade
B) Gypsum
C) A gold coin
D) A piece of bread

Key Takeaway
Using appropriate materials and following the prophetic adab transforms a mundane act into worship.

Prohibited Actions and Exceptions During Istinja'
Lists prohibited actions and exceptions in the toilet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the actions that are makruh tahrimi during istinja', explain the exceptions for necessity, and distinguish between facing the qiblah and facing the sun/moon.

Core Idea
Modesty and reverence for the qiblah and environment are paramount; avoid facing the qiblah, sun, moon, wind, and avoid impurity in certain places.

This section details the actions that are disliked (makruh tahrimi for qiblah, makruh for others) during relieving oneself. These include facing or turning the back to the qiblah, facing the sun or moon directly, standing to urinate without excuse, and soiling public places. The passage also provides exceptions for necessity.

Guided Path
1
List the prohibitions
Facing or turning back to the qiblah (makruh tahrimi), facing the sun or moon directly, facing the wind, urinating in water, in the shade, in a hole, on a road, under a fruit tree, standing urination without excuse.
Qiblah prohibition is stronger (tahrimi).
2
Understand the exceptions
For qiblah: if wind forces, no dislike. For sun/moon: only if directly seen. For shade: only if it's a public sitting area. For roads: absolutely disliked even on the side.
3
Apply the principle of reverence
The reasoning is to avoid disrespect: the qiblah is sacred; facing it while exposing private parts is extremely disrespectful. Similarly, facing the sun/moon is associated with other religions' practices.
4
Distinguish between types of dislike
The passage uses 'yukrahu tahriman' for qiblah (prohibitively disliked) and 'yukrahu' for others (disliked, likely tanzih). This affects sin and necessity of compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

يكره تحريما (yukrahu taḥrīman): Disliked with a prohibition-level dislike; closer to haram than to permissible
الظل (al-zill): Shade that people sit in

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Modesty in the toilet includes avoiding disrespect to sacred directions and public places; necessity can lift prohibitions but not without reason.

Rulings on Istinja: Permissible Materials and Use of Hands
Ruling on materials and hand use for istinja

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the permissible materials for istinja in the Hanafi school and state the ruling on using the right and left hand.

Core Idea
Istinja with solids is valid but water is superior; the right hand is preferred unless a valid excuse exists.

This passage from Nur al-Idah specifies which materials can be used for istinja (cleansing after relieving oneself) and the ruling on using the right hand. Understanding these rulings ensures one performs purification correctly according to the Hanafi school, balancing between what is permissible and what is recommended.

Guided Path
1
List the permissible materials
Identify each material mentioned: pottery shards, charcoal, glass, gypsum, and any revered substance like silk cloth and cotton. Note that these are solid, absorbent, and permissible.
The list is not exhaustive; the phrase 'كخرقة ديباج وقطن' indicates any similar revered cloth is allowed.
2
Understand the hand ruling
The default is to use the right hand for istinja. However, if there is an excuse (e.g., a problem with the right hand), the left hand is permissible. The commentary clarifies that using the left hand is allowed only with excuse, but if these materials are used, it is valid.
The commentary explains 'إلا من عذر' as referring to using the left hand.
3
Distinguish between materials and water
While these solids are permissible, washing with water is the superior and more complete method. This is a general Hanafi principle not explicitly in the passage but necessary for full understanding.
Water is afdal (superior) but not obligatory.
4
Apply the ruling to new scenarios
Consider other materials: a clean napkin is permissible under 'revered substance', but bone or food are impermissible because they are not listed and are considered unlclean or wasteful.
The ruling is based on the material being pure and absorbent.

Source Text

What is permissible for istinja: pottery shards, charcoal, glass, gypsum, and anything revered like a piece of silk cloth and cotton, and with the right hand except for an excuse. He enters the toilet with his left foot, seeks refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan before entering, sits leaning on his left, does not speak except out of necessity. It is prohibitively disliked to face or turn one's back to the qibla even in a building, and to face the sun, moon, and the direction of the wind. It is disliked to urinate or defecate in water, in shade, in a hole, on a road, under a fruit-bearing tree, and to urinate standing except for an excuse. (Pottery shards: fired clay) (Toilet: he seeks refuge) (Before uncovering his private parts because it is hated) (Facing them) (Defecate: meaning relieve oneself) (For its superiority after exiting) (Except for an excuse: meaning he does not use the left hand for istinja except due to an excuse like paralysis, etc., but if he uses these things it is permissible) (Eye of the sun and moon: meaning the actual disk, so if in a level place and he does not see them, it is not disliked) (Shade: meaning the shade where people sit, and the dislike is restricted to if it is public; if privately owned, it is forbidden without permission) (Hole: a cavity in the ground or wall) (Road: absolutely, even at the side) (Under a fruit-bearing tree: due to fear that it may fall back on him) (Urinating standing: except for an excuse due to spread of impurity, e.g., back pain) (Then upon exiting he says: Praise be to Allah who removed from me harm and granted me well-being. Harm: by the exit of waste whose retention causes illness; granted me well-being: by preserving the property of food which if retained entirely or exited would cause destruction).
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah presents the rulings (ahkam) pertaining to istinja (cleansing after using the toilet) and the etiquette (adab) of entering and exiting the toilet. It is a ruling statement with accompanying commentary from Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi. The passage first lists the permissible materials for istinja: pottery shards, charcoal, glass, gypsum, and any revered substance like silk cloth or cotton. The use of the right hand is preferred, but if there is an excuse (e.g., left hand paralyzed), using the left hand is allowed. The commentary clarifies that 'except for an excuse' applies to using the left hand, and that using these materials is valid. The adab include: entering with the left foot, seeking refuge in Allah from Shaytan before entering, sitting leaning on the left leg, and not speaking except for necessity. After exiting, one should step out with the right foot and recite the prescribed supplication. The passage then lists several makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) acts: facing or turning one's back to the qibla, even inside a building; facing the sun or moon directly; urinating or defecating in water, in public shade, in a hole, on a road, under a fruit-bearing tree; and urinating while standing without an excuse. The commentary provides further detail: the dislike of facing the sun/moon only applies if the disk is visible; the shade referred to is where people sit; privately owned shade requires permission; a hole is a cavity in ground or wall; the road is disliked even at the side; under a fruit tree due to possible harm from falling objects; and standing urination is only excused due to back pain or similar. The dua after exiting thanks Allah for removing harmful waste and preserving the body's nourishment.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinja): Cleansing the private parts after urination or defecation using water or solid purifiers like stones or pottery shards.
الخزف (al-khazaf): Fired clay used as a solid purifier (for istijmar).
الخلاء (al-khala): The place designated for relieving oneself (toilet).
عذر (udhr): An excuse that permits an otherwise prohibited or disliked action, e.g., using the left hand for istinja due to right hand ailment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Istinja with solids is valid if the material is pure and absorbent; the right hand is used unless an excuse exists.

Toilet Etiquette: Entering, Exiting, and Disliked Acts
Rulings on toilet etiquette and disliked acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the adab of entering and exiting the toilet and identify the acts that are makruh tahrimi or makruh tanzihi according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The toilet is a place of vulnerability; following the prophetic adab safeguards one's dignity and worship.

This passage details the recommended etiquette (adab) for entering and leaving the toilet and enumerates disliked acts (makruhat) that a Muslim should avoid. These rulings protect the sacredness of the qibla and public spaces.

Guided Path
1
List the adab of entering
Identify the recommended acts when entering: enter with left foot, seek refuge in Allah from Shaytan before entering, sit leaning on the left leg, and do not speak except out of necessity.
The commentary notes that refuge is sought before uncovering the private parts.
2
List the adab of exiting
Upon exiting, step out with the right foot and recite the supplication: 'Praise be to Allah who removed from me harm and granted me well-being.'
The dua is a recognition of Allah's mercy in removing harmful waste.
3
Identify the disliked acts
The passage mentions several makruh acts: facing or turning the back to the qibla (prohibitively disliked even in a building), facing the sun or moon, urinating or defecating in water, public shade, holes, roads, under fruit-bearing trees, and urinating standing without an excuse.
The commentary refines: facing sun/moon only disliked if the disk is visible; shade dislike depends on ownership; standing urination excused with back pain.
4
Analyze the commentary refinements
The commentary provides important qualifications: for example, 'shade' refers to public shade; if it is privately owned, the act is forbidden without permission. The standing urination is excused if there is a backache.
These refinements show that rulings are not absolute but contextual.
5
Apply to modern settings
In modern toilets, one should avoid facing the qibla direction. Many restrooms are designed with toilets facing away from qibla. The adab of entering left foot and dua remain relevant.
The ruling on facing qibla applies even inside a building.

The Four Pillars of Wudu in the Hanafi School
Definition of the four pillars of wudu with their boundaries and legal definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four pillars of wudu, define their legal boundaries, and explain the Hanafi distinction between fard qat'i and fard zanni.

Core Idea
Wudu has four pillars; washing requires flowing water, wiping one quarter of the head suffices, and each limb has precise boundaries.

This passage from Nur al-Idah defines the essential pillars (arkan) of wudu according to the Hanafi school. Understanding these boundaries is crucial for valid purification. The text also clarifies the legal concept of 'fard' and distinguishes between definitive and speculative obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four pillars
List the four obligations mentioned in the text: washing the face, washing the hands and forearms including elbows, washing the feet including the ankles, and wiping one quarter of the head.
2
Define the boundaries for each pillar
For the face: from the top of the forehead to the bottom of the chin lengthwise, and between the earlobes widthwise. For hands: up to and including the elbows. For feet: up to and including the ankles (the protruding bones). For head: one quarter.
The precise definition of 'ka'b' (ankle) is the protruding bone on each side.
3
Understand the definition of 'ghusl' (washing)
Ghusl means causing water to flow over the limb so that it drips. The minimum is two drops. Mere pouring without dripping is insufficient.
This is a Hanafi requirement; other schools may have different definitions.
4
Understand the definition of 'masah' (wiping)
Masah legally means touching the wet hand to the limb. It does not require passing the hand over (imrar) nor using fresh moisture; leftover water from washing a previous limb suffices. If rainwater touches the required area, it counts.
5
Distinguish between fard qat'i and fard zanni
Fard qat'i is established by definitive evidence; denying it makes one a kafir. Fard zanni is established by speculative evidence; denying it does not make one a kafir but its omission invalidates the act. The washing of limbs is qat'i, while the specific measure (one quarter of head) is zanni.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الوضوء بيان الوضوء أي في أحكامه أركان الوضوء أربعة وهي فرائضه الأول: غسل الوجه، وحده طولا من مبدأ سطح الجبهة إلى أسفل الذقن وحده عرضا ما بين شحمتي الأذنين، والثاني: غسل يديه مع مرفقيه والثالث: غسل رجليه مع كعبيه، والرابع: مسح ربع رأسه عن الوجه. وسنن الوضوء وآدابه مذكورة في محلها. وسببه استباحة ما لا يحل إلا به، وهو حكمه الدنيوي، وحكمه الأخروي الثواب في الآخرة. (الوضوء: قدم على الغسل؛ لأن الله قدمه عليه. ولأنه جزء منه، ولكثرة الاحتياج إليه. فرائضه: الفرض قسمان: قطعي، وهو ما ثبت بدليل قطعي موجب للعلم البديهي، ويكفر جاحده؛ وظني، وهو ما ثبت بدليل قطعي لكن فيه شبهة، ويسمى عمليا، وهو ما يفوت الجواز بفوته، وحكمه كالأول غير أنه لا يكفر جاحده. والغسل: إسالة الماء على المحل بحيث يتقاطر، وأقله قطرتان في الأصح، ولا تكفي الإسالة بدون التقاطر. ومبدأ سطح الجبهة: أي من أول أعلى الجبهة سواء كان به شعر أم لا. ويديه مع مرفقيه: بكسر الميم وفتح الفاء. وكعبيه: وهما العظمان المرتفعان في جانبي القدم. ومسح: لغة إمرار اليد على الشيء، وشرعا: إصابة اليد المبتلة العضو ولو بعد غسل عضو، لا مسحه ولا ببلل أخذ من عضو، وإن أصابه ماء أو مطر قدر المفروض أجزأه. وسببه: السبب ما أفضى إلى الشيء من غير تأثير فيه، فخرج به العلة كالعقد فإنه علة مؤثرة في حل النكاح. واستباحة: أي حل الإقدام على الفعل متوضأ. والثواب في الآخرة مقيدة بما إذا كان الوضوء منويا.)
Chapter on Wudu. Explanation of wudu, i.e., its rulings. The pillars of wudu are four, which are its obligations. First: washing the face; its boundary lengthwise from the beginning of the surface of the forehead to the bottom of the chin; its boundary widthwise between the two earlobes. Second: washing his hands including the elbows. Third: washing his feet including the ankles. Fourth: wiping one quarter of his head. And the sunnas and adab of wudu are mentioned in their place. Its cause is to make permissible what is otherwise not permissible, and that is its worldly ruling; its otherworldly ruling is reward in the Hereafter. (Wudu: it is mentioned before ghusl because Allah mentioned it before it, and because it is part of it, and due to greater need. Its obligations: obligation (fard) is of two types: qat'i (definitive) – established by definitive evidence, denier becomes kafir; and zanni (speculative) – established by definitive evidence but contains some doubt, called practical, its omission invalidates the act, its ruling is like the first except its denier is not a kafir. Washing (ghusl): causing water to flow on the part so that it drips; the minimum is two drops in the most correct view; mere pouring without dripping is insufficient. Beginning of the surface of the forehead: i.e., from the topmost part of the forehead whether it has hair or not. His hands including the elbows: with kasra on meem and fatha on fa. His ankles: the two protruding bones on the sides of the foot. Wiping (mash): linguistically, passing the hand over something; legally, touching the wet hand to the limb even after washing a limb, not wiping nor with moisture taken from a limb; if water from rain or similar touches it to the extent of the obligatory portion, it suffices. Its cause: a cause is that which leads to a thing without affecting it, thus excluding the effective cause (illa) like a contract which is an effective cause for making marriage permissible. 'Permissibility' (istibaha): i.e., making lawful to proceed with an action while in a state of wudu. The reward in the Hereafter is conditioned on performing wudu with intention.)
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah defines the four pillars (fara'id) of wudu, which are obligatory for its validity. The passage type is a definition and ruling statement, with commentary from Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi expanding on the terminology. The first pillar is washing the entire face, from the top of the forehead (including hairless parts) to the bottom of the chin lengthwise, and between the earlobes widthwise. It is important to note that merely wetting the face is insufficient; water must flow (ghusl) with at least two drops dripping. The second pillar is washing both hands including the elbows (the entire arm up to the elbow joint). The third is washing both feet including the ankles (the protruding bones on each side). The fourth is wiping one quarter of the head (masah), which in Hanafi school is defined as touching the wet hand to the head; it is not required to pass the hand over (imrar) nor to use fresh water; the moisture from previous washing suffices. The passage also distinguishes between fard qat'i (definitive obligation, denial causes kufr) and fard zanni (speculative obligation, denial does not cause kufr); the washing of limbs is qat'i, but the precise extent (like one quarter of the head) is zanni. The cause (sabab) of wudu is the intention to perform acts that require purity, such as prayer; the worldly ruling is that it permits such acts, and the otherworldly ruling is reward, provided there is intention (niyya). The sunan and adab are stated to be in their proper place (later in the text).

Key Terms
الفرض (al-fard): An obligation established by definitive evidence (qat'i) or speculative evidence (zanni); omitting it invalidates the act.
الغسل (al-ghusl): Causing water to flow over the limb so that it drips; minimum two drops
المسح (al-masah): Legally, touching the wet hand to the limb without necessarily passing (imrar) or using fresh moisture
الكعب (al-ka'b): The protruding ankle bone on each side of the foot

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the four pillars of wudu according to the Hanafi school?
A) Washing the face
B) Washing the hands and forearms including elbows
C) Wiping the entire head
D) Washing the feet including the ankles

Key Takeaway
The four pillars of wudu are washing the face, hands to elbows, feet to ankles, and wiping one quarter of the head; each has precise legal boundaries and definitions that must be observed for valid purification.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
The Four Pillars (Arkan) of Wudu
Listing and explaining the four pillars of wudu with definitions and boundaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four pillars of wudu, state their precise boundaries as defined by the Hanafi school, and explain the legal definitions of ghusl and mas'hu.

Core Idea
Wudu has four obligatory acts: washing face, hands, feet, and wiping one quarter of the head.

This lesson delves into the four pillars of wudu as defined in the Hanafi school. Understanding these pillars is essential because omitting any one invalidates the wudu. We will explore the precise boundaries of each limb and the specific legal definitions of washing (ghusl) and wiping (mas'hu).

Guided Path
1
Identify the four pillars
List them as stated: washing the face, washing the hands including elbows, washing the feet including ankles, and wiping a quarter of the head.
These are the arkan (obligatory integrals).
2
Define the boundaries
For the face: from the forehead (hairline) to the chin, and between the earlobes. For the hands: include the elbows. For the feet: include the ankles (the protruding bones). For the head: at least one quarter.
The boundaries are based on the text and commentary.
3
Understand the legal definitions
Ghusl (washing) requires water to flow and drip; mere wetting without dripping is insufficient. Mas'hu (wiping) is touching the wet hand to the limb; not necessarily a wiping motion.
The minimum for ghusl is two drops in the preferred view.
4
Recognize the consequence of omission
Omitting any pillar makes the wudu invalid (batil). It must be repeated.
This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that rukn omission invalidates.

بيان الوضوء
شروط وجوب الوضوء]
وشرط وجوبه العقل والبلوغ والإسلام وقدرة على استعمال الماء الكافي، وهو شرط الوجوب أيضا ووجود الحدث، وعدم الحيض والنفاس، وضيق الوقت.
شروط صحة الوضوء]
وشرط صحته ثلاثة عموم البشرة بالماء الطهور، وانقطاع ما ينافيه يخالفه المطهر وشرط الشرط: ما يلزم من عدمه العدم، ولا يلزم من وجوده وجود ولا عدم [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦١] العقل: فلا يجب على المجنون، ولا على الصبي، ولا على الكافر. مراقي الفلاح (٦١] وقدرة: أي قدرة المكلف على استعمال الماء الطهور الكافي لجميع الأعضاء مرة مرة شرط لوجوب الوضوء، فإن قدر غير المكلف، أو قدر المكلف على الماء ولكن لم يقدر على استعماله بأن كان الماء في ملكه ولكنه مريض، أو قدر المكلف على استعمال الماء ولكن الماء غير طهور، أو قدر المكلف على استعمال الماء الطهور لكنه لا يكفي لجميع أعضائه مرة مرة، لا يجب عليه الوضوء، وينبغي أن يقيد الماء بكونه غير محتاج إليه للعطش وغيره فإن الماء المحتاج إليه للعطش مشغول بحاجته، والمشغول بالحاجة كالمعدوم. الكافي: الجميع الأعضاء ولو مرة واحدة. الحدث : فلا يلزم الوضوء على الوضوء [مراقي الفلاح: ٦١] وضيق: فإن الوضوء لا يجب وجوباً مضيقاً ما دام الوقت موسعاً، وإذا ضاق الوقت يجب الوضوء وجوباً مضيقاً، واعلم أن شروط وجوب الوضوء لثمانية، وقد اختصرت هذا الشروط في واحد، هو قدرة المكلف بالطهارة عليها بالماء". الوقت: اعلم أن الوضوء لا يجب وجوباً مضيقاً بمجرد دخول وقت الصلاة ما لم يضيق وقتها، فحينئذ يجب الوضوء، فهذا الشرط للوجوب المضيق.
وشرط صحته في حاشية الأشباه" للحموي : شرط الصحة في العبادات عبارة عن سقوط القضاء بالفعل. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦١] ثلاثة وترجع هذه الثلاثة لواحد، هو عموم المطهر شرعاً البشرة. (مراقي الفلاح) عموم حتى لو بقي مقدار مغرز إبرة لم يصبه الماء من المفروض غسله، لم يصح الوضوء. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦١] البشرة: فلو بقي من البشر شيء ولو كان شعراً أو شعرتين، لا يصح الوضوء. وانقطاع ما ينافيه الخ: أي ما لم ينقطع ما ينافي الوضوء لا يصح الوضوء، فلو توضأت الحائض أو النفساء قبل انقطاع حيضها أو نفاسها لا يعتد بالوضوء، أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا انقطع على تمام العادة، وكذا انقطاع حدث مقيد بحال التوضؤ؛ لأنه بظهور بول وسيلان ناقض لا يصح الوضوء.
The Book of Purification. Chapter on Wudu. Explanation of Wudu, i.e., its rulings. The pillars of wudu are four, and they are its obligatory acts: First: washing the face, its limit lengthwise from the beginning (i.e., the entire face) the surface of the forehead to the bottom of the chin, and its limit widthwise between the two earlobes. Second: washing his hands along with the elbows. Third: washing his feet along with the ankles. Fourth: wiping a quarter of his head. The cause of wudu and its ruling: its cause is to permit what is not permissible except with it, and that is its worldly ruling; its otherworldly ruling is reward. Like prayer and touching the Quran. Wudu is placed before ghusl because Allah placed it before it [Maraqi al-Falah 56] and because it is part of it, and due to frequent need. (Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi) Its obligatory acts: The fard is of two types: qat'i (definitive) – that which is established by a definitive proof leading to intuitive knowledge, and its denier becomes a disbeliever; and zanni (speculative) – that which is established by a definitive proof but there is ambiguity, and it is called 'amali (practical), and its omission causes loss of permissibility, and its ruling is like the first except that its denier is not declared a disbeliever. If one considers the essence of washing and wiping, it is of the first type; if one considers the measure, it is of the second [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 56]. Washing the face: Ghusl is causing water to flow over the spot such that it drips, and its minimum is two drops in the soundest view, and mere flow without dripping is insufficient [Maraqi al-Falah 57]. 'Beginning' means from the top of the forehead, whether it has hair or not, indicating that even the bald, naturally bald, and those with receding hairlines must wash the face as mentioned [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi]. 'Hands' with kasr of the mim and fatha of the fa. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with 'ka'bayhi' which are the two protruding bones on the sides of the foot. Wiping linguistically is passing the hand over something, and legally it is touching the wet hand to the limb, even after washing a limb, not wiping it nor with moisture taken from a limb, and if water or rain touches it in the required amount it suffices [Maraqi al-Falah 60]. Its cause: The cause is that which leads to something without affecting it, thus excluding the 'illa like a contract, which is an effective cause in the permissibility of marriage [Maraqi al-Falah 60]. And it is the permissibility of proceeding with the act while in a state of wudu [Maraqi al-Falah 61]. The otherworldly [reward] is conditioned upon the wudu being performed with intention.

Conditions of the obligation of wudu: The conditions of its obligation are: sanity, puberty, Islam, ability to use sufficient water (this is also a condition for obligation), existence of hadath (ritual impurity), absence of menstruation and postpartum bleeding, and narrowness of time.
Conditions of the validity of wudu: The conditions of its validity are three: covering the skin with pure water (tahur), cessation of what contradicts it, and the condition of a condition is: its absence necessitates absence, but its presence does not necessitate presence or absence [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 61]. Sanity: it is not obligatory upon the insane, nor upon the minor, nor upon the disbeliever [Maraqi al-Falah 61]. Ability: i.e., the ability of the legally responsible person to use pure water sufficient for all limbs once each is a condition for the obligation of wudu. If one who is not legally responsible is able, or the responsible person has water but cannot use it (like water in his possession but he is sick), or the responsible person can use water but it is not pure (tahur), or the responsible person can use pure water but it is insufficient for all limbs once each, wudu is not obligatory. It is appropriate to restrict water to that which is not needed for drinking or other purposes, because water needed for drinking is occupied with a need, and what is occupied with a need is like nothingness. Sufficient means for all limbs even once. Hadath: wudu upon wudu is not required [Maraqi al-Falah 61]. Narrowness of time: wudu is not obligatory with strict obligation as long as time is expansive, and when time becomes narrow, wudu becomes obligatory with strict obligation. Know that the conditions for the obligation of wudu are eight, and I have summarized these conditions in one: the ability of the responsible person to perform purification with water.
Time: Know that wudu is not obligatory with strict obligation merely upon the entry of prayer time until its time becomes narrow, then wudu becomes obligatory. So this condition is for strict obligation.
And the condition of its validity: In Hashiyat al-Ashbah for al-Hamawi: The condition of validity in acts of worship is the non-requirement of making up (qada) by the act [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 61]. Three, and these three return to one: covering of the skin with what is legally purifier (mutahir). (Maraqi al-Falah) Completely, such that if the amount of a needle insertion remains without water from that which is obligatory to wash, the wudu is not valid [Maraqi al-Falah 61]. The skin: if any part of the skin remains [dry], even hair or two hairs, wudu is not valid. Cessation of what contradicts it: i.e., as long as that which invalidates wudu has not ceased, wudu is not valid. So if a menstruating or postpartum woman performs wudu before her period or postpartum bleeding ceases, the wudu is not considered. It is absolute but conditioned upon cessation at the completion of the usual period. Similarly, cessation of hadath (ritual impurity) is conditioned upon the state of performing wudu; because if urine flow or something nullifying appears, wudu is not valid.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the pillars (arkan) and conditions (shurut) of wudu (ablution) according to the Hanafi school, as presented in the matn of Nur al-Idah with commentary from Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi. The passage begins by stating that the pillars of wudu are four: washing the face, washing the hands including the elbows, washing the feet including the ankles, and wiping a quarter of the head. Each is defined precisely: the face extends from the forehead to the chin and between the earlobes; the hands include the elbows; the feet include the ankles (the two protruding bones); and wiping must cover at least one quarter of the head. The text then discusses the cause (sabab) and ruling (hukm) of wudu: the cause is the need to perform acts that are prohibited without purification, such as prayer and touching the Quran; the worldly ruling is that such acts become permissible, and the otherworldly ruling is reward, provided the wudu is performed with intention (niyyah). The passage explains the concept of fard (obligatory), distinguishing between qat'i (definitive, denying which leads to disbelief) and zanni (speculative, denying which does not cause disbelief). Washing and wiping in essence are qat'i, but the specific measures (e.g., one quarter of the head) are zanni. The text clarifies the definition of ghusl (washing) as causing water to flow over the part such that it drips, with a minimum of two drops; mere flow without dripping is insufficient. It defines mas'hu (wiping) legally as touching the wet hand to the limb, but not necessarily wiping it, and if rainwater suffices, it is acceptable. The cause (sabab) is distinct from 'illa (e.g., a contract is an 'illa for marriage). The passage then lists the conditions for the obligation of wudu: sanity, puberty, Islam, ability to use sufficient pure water, existence of hadath (ritual impurity), absence of menstruation and postpartum bleeding, and narrowness of time (i.e., prayer time is about to expire). It emphasizes that wudu is not obligatory with strict obligation except when time is narrow. The conditions for the validity of wudu are summarized as three, which revert to one: complete coverage of the skin with purifying water (tahur), cessation of anything that contradicts wudu (such as menstruation or ongoing hadath), and the condition that nothing remains dry even to the extent of a needle's insertion. The passage also notes that if the water is needed for drinking or other essential uses, it is considered non-existent and wudu is not obligatory. This passage is a comprehensive Hanafi treatment of the essential elements and prerequisites of wudu, suitable for students learning the foundational rulings.

Key Terms
الركن (al-rukn): The obligatory act (fard) that constitutes an integral part of wudu; omission invalidates it.
الغسل (al-ghusl): Causing water to flow over the limb such that it drips; minimum two drops.
المسح (al-mas'hu): Legally: touching the wet hand to the limb; not necessarily wiping or using moisture taken from another limb.

Checkpoint
What is the minimum area of the head that must be wiped for wudu to be valid according to the Hanafi school?
A) The entire head
B) Half the head
C) One quarter of the head
D) Three fingers' width

Key Takeaway
The four pillars of wudu must be completed exactly; any omission invalidates the ablution.

Taharah — Purification

The Conditions (Shurut) of Wudu
Listing conditions for obligation and validity of wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conditions of obligation and conditions of validity for wudu, list all eight conditions, and apply them to determine when wudu is required and valid.

Core Idea
Wudu is only obligatory when certain conditions (like sanity, puberty, ability, and narrow prayer time) are met; its validity depends on full skin coverage with pure water and absence of contradictions.

This lesson focuses on the conditions (shurut) that govern the obligation and validity of wudu according to the Hanafi school. It is important to understand these conditions because they determine both when wudu is required and what makes it legally acceptable. We will explore the detailed list from the text.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between conditions of obligation and validity
Obligation conditions determine when wudu becomes required; validity conditions determine whether the wudu performed is legally sound.
These are separate categories.
2
List the conditions of obligation
Eight conditions: sanity, puberty, Islam, ability to use sufficient pure water, existence of hadath, absence of menstruation/nifas, narrowness of time, and water not needed for essential use.
The text summarizes them as 'ability of the responsible person to perform purification with water'.
3
List the conditions of validity
Three conditions that reduce to one: complete coverage of the skin with purifying water (tahur) and cessation of anything that contradicts wudu.
Complete coverage means no spot remains dry, even the size of a needle insertion.
4
Understand special cases
If water is needed for drinking or other essentials, it is considered non-existent; wudu is not obligatory. Also, menstruating or postpartum women cannot perform valid wudu until bleeding ceases.
These derive from the principle 'what is occupied with need is like non-existent'.
5
Apply to scenarios
Given a scenario, first check if conditions of obligation are met, then if conditions of validity would be satisfied.
Example: A sick person unable to use water is not obligated to do wudu.
