وشرط وجوبه العقل والبلوغ والإسلام وقدرة على استعمال الماء الكافي، وهو شرط الوجوب أيضا ووجود الحدث، وعدم الحيض والنفاس، وضيق الوقت.
شروط صحة الوضوء]
وشرط صحته ثلاثة عموم البشرة بالماء الطهور، وانقطاع ما ينافيه يخالفه المطهر وشرط الشرط: ما يلزم من عدمه العدم، ولا يلزم من وجوده وجود ولا عدم [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦١] العقل: فلا يجب على المجنون، ولا على الصبي، ولا على الكافر. مراقي الفلاح (٦١] وقدرة: أي قدرة المكلف على استعمال الماء الطهور الكافي لجميع الأعضاء مرة مرة شرط لوجوب الوضوء، فإن قدر غير المكلف، أو قدر المكلف على الماء ولكن لم يقدر على استعماله بأن كان الماء في ملكه ولكنه مريض، أو قدر المكلف على استعمال الماء ولكن الماء غير طهور، أو قدر المكلف على استعمال الماء الطهور لكنه لا يكفي لجميع أعضائه مرة مرة، لا يجب عليه الوضوء، وينبغي أن يقيد الماء بكونه غير محتاج إليه للعطش وغيره فإن الماء المحتاج إليه للعطش مشغول بحاجته، والمشغول بالحاجة كالمعدوم. الكافي: الجميع الأعضاء ولو مرة واحدة. الحدث : فلا يلزم الوضوء على الوضوء [مراقي الفلاح: ٦١] وضيق: فإن الوضوء لا يجب وجوباً مضيقاً ما دام الوقت موسعاً، وإذا ضاق الوقت يجب الوضوء وجوباً مضيقاً، واعلم أن شروط وجوب الوضوء لثمانية، وقد اختصرت هذا الشروط في واحد، هو قدرة المكلف بالطهارة عليها بالماء". الوقت: اعلم أن الوضوء لا يجب وجوباً مضيقاً بمجرد دخول وقت الصلاة ما لم يضيق وقتها، فحينئذ يجب الوضوء، فهذا الشرط للوجوب المضيق.
وشرط صحته في حاشية الأشباه" للحموي : شرط الصحة في العبادات عبارة عن سقوط القضاء بالفعل. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦١] ثلاثة وترجع هذه الثلاثة لواحد، هو عموم المطهر شرعاً البشرة. (مراقي الفلاح) عموم حتى لو بقي مقدار مغرز إبرة لم يصبه الماء من المفروض غسله، لم يصح الوضوء. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦١] البشرة: فلو بقي من البشر شيء ولو كان شعراً أو شعرتين، لا يصح الوضوء. وانقطاع ما ينافيه الخ: أي ما لم ينقطع ما ينافي الوضوء لا يصح الوضوء، فلو توضأت الحائض أو النفساء قبل انقطاع حيضها أو نفاسها لا يعتد بالوضوء، أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا انقطع على تمام العادة، وكذا انقطاع حدث مقيد بحال التوضؤ؛ لأنه بظهور بول وسيلان ناقض لا يصح الوضوء.
The Book of Purification. Chapter on Wudu. Explanation of Wudu, i.e., its rulings. The pillars of wudu are four, and they are its obligatory acts: First: washing the face, its limit lengthwise from the beginning (i.e., the entire face) the surface of the forehead to the bottom of the chin, and its limit widthwise between the two earlobes. Second: washing his hands along with the elbows. Third: washing his feet along with the ankles. Fourth: wiping a quarter of his head. The cause of wudu and its ruling: its cause is to permit what is not permissible except with it, and that is its worldly ruling; its otherworldly ruling is reward. Like prayer and touching the Quran. Wudu is placed before ghusl because Allah placed it before it [Maraqi al-Falah 56] and because it is part of it, and due to frequent need. (Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi) Its obligatory acts: The fard is of two types: qat'i (definitive) – that which is established by a definitive proof leading to intuitive knowledge, and its denier becomes a disbeliever; and zanni (speculative) – that which is established by a definitive proof but there is ambiguity, and it is called 'amali (practical), and its omission causes loss of permissibility, and its ruling is like the first except that its denier is not declared a disbeliever. If one considers the essence of washing and wiping, it is of the first type; if one considers the measure, it is of the second [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 56]. Washing the face: Ghusl is causing water to flow over the spot such that it drips, and its minimum is two drops in the soundest view, and mere flow without dripping is insufficient [Maraqi al-Falah 57]. 'Beginning' means from the top of the forehead, whether it has hair or not, indicating that even the bald, naturally bald, and those with receding hairlines must wash the face as mentioned [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi]. 'Hands' with kasr of the mim and fatha of the fa. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with 'ka'bayhi' which are the two protruding bones on the sides of the foot. Wiping linguistically is passing the hand over something, and legally it is touching the wet hand to the limb, even after washing a limb, not wiping it nor with moisture taken from a limb, and if water or rain touches it in the required amount it suffices [Maraqi al-Falah 60]. Its cause: The cause is that which leads to something without affecting it, thus excluding the 'illa like a contract, which is an effective cause in the permissibility of marriage [Maraqi al-Falah 60]. And it is the permissibility of proceeding with the act while in a state of wudu [Maraqi al-Falah 61]. The otherworldly [reward] is conditioned upon the wudu being performed with intention.

Conditions of the obligation of wudu: The conditions of its obligation are: sanity, puberty, Islam, ability to use sufficient water (this is also a condition for obligation), existence of hadath (ritual impurity), absence of menstruation and postpartum bleeding, and narrowness of time.
Conditions of the validity of wudu: The conditions of its validity are three: covering the skin with pure water (tahur), cessation of what contradicts it, and the condition of a condition is: its absence necessitates absence, but its presence does not necessitate presence or absence [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 61]. Sanity: it is not obligatory upon the insane, nor upon the minor, nor upon the disbeliever [Maraqi al-Falah 61]. Ability: i.e., the ability of the legally responsible person to use pure water sufficient for all limbs once each is a condition for the obligation of wudu. If one who is not legally responsible is able, or the responsible person has water but cannot use it (like water in his possession but he is sick), or the responsible person can use water but it is not pure (tahur), or the responsible person can use pure water but it is insufficient for all limbs once each, wudu is not obligatory. It is appropriate to restrict water to that which is not needed for drinking or other purposes, because water needed for drinking is occupied with a need, and what is occupied with a need is like nothingness. Sufficient means for all limbs even once. Hadath: wudu upon wudu is not required [Maraqi al-Falah 61]. Narrowness of time: wudu is not obligatory with strict obligation as long as time is expansive, and when time becomes narrow, wudu becomes obligatory with strict obligation. Know that the conditions for the obligation of wudu are eight, and I have summarized these conditions in one: the ability of the responsible person to perform purification with water.
Time: Know that wudu is not obligatory with strict obligation merely upon the entry of prayer time until its time becomes narrow, then wudu becomes obligatory. So this condition is for strict obligation.
And the condition of its validity: In Hashiyat al-Ashbah for al-Hamawi: The condition of validity in acts of worship is the non-requirement of making up (qada) by the act [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 61]. Three, and these three return to one: covering of the skin with what is legally purifier (mutahir). (Maraqi al-Falah) Completely, such that if the amount of a needle insertion remains without water from that which is obligatory to wash, the wudu is not valid [Maraqi al-Falah 61]. The skin: if any part of the skin remains [dry], even hair or two hairs, wudu is not valid. Cessation of what contradicts it: i.e., as long as that which invalidates wudu has not ceased, wudu is not valid. So if a menstruating or postpartum woman performs wudu before her period or postpartum bleeding ceases, the wudu is not considered. It is absolute but conditioned upon cessation at the completion of the usual period. Similarly, cessation of hadath (ritual impurity) is conditioned upon the state of performing wudu; because if urine flow or something nullifying appears, wudu is not valid.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the pillars (arkan) and conditions (shurut) of wudu (ablution) according to the Hanafi school, as presented in the matn of Nur al-Idah with commentary from Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi. The passage begins by stating that the pillars of wudu are four: washing the face, washing the hands including the elbows, washing the feet including the ankles, and wiping a quarter of the head. Each is defined precisely: the face extends from the forehead to the chin and between the earlobes; the hands include the elbows; the feet include the ankles (the two protruding bones); and wiping must cover at least one quarter of the head. The text then discusses the cause (sabab) and ruling (hukm) of wudu: the cause is the need to perform acts that are prohibited without purification, such as prayer and touching the Quran; the worldly ruling is that such acts become permissible, and the otherworldly ruling is reward, provided the wudu is performed with intention (niyyah). The passage explains the concept of fard (obligatory), distinguishing between qat'i (definitive, denying which leads to disbelief) and zanni (speculative, denying which does not cause disbelief). Washing and wiping in essence are qat'i, but the specific measures (e.g., one quarter of the head) are zanni. The text clarifies the definition of ghusl (washing) as causing water to flow over the part such that it drips, with a minimum of two drops; mere flow without dripping is insufficient. It defines mas'hu (wiping) legally as touching the wet hand to the limb, but not necessarily wiping it, and if rainwater suffices, it is acceptable. The cause (sabab) is distinct from 'illa (e.g., a contract is an 'illa for marriage). The passage then lists the conditions for the obligation of wudu: sanity, puberty, Islam, ability to use sufficient pure water, existence of hadath (ritual impurity), absence of menstruation and postpartum bleeding, and narrowness of time (i.e., prayer time is about to expire). It emphasizes that wudu is not obligatory with strict obligation except when time is narrow. The conditions for the validity of wudu are summarized as three, which revert to one: complete coverage of the skin with purifying water (tahur), cessation of anything that contradicts wudu (such as menstruation or ongoing hadath), and the condition that nothing remains dry even to the extent of a needle's insertion. The passage also notes that if the water is needed for drinking or other essential uses, it is considered non-existent and wudu is not obligatory. This passage is a comprehensive Hanafi treatment of the essential elements and prerequisites of wudu, suitable for students learning the foundational rulings.

Key Terms
الشَّرْط (al-shart): A condition; its absence necessitates absence (of the conditioned), but its presence does not necessitate presence. In wudu, conditions include sanity, purity of water, etc.
الحدث (al-hadath): Ritual impurity that requires ablution; existence of hadath is a condition for the obligation of wudu.
الطهور (al-tahur): Water that is both pure and purifying; it must be used for wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition of 'narrowness of time' for the obligation of wudu?
A) Any time after adhan.
B) When prayer time is about to expire.
C) At the start of prayer time.
D) Only for Fajr prayer.

Key Takeaway
Wudu is only obligatory when all eight conditions are met; its validity depends on complete skin coverage with pure water and cessation of contradictions.

Taharah — Purification
beginner

The Eight Conditions for Wudu to Be Obligatory
Lists eight conditions for wudu to be obligatory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight conditions for wudu to be obligatory and explain how each condition affects the obligation.

Core Idea
Wudu is obligatory only when eight conditions are met; if any is absent, no obligation.

This lesson unpacks the conditions that trigger the obligation of wudu. Understanding these conditions is crucial because wudu is not always required; it only becomes obligatory when certain prerequisites are satisfied. We will walk through each condition as stated in the classical Hanafi text Nur al-Idah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions of obligation
Read the matn and list all eight shurut wujub mentioned: aql, bulugh, Islam, qudra, hadath, absence of hayd, absence of nifas, dhiq al-waqt.
These are prerequisites before wudu becomes mandatory.
2
Explain each condition briefly
For each condition, state what it means and why it is required. For example, 'aql excludes the insane; bulugh excludes children; Islam excludes the disbeliever; qudra requires ability to use water; hadath requires being in a state of minor impurity; hayd/nifas exclude women during menses/lochia; dhiq al-waqt means time for prayer is narrow.
Each condition has a clear legal rationale.
3
Understand the exceptions
Note cases where a condition is not met: e.g., a sick person who cannot use water, or water insufficient for all limbs, etc. In such cases, wudu is not obligatory.
The commentary elaborates on the qudra condition.
4
Distinguish between wide and narrow time
Recognize that wudu is not obligatory immediately upon entry of prayer time; it only becomes obligatory when time is about to end (dhiq al-waqt).
This is a key nuance of the obligation.
5
Summarize the one overarching condition
The author notes that all eight conditions reduce to one: the ability of the accountable person to perform purification with water. Reflect on how this overarching condition encapsulates the others.
This distillation aids memorization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شروط وجوب الوضوء]
وشرط وجوبه العقل والبلوغ والإسلام وقدرة على استعمال الماء الكافي،
وهو شرط الوجوب أيضا
ووجود الحدث، وعدم الحيض والنفاس، وضيق الوقت.
العقل: فلا يجب على المجنون، ولا على الصبي، ولا على الكافر. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦١] وقدرة: أي قدرة المكلف على استعمال الماء الطهور الكافي لجميع الأعضاء مرة مرة شرط لوجوب الوضوء، فإن قدر غير المكلف، أو قدر المكلف على الماء ولكن لم يقدر على استعماله بأن كان الماء في ملكه ولكنه مريض، أو قدر المكلف على استعمال الماء ولكن الماء غير طهور، أو قدر المكلف على استعمال الماء الطهور لكنه لا يكفي لجميع أعضائه مرة مرة، لا يجب عليه الوضوء، وينبغي أن يقيد الماء بكونه غير محتاج إليه للعطش وغيره فإن الماء المحتاج إليه للعطش مشغول بحاجته، والمشغول بالحاجة كالمعدوم. الكافي: الجميع الأعضاء ولو مرة واحدة. الحدث : فلا يلزم الوضوء على الوضوء [مراقي الفلاح: ٦١] وضيق: فإن الوضوء لا يجب وجوباً مضيقاً ما دام الوقت موسعاً، وإذا ضاق الوقت يجب الوضوء وجوباً مضيقاً، واعلم أن شروط وجوب الوضوء لثمانية، وقد اختصرت هذا الشروط في واحد، هو قدرة المكلف بالطهارة عليها بالماء". الوقت: اعلم أن الوضوء لا يجب وجوباً مضيقاً بمجرد دخول وقت الصلاة ما لم يضيق وقتها، فحينئذ يجب الوضوء، فهذا الشرط للوجوب المضيق.
[Conditions of obligation of wudu] And the condition of its obligation is: intellect, puberty, Islam, and ability to use sufficient pure water. (And this is also a condition of obligation.) And existence of hadath, and absence of menstruation and postnatal bleeding, and narrowness of time. Intellect: so it is not obligatory upon the insane, nor upon the child, nor upon the disbeliever. [Maraqi al-Falah: 61] And ability: meaning the ability of the accountable person to use pure water sufficient for all limbs once each is a condition for the obligation of wudu. If a non-accountable person is able, or an accountable person is able to get water but unable to use it — because the water is in his possession but he is sick, or he is able to use water but it is not pure, or he is able to use pure water but it is insufficient for all his limbs once each — then wudu is not obligatory upon him. It should be qualified that the water is not needed for thirst etc., because water needed for thirst is occupied with his need, and what is occupied with need is like nonexistent. Sufficient: for all limbs at least once. Hadath: so wudu is not required upon wudu [Maraqi al-Falah: 61]. And narrowness: wudu is not obligatory with a restricted obligation as long as time is expansive, but when time becomes restricted, wudu becomes obligatory with a restricted obligation. Know that the conditions of obligation of wudu are eight, and I have summarized these conditions into one: the ability of the accountable person to perform purification with water. Time: know that wudu is not obligatory with restricted obligation merely by the entrance of prayer time until its time becomes restricted, then it becomes obligatory. So this condition is for the restricted obligation.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage presents the conditions for wudu to be obligatory. The author first lists the main conditions in the matn: intellect, puberty, Islam, ability to use sufficient pure water, existence of hadath (ritual impurity), absence of menstruation/postnatal bleeding, and narrowness of time. The commentary then explains each condition in detail. Intellect excludes the insane, the child, and the disbeliever. Ability is elaborated: the person must have the physical and financial ability to use pure water sufficient for all limbs once. If any factor prevents usage, obligation is lifted. Water needed for thirst is considered unavailable. The condition of hadath means that one must be in a state of ritual impurity; wudu is not required if one is already in wudu. The narrowness of time condition distinguishes between expansive and restricted obligation: as long as prayer time remains expansive, wudu is not obligatory with a restricted sense, but when time becomes tight, wudu becomes immediately obligatory. The author notes that all eight conditions reduce to one: the ability of the accountable person to perform purification with water. This is a key Hanafi principle: obligation is contingent on capacity.

Key Terms
شرط وجوب (shart wujub): A condition that must exist for the act to be obligatory; if absent, the act is not required.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that prevents prayer; wudu removes minor hadath (hadath asghar).
قدرة (qudra): Ability to use sufficient pure water; includes physical and financial capacity.
ضيق الوقت (dhiq al-waqt): Narrowness of time; the condition that wudu becomes obligatory with a restricted obligation when prayer time is about to end.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the obligation of wudu?
A) Intellect
B) Puberty
C) Intention
D) Ability to use water

Key Takeaway
The obligation of wudu depends on eight conditions; understanding them prevents incorrect assumptions about when purification is required.

Conditions of Validity of Wudu
States the three conditions for wudu to be valid and elaborates with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions of validity of wudu, identify violations of each condition, and explain the legal definition of a condition (shart).

Core Idea
Wudu is valid only when water reaches every part of the skin, free from any state that opposes purity, and with no physical barrier.

The validity of wudu depends not only on performing its actions but also on three preconditions. These conditions ensure that the act of wudu is legally sound. If any of these conditions is missing, wudu is invalid and must be repeated. This lesson examines each condition with practical examples and also clarifies the meaning of a 'condition' in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
From the text, extract the three conditions: covering the skin with pure water, cessation of contradictory states, and removal of barriers.
These are the shurut of sihha.
2
Understand the definition of a condition (shart)
The text defines shart: its absence entails absence of the conditioned, but its presence does not entail presence or absence of the conditioned.
This logical definition is important for distinguishing conditions from causes.
3
Analyze each condition in detail
For 'covering the skin' – even a needle's insertion area left dry invalidates wudu. For 'cessation' – menses, postnatal bleeding, and hadath must stop. For 'removal of barriers' – wax, fat, fish skin, dry bread are barriers; oil residue is not.
Pay attention to what is not a barrier.
4
Apply the unified principle
All three conditions reduce to one: covering the skin with legally purifying water.
This highlights the overarching requirement.
5
Distinguish between barrier and non-barrier substances
Substances like wax, fat, and dried bread that form a physical barrier require removal. Residue like oil that does not block water is not a barrier.
This distinction is practical for daily life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شروط صحة الوضوء]
وشرط صحته ثلاثة عموم البشرة بالماء الطهور، وانقطاع ما ينافيه من حيض ونفاس وحدث، وزوال ما يمنع وصول الماء إلى الجسد كشمع وشحم.
وشرط الشرط: ما يلزم من عدمه العدم، ولا يلزم من وجوده وجود ولا عدم [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦١] 
وشرط صحته في حاشية الأشباه" للحموي : شرط الصحة في العبادات عبارة عن سقوط القضاء بالفعل. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦١] ثلاثة وترجع هذه الثلاثة لواحد، هو عموم المطهر شرعاً البشرة. (مراقي الفلاح) عموم حتى لو بقي مقدار مغرز إبرة لم يصبه الماء من المفروض غسله، لم يصح الوضوء. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦١] البشرة: فلو بقي من البشر شيء ولو كان شعراً أو شعرتين، لا يصح الوضوء. وانقطاع ما ينافيه الخ: أي ما لم ينقطع ما ينافي الوضوء لا يصح الوضوء، فلو توضأت الحائض أو النفساء قبل انقطاع حيضها أو نفاسها لا يعتد بالوضوء، أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا انقطع على تمام العادة، وكذا انقطاع حدث مقيد بحال التوضؤ؛ لأنه بظهور بول وسيلان ناقض لا يصح الوضوء.
وزوال ما يمنع إلخ أي وزوال المانع عن وصول الماء إلى الجسد شرط لصحة الوضوء، فلو غسل المتوضئ رجليه وبهما شمع لشقوقهما لا يصح وضوؤه ما لم يزله وهذا على حرم الشمع لا على أثره. كشمع قيد به؛ لأن بقاء دسومة الزيت ونحوه لا يمنع؛ لعدم الحائل. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٢] وشحم وكجلد السمك والخبز الممضوغ الجاف.
[Conditions of validity of wudu] And the condition of its validity are three: covering the skin with pure water, cessation of what opposes it from menstruation, postnatal bleeding, and hadath, and removal of what prevents water reaching the body like wax and fat. And the condition of a condition is: what necessarily entails absence from its absence, but its existence does not necessarily entail existence nor absence [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 61]. And the condition of validity in Hashiyat al-Ashbah by al-Hamawi: the condition of validity in acts of worship is the dropping of the duty (qada) by the act. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 61] Three, and these three reduce to one: the covering of the skin with what is legally purifying. (Maraqi al-Falah) Coverage: even if the amount of a needle's insertion remains unaffected by water from what is obligatory to wash, wudu is invalid. [Maraqi al-Falah: 61] The skin: if any part of the skin remains, even if it is hair or two hairs, wudu is invalid. And 'cessation of what opposes it' etc.: meaning as long as what opposes wudu has not ceased, wudu is not valid. So if a menstruating woman or a woman in postnatal bleeding performs wudu before her menstruation or postnatal bleeding ceases, her wudu is not counted. This is absolute, but it is restricted to when it ceases after the completion of the usual period. Similarly, cessation of hadath is restricted to the state of wudu; because if urine emerges or it flows, that invalidates wudu, so wudu is not valid. And 'removal of what prevents' etc.: meaning removal of the barrier preventing water reaching the body is a condition for validity of wudu. So if the person performing wudu washes his feet and there is wax on them for cracks, his wudu is not valid until he removes it, and this is regarding the substance of wax, not its trace. Wax is specified because the oiliness from oil etc. does not prevent water reaching the skin due to the absence of a barrier. [Maraqi al-Falah: 62] And also fat, fish skin, and dry chewed bread.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage explains the conditions for wudu to be valid. The three conditions are: 1) covering the skin with pure water (so every part must be washed), 2) cessation of anything that contradicts wudu such as menstruation or passing urine (so a woman in menses cannot have valid wudu until it ends), and 3) removal of any physical barrier that prevents water from reaching the skin (like wax or fat). The commentary elaborates: even a small area left dry invalidates wudu. The definition of a condition (shart) is given: it is something whose absence entails absence of the conditioned, but its presence does not entail presence or absence. The three conditions reduce to one: the skin must be covered with legally purifying water. The commentary also discusses specific examples: wax on feet must be removed; oil residue does not form a barrier. This highlights the Hanafi emphasis on actual physical contact of water with skin.

Key Terms
شرط صحة (shart sihha): A condition that must exist for the act to be valid; if absent, the act is invalid and must be repeated.
عموم البشرة (umum al-bashara): Covering all of the skin that is obligatory to wash with water.
انقطاع ما ينافيه (inqita' ma yunafihi): Cessation of any state that contradicts the state of purity, such as menses or urine.
زوال المانع (zawal al-mani'): Removal of any physical barrier that prevents water from reaching the skin.
شرط (shart): A condition in legal theory: something whose absence entails absence of the conditioned, but its presence does not entail presence or absence of the conditioned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a barrier that invalidates wudu if not removed?
A) Oil residue
B) Dried chewed bread
C) Perspiration
D) Dust

Key Takeaway
The three conditions of wudu are covering the skin with pure water, cessation of contradictory states, and removal of physical barriers; all reduce to ensuring water reaches the entire skin.

Washing the Beard in Wudu
Rulings on washing the beard in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for washing the thick beard, the thin beard, and identify which parts of facial hair are exempt from washing.

Core Idea
For a thick beard, only the outer part is wajib; for a thin beard, water must reach the skin.

The beard is an important part of the face in wudu. However, the Hanafi school distinguishes based on density: a thick beard that hides the skin requires only washing the outer surface, while a thin beard requires water to reach the skin. Additionally, hair that hangs below the oval of the face and the area between closed lips are not obligated to be washed, though wiping the hanging hair is recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of beard
Distinguish between thick (skin not visible) and thin (skin visible) beard based on the text's definition.
The text defines 'al-lihya al-kaththa' as that whose skin is not seen.
2
Apply the obligation
For thick beard: wash the apparent part (wajib). For thin beard: deliver water to the skin (wajib).
3
Recognize what is not obligatory
Hair beyond the face oval (mustarsil) and between closed lips are not required to be washed. Wiping the mustarsil is sunnah.
The text says 'no obligation without disagreement' for these.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Earlier views (one-third, one-fourth, or wiping all) are retracted; the relied-upon position is washing the outer part.
The phrase 'fi asahh ma yufata bihi' indicates the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل [ في تمام أحكام الوضوء]
يجب غسل ظاهر اللحية الكثة في أصح ما يفتى به، ويجب إيصال الماء إلى بشرة اللحية الخفيفة، ولا يجب إيصال الماء إلى المسترسل من الشعر عن دائرة الوجه، ولا إلى ما انكتم من الشفتين عند الانضمام، ولو انضمت الأصابع أو طال الظفر فغطى الأنملة، أو كان فيه ما يمنع الماء كعجين وجب غسل ما تحته، ولا يمنع الدرن في المحل المفروض الغسل وخرء البراغيث ونحوها ويجب تحريك الخاتم الضيق، ولو ضره غسل شقوق رجليه جاز إمرار الماء على الدواء الذي وضعه فيها.
اللحية الكثة: وهي التي لا ترى بشرتها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٢] في أصح ما إلخ ورجعوا عما قيل من الاكتفاء بثلثها أو ربعها أو مسح كلها ونحوه. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٢] ولا يجب إلخ: أي لا يجب غسله ولا مسحه بلا خلاف عندنا نعم سن مسحه. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٢] ولو انضمت بحيث لا يصل الماء بنفسه إلى ما بينها. (مراقي الفلاح) طال ومنع وصول الماء إلى ما تحته مراقي (الفلاح الدرن أي وسخ الأظفار، سواء للقروي والمصري في الأصح، فيصح الغسل مع وجوده مراقي الفلاح (٦٣] ولو ضره وإن ضره إمرار الماء على الدواء مسح عليه، وإن ضره أيضًا تركه وإن كان لا يضره شيء من ذلك تعين بقدر ما لا يضره حتى لو كان يضره الماء البارد دون الحار، وهو قادر عليه لزمه استعمال الحار. [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٣] جاز إلخ: اعلم أن محل جواز إمرار الماء على الدواء إذا لم يزد على رأس الشقاق، فإن زاد تعين غسل ما تحت الزائد كما في ابن أمير الحاج، ومثله في "الدر" "المجتبى"، لكن ينبغي أن يقيد بعدم الضرر [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٣]
[Section on the complete rulings of wudu] It is obligatory to wash the apparent part of the thick beard according to the most sound position relied upon for fatwa, and it is obligatory to deliver water to the skin of the thin beard. It is not obligatory to deliver water to the hanging hair beyond the circle of the face, nor to what is hidden between the lips when they are closed. And if the fingers are stuck together, or the nail is long and covers the fingertip, or there is something blocking water like dough, it is obligatory to wash what is underneath. And dirt on the area that is obligatory to wash does not prevent (validity), nor does flea dirt and the like. And it is obligatory to move a tight ring. And if washing the cracks of his feet harms him, he may pass water over the medicine he placed on them. The thick beard: that whose skin is not visible. [Maraqi al-Falah: 62] Regarding 'the most sound' etc.: they have retracted from the positions that sufficed with washing one-third or one-fourth or wiping all of it etc. [Maraqi al-Falah: 62] 'It is not obligatory' etc.: meaning it is not obligatory to wash it nor wipe it, without disagreement among us; rather it is recommended to wipe it. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 62] 'If they are stuck': such that water does not reach between them by itself. (Maraqi al-Falah) 'Long and prevents water reaching what is under it': dirt means filth of the nails, whether for the villager or the city dweller in the most sound, the washing is valid with its presence. [Maraqi al-Falah: 63] 'And if it harms him': meaning if passing water over the medicine harms him, he may wipe over it; and if it also harms him to leave it, then if it does not harm him any of that, he must do what does not harm him, to the extent that if cold water harms him but hot does not, and he is able, he must use hot. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 63] 'He may': know that the place of permissibility of passing water over medicine is if it does not exceed the top of the crack; if it exceeds, it becomes obligatory to wash what is under the excess as in Ibn Amir al-Hajj, and similar in al-Durr and al-Mujtaba, but it should be qualified by the absence of harm. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 63]
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This section provides detailed rulings for wudu. For a thick beard (where skin is not visible), only the outer part must be washed; for a thin beard, water must reach the skin. Hair extending beyond the face's oval (like long beard) does not need washing. Between lips need not be washed when mouth is closed. If fingers are tightly pressed together or nails are long, water must reach the skin between them. Dirt under nails and flea dirt do not invalidate wudu. A tight ring must be moved to allow water under it. For cracked feet with medicine, if washing with water harms, one may simply pass water over the medicine, but if the medicine extends beyond the crack, the excess must be washed. The commentary clarifies that the relied-upon position for thick beard is to wash the apparent part, not just a portion. It also notes that washing the hair on the sides of the face is recommended but not obligatory. For cracks, if cold water harms but hot is available and harmless, hot water must be used. This shows the principle of necessity (darura) in wudu: obligation is lifted when harm occurs.

Key Terms
اللحية الكثة (al-lihya al-kaththa): A thick beard where the skin underneath is not visible.
المسترسل من الشعر (al-mustarsil min al-sha'r): Hair that hangs down from the oval of the face, like a long beard.
اللحية الخفيفة (al-lihya al-khafifa): A thin beard where the skin is visible through the hair.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Must wash the entire beard including the skin underneath
B) Must wash only the outer apparent part
C) Must wash one-third of the beard
D) No washing needed

Key Takeaway
For a thick beard, only the outer part needs to be washed; for a thin beard, water must reach the skin; hanging hair beyond the face is not obligatory.

Wajibat and Conditions in Wudu: Beard, Barriers, and Ring
Detailed legal rulings on mandatory washing and barrier removal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on washing the beard, removing barriers, and moving the tight ring in wudu, and apply them to common scenarios.

Core Idea
Exterior of thick beard wajib to wash; barriers like wax must be removed; tight ring must be moved — obligations, not sunnahs.

This lesson unpacks the detailed rulings from Nur al-Idah on what exactly must be washed in wudu. It clarifies the distinction between the thick and thin beard, the necessity of removing physical barriers, and the peculiar case of a tight ring. These are not just recommendations but obligations that affect the validity of wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wajib acts
Find all explicit wajib acts mentioned: washing beard exterior, moving tight ring, removing barriers.
Also note the sunnah acts like wiping hanging beard.
2
Categorize as wajib or shart
Distinguish between a condition (shart) like barrier removal and an obligation (wajib) like moving the ring.
Conditions must be met for validity; wajib acts omitted require compensation.
3
Note the intra-madhhab dispute
The text says the beard ruling is 'the soundest position' after retracting earlier views of one-third or wiping.
Understand that the mufta bihi is the full washing of the exterior.
4
Apply barrier removal to examples
Consider scenarios: wax on feet, dough under nails, residue of oil. The text specifies that the substance itself, not its residue, blocks water.
Residue of oil does not prevent water, so wudu is valid.
5
Summarize practical implications
List what a person must ensure before wudu: no physical barriers, ring moved, beard exterior washed, medicine on cracks wiped over if harmful to wash.
Use the conditions-pillars framework to structure the summary.

The Book of Purification. 24. Explanation of wudu. From menstruation, postpartum bleeding, hadath, and removal of what prevents water reaching the body like wax and fat. Explanation of 'ma'. Section on the complete rulings of wudu. It is obligatory to wash the exterior of the thick beard in the soundest position given for fatwa, and it is obligatory to bring water to the skin of the thin beard, and it is not obligatory to bring water to the hanging hair beyond the face circle, nor to what is concealed of the lips when closed, and if the fingers are closed or the nail is long and covers the fingertip, or there is something that prevents water like dough, it is obligatory to wash what is under it, and dirt in the site of obligatory washing does not prevent, nor flea droppings and the like, and it is obligatory to move a tight ring, and if washing the cracks of his feet harms him, it is permissible to pass water over the medicine he placed in them. Removal of what prevents etc.: removal of the barrier preventing water reaching the body is a condition for the validity of wudu. If the person performing wudu washes his feet and there is wax on them for cracks, his wudu is not valid until he removes it, and this refers to the wax itself, not its residue. Wax is specified because the residue of oil and the like does not prevent due to lack of barrier. (Maraqi al-Falah 62) And fat, fish skin, dry chewed bread. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: apparent specification indicates that washing under the upper layer of hair roots is not obligatory. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 62) The thick beard: that whose skin is not visible. (Maraqi al-Falah 62) In the soundest etc.: they retracted from what was said of being content with one-third or one-fourth or wiping all of it and so on. (Maraqi al-Falah 62) And it is not obligatory etc.: it is not obligatory to wash it nor wipe it without disagreement among us, rather it is sunnah to wipe it. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 62) And if they are closed such that water does not reach between them by itself. (Maraqi al-Falah) And long and prevents water reaching under it. (Maraqi al-Falah) Dirt: that is, dirt of nails, whether for the villager or city dweller in the soundest, so washing is valid with its presence. (Maraqi al-Falah 63) And if it harms him: if passing water over the medicine harms him, he wipes over it, and if it also harms him to leave it, then if nothing harms him, it is determined to the extent that does not harm him, so if cold water harms him but not hot, and he is able, then it is obligatory upon him to use hot. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 63) It is permissible etc.: know that the place of permissibility of passing water over the medicine is if it does not exceed the top of the crack; if it exceeds, it is obligatory to wash what is under the excess as in Ibn Amir al-Hajj, and similar in al-Durr and al-Mujtaba, but it should be qualified by lack of harm. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 63) From. Sunnas of wudu. And wiping or washing is not repeated on the place of hair after shaving it, nor washing by cutting his nail even if from janabah and his mustache. Not repeated. With cutting. Section on the sunnas of wudu. Eighteen things are sunnah in wudu: washing the hands to the wrists, saying the basmalah at the beginning, and the siwak at its beginning even with the finger when it is absent, and rinsing the mouth three times even with one handful, and nasally?
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling detailing the obligations (wajibat) and conditions (shurut) of wudu in the Hanafi school. It begins by stating that the externalt of a thick beard must be washed—this is the relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi), overruling other opinions of one-third or wiping. For a thin beard, water must reach the skin. Hair that hangs below the face circle is not obligatory to wash. When lips or fingers are closed, the hidden parts need not be washed unless water cannot reach them. Long nails covering the fingertip or any substance like dough that prevents water requires washing underneath. Ordinary dirt under nails does not invalidate, nor do flea droppings. A tight ring must be moved. If washing cracked feet causes pain, passing water over the medicine is permissible. The removal of physical barriers (like wax) is a condition for wudu's validity; residue of oil does not count as a barrier. The commentary clarifies that the thick beard is one where the skin is not visible, and the sunnah is to wipe the hanging part of the beard. For medicine on cracks, if it exceeds the crack's top, the excess must be removed and washed. The text then transitions to the sunnahs of wudu, listing them: washing hands to wrists, basmalah, siwak (even with finger if no stick), and rinsing the mouth three times.

Key Terms
اللحية الكثة (al-lihyah al-kaththah): The thick beard where the skin is not visible.
المسترسل (al-mustarsal): Hair that hangs below the face circle (beard length).
المنانع (al-mana'i'): Substances like wax or dough that block water from skin.
الخاتم الضيق (al-khatim al-dayyiq): A tight ring that prevents water reaching the finger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is not required as long as water reaches the skin.

Key Takeaway
Washing the exterior of a thick beard, removing physical barriers, and moving a tight ring are obligatory in wudu; neglecting any invalidates it.

The Eighteen Sunnahs of Wudu
Listing of recommended acts in wudu with definitions and clarifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sunnah acts of wudu mentioned in the text and explain the Hanafi definition of sunnah.

Core Idea
Sunnah acts in wudu are recommended; omitting them is not sinful but consistent neglect is disliked.

The Hanafi school outlines eighteen recommended acts (sunan) in wudu. This lesson details the first four: washing hands to wrists, saying the basmalah at the very beginning, using a siwak, and rinsing the mouth. Understanding these helps distinguish obligatory from recommended acts in daily purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah acts
List each sunnah mentioned in the passage: washing hands to wrists, basmalah at the beginning, siwak at the beginning, and madmadah three times. Note any conditions (e.g., basmalah only counts at the start).
The text says 'eighteen things are sunnah' but only details these four.
2
Understand the definition of sunnah
The passage defines sunnah technically as a method in religion by word or deed without obligation (fard) and without disapproval (wajib). It is not a specificity of the Prophet.
This contrasts with fard (obligatory) and wajib (necessary but with lighter proof).
3
Apply the details
For each sunnah, note the specific ruling: e.g., if you forget basmalah and remember during, you do not get the sunnah; siwak with finger only when stick is absent; madmadah requires filling the mouth, but spitting is better.
These details come from the commentary (Maraqi al-Falah et al.).

يسن في الوضوء ثمانية عشر شيئاً: غسل اليدين إلى الرسغين، والتسمية ابتداء،
في ابتداء الوضوء

وصلية تناول الماء مرة باليد
ولا يعاد أي إذا غسل ولو من جنابة، أو توضأ ولو بعد حدث موجب للوضوء، ثم حلق الشعر، أو غسل ثم قص ظفره وشاربه لا يعاد الغسل؛ لأن الفرض سقط، والساقط لا يعود، ولكنه يستحب الغسل. يسن: السنة لغة: الطريقة ولو سيئة، واصطلاحاً: طريقة مسلوكة في الدين بقول أو فعل من غير لزوم – خرج به الفرض – ولا إنكار - خرج به الواجب - على تاركها، وليست خصوصية - خرج به ما هو من خصائصه كصوم الوصال - ثمانية عشر: ذكر العدد تسهيلاً للطالب لا للحصر. (مراقي الفلاح) غسل اليدين: أطلقه فشمل ما إذا استيقظ من نوم أو لا، ولكنه أكد في الذي استيقظ. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٥] الرسغين: تثنية رسغ بضم الراء وسكون السين المهملة وبالغين المعجمة: المفصل الذي بين الساعد والكف وبين الساق والقدم. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٥] والتسمية المنقول عن السلف، وقيل عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في لفظها: "بسم الله العظيم، والحمد لله على دين الإسلام"، وقيل: الأفضل "بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم"؛ لعموم "كل أمر ذي بال" الحديث. [ مراقي الفلاح: ٦٧] ابتداءً حتى لو نسيها فتذكرها في خلاله وسمى لا تحصل له السنة، بخلاف الأكل؛ لأن الوضوء عمل واحد، وكل لقمة فعل مستأنف ؛ لقوله : من توضأ وذكر اسم الله فإنه يظهر جسده كله، توضاً و لم يذكر اسم الله لم يطهر إلا موضع الوضوء". [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٧] والسواك: بكسر السين اسم للاستياك وللعود أيضًا، والمراد الأول [مراقي الفلاح: ٦٧] ووقته المسنون في ابتدائه، قال الزيلعي في "شرح الكنز": والصحيح أنهما مستحبان - يعني السواك والتسمية -؛ لأنهما ليسا من خصائص الوضوء. [تبيين الحقائق: ٣٥/١] ولو بالإصبع إلخ : أي ولو كان الاستياك بالإصبع عند فقد السواك أو فقد أسنانه أو ضرر بفمه أفاد بقوله: عند فقده أنه لا يسن السواك بالإصبع عند وجود السواك كما في "الكافي". والمضمضة: هي لغة: التحريك، واصطلاحاً: استيعاب الماء جميع الفم، وفي اللغة: التحريك، والإدارة والمج ليسا بشرط، فلو شرب الماء عباً أجزأه، ولو شرب مصاً لا يجزئه كما في "الفتح"، لكن الأفضل أن يمجه؛ لأنه ماء مستعمل كما في السراج". [ مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٩]
ومن
Section on the sunnas of wudu. Eighteen things are sunnah in wudu: washing the hands to the wrists, saying the basmalah at the beginning, and the siwak at its beginning even with the finger when it is absent, and rinsing the mouth three times even with one handful, and nasally? And it is not repeated: meaning if he washed even from janabah, or performed wudu even after an event requiring wudu, then shaved his hair, or washed then cut his nail and mustache, the washing is not repeated because the obligation has fallen and what falls does not return, but washing is recommended. Sunnah: linguistically: a way even if bad; technically: a method followed in religion by word or deed without obligation – excludes fard – and without disapproval – excludes wajib – upon its abandoner, and it is not a specificity – excludes what is specific to him like fasting wisal. Eighteen: mentioning the number is to facilitate the student, not for limitation. (Maraqi al-Falah) Washing the hands: it is general and includes whether he woke from sleep or not, but it is emphasized for the one who woke. [Maraqi al-Falah 65] The wrists: dual of rusgh with damma on ra and sukun on seen and ghayn: the joint between forearm and palm and between leg and foot. [Maraqi al-Falah 65] And the basmalah reported from the Salaf, and it is reported from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in its wording: 'In the name of Allah the Great, and praise be to Allah for the religion of Islam', and it is said that the best is 'In the name of Allah the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful' due to the generality of the hadith 'Every matter of importance'. [Maraqi al-Falah 67] At the beginning: even if he forgot and remembered during it and said it, he does not attain the sunnah, unlike eating because wudu is one action and each mouthful is a separate action; due to his saying: whoever performs wudu and mentions Allah's name, his whole body is purified; whoever performs wudu and does not mention Allah's name, only the site of wudu is purified. [Maraqi al-Falah 67] And siwak: with kasr on sin, it is the name for the act of using a siwak stick and also for the stick itself, and the intended meaning is the first. [Maraqi al-Falah 67] And its recommended time is at its beginning. Al-Zayla'i said in Sharh al-Kanz: the correct view is that both (siwak and basmalah) are recommended because they are not specific to wudu. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/35] And even with the finger etc.: meaning even if using the siwak with the finger when the siwak stick is absent, or when he has no teeth, or harm to his mouth; his statement 'when it is absent' indicates that siwak with the finger is not sunnah when the stick is present, as in al-Kafi. And al-madmadah: linguistically: movement; technically: filling the entire mouth with water; linguistically: movement, and swishing and spitting are not conditions; if he drinks water in gulps, it suffices him; if he drinks by sucking, it does not suffice him as in al-Fath, but it is better to spit it out because it is used water as in al-Siraj. [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 69] And from.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement listing the sunnah acts (mustahabbat) of wudu and providing definitions. The opening of the section (previous page) states that eighteen things are sunnah; here the first few are detailed. The first sunnah is washing the hands to the wrists (including the joint). Second is saying the basmalah at the very beginning of wudu; if forgotten and remembered during, the sunnah is not attained because wudu is a single continuous act. Third is using a siwak at the beginning; if no siwak stick is available, the finger may be used, but not if the stick is available. Fourth is rinsing the mouth (madmadah) three times, even with a single handful of water; it is defined as filling the entire mouth with water; swallowing is not required, but spitting out is better as the water becomes used. The commentary also clarifies that the siwak and basmalah are not specific to wudu but recommended generally. Additionally, the text repeats the ruling that washing is not repeated after shaving hair or cutting nails because the obligation has already been fulfilled; however, it is recommended (mustahabb) to wash again for the sake of renewing purification.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): A religious practice without obligation; its omission is not sinful but leaving it consistently is disliked.
المضمضة (al-madmadah): Filling the entire mouth with water and swishing it, then spitting it out.
السواك (al-siwak): The act of cleaning teeth using a siwak stick or finger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Twenty
D) Twelve

Key Takeaway
The sunnah acts of wudu are recommended practices; knowing them helps complete one's wudu with reward.

Ruling on Not Repeating Washing After Shaving Hair or Cutting Nails
Ruling statement with explanatory reason

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether ghusl or wudu must be repeated after shaving hair or cutting nails, and explain the legal principle behind it.

Core Idea
Once the fard of washing is fulfilled, it does not return—removing hair or nails does not necessitate repeating purification.

A common question after performing ghusl or wudu: if you shave your head or cut your nails, does your purification become invalid? The Hanafi school addresses this clearly: the obligation has already been discharged. This lesson explains the ruling and the underlying principle that the obligation does not revive merely due to changes in the body.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Recognize that the act in question is performing ghusl (or wudu). Understand that the ruling of ghusl is fard (obligatory) when required, but our focus is on the act of washing after it has been completed.
The source text begins with 'ولا يعاد الغسل' meaning washing is not repeated.
2
Recognize the scenario
The scenario is: after washing (ghusl or wudu), one shaves hair or cuts nails. Consider whether this nullifies the previous washing.
The text mentions shaving hair, cutting nails, and even shaving the mustache.
3
Understand the author's ruling
The ruling is that washing is not repeated. The author emphasizes 'لا يعاد' (it is not repeated) and clarifies that this applies even if the washing was from janabah (major impurity) or after a minor event that required wudu.
The ruling is definitive: no obligation to repeat.
4
Grasp the legal cause (illah)
The reason given: 'لأن الفرض سقط، والساقط لا يعود' (because the obligation has fallen, and what has fallen does not return). This is the key principle.
The fard of washing is attached to the body at the time of washing; later removal of hair/nails does not revive that obligation.
5
Note the recommendation
Although not obligatory, the author notes it is 'mustahabb' (recommended) to wash again. This shows the ruling is not absolute prohibition but non-obligation with preference.
The text ends with 'ولكنه يستحب الغسل'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يعاد المسح ولا الغسل على موضع الشعر بعد حلقه، ولا الغسل بقص ظفره ولو من جنابة وشاربه. ولا يعاد أي إذا غسل ولو من جنابة، أو توضأ ولو بعد حدث موجب للوضوء، ثم حلق الشعر، أو غسل ثم قص ظفره وشاربه لا يعاد الغسل؛ لأن الفرض سقط، والساقط لا يعود، ولكنه يستحب الغسل.
And wiping is not repeated nor washing on the place of hair after shaving it, nor washing by cutting his nail even if from janabah and his mustache. It is not repeated: meaning if he washed even from janabah, or performed wudu even after an event necessitating wudu, then shaved his hair, or washed then cut his nail and mustache, the washing is not repeated because the obligation has fallen, and what has fallen does not return, but it is recommended to wash.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining that after performing ghusl or wudu, if one subsequently shaves hair or cuts nails, the washing does not need to be repeated. The author clarifies that this applies even if the washing was from janabah (major impurity) or wudu (minor impurity). The reasoning is that the obligatory washing (fard) has already been fulfilled. Once the obligation is discharged, it does not return merely because the body parts change (hair removed, nails cut). However, the author notes that it is mustahabb (recommended) to repeat the washing voluntarily, as a matter of preference, not obligation. This is a Hanafi position emphasizing that the obligation of taharah is attached to the body parts at the time of washing, not to the hair or nails after removal.

Key Terms
الغسل (al-ghusl): The act of washing the entire body (major ablution) or washing a limb; in this context, it refers to the obligatory washing that has already been performed.
الفرض (al-fard): Obligatory act; here it means the mandatory washing that has been fulfilled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) He must perform wudu instead of ghusl.
D) He must repeat both ghusl and wudu.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of washing does not return after its fulfillment, even if the washed body parts change.

The 18 Sunnah Acts of Wudu and Their Hanafi Definitions
Enumerates and defines the eighteen sunnah acts of wudu with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the 18 sunnah acts of wudu and explain the ruling and manner of each according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
18 sunnah acts perfect wudu; missing them does not invalidate but loses reward.

This lesson covers the detailed enumeration of the sunnah (recommended) acts of wudu as taught in the Hanafi school. The text from Nur al-Idah, with commentary from Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, provides not just a list but also the proper method and rulings for each act. Understanding these sunnah acts helps you perform a more complete and rewarded wudu while distinguishing them from the obligatory elements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the 18 acts
Read the Arabic text carefully and list the 18 sunnah acts of wudu. The author explicitly numbers them: washing hands to wrists, tasmiyah, siwak, madmadah, etc.
Some acts have sub-rules, like the number of repetitions.
2
Understand the definitions
For each act, note its technical definition and manner as explained in the commentary. For example, madmadah is defined as circulating water throughout the mouth, and istinshaq as reaching water to the soft part of the nose.
Pay attention to exceptions, e.g., for fasting persons.
3
Classify the ruling level
Identify which acts are sunnah muakkadah (emphatic) and which are ordinary sunnah. The first washing of each limb is fard; subsequent washings are sunnah muakkadah.
The text states: 'المرة الأولى فرض والثنتان بعدها سنتان مؤكدتان'.
4
Note conditions and exceptions
Observe conditions like continuity (wala') being relative to body, time, and place, and the prohibition of exaggeration for fasting persons.
Continuity is not required if the skin absorbs water or the air is dry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل [في سنن الوضوء] يسن في الوضوء ثمانية عشر شيئاً: غسل اليدين إلى الرسغين، والتسمية ابتداء، في ابتداء الوضوء والسواك في ابتدائه ولو بالإصبع عند فقده، والمضمضة ثلاثاً ولو بغرفة، وصلية تناول الماء مرة باليد والاستنشاق بثلاث غرفات والمبالغة في المضمضة والاستنشاق لغير الصائم، وتخليل اللحية الكثة بكف ماء من أسفلها، وتخليل الأصابع، وتثليث الغسل، واستيعاب كلها الرأس بالمسح مرة، ومسح الأذنين ولو بماء الرأس، والدَّلك، والولاء والنية ... كمسح الجبيرة والتيمم والاستنشاق لغة هو النشق: جذب الماء ونحوه بريح الأنف إليه، واصطلاحاً: إيصال الماء إلى المارن، وهو من ما لان من الأنف، أفاد أن الجذب بريح الأنف ليس شرطاً فيه شرعاً مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٩] والمبالغة: قال الإمام خواهر زاده هي في المضمضة الغرغرة، وهي تردد الماء في الحلق، وفي الاستنشاق أن يجذب الماء بنفسه إلى ما اشتد أنفه. قال في "البحر": وهو الأولى. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٠] من لغير الصائم قيد به، فإن الصائم لا يبالغ في المضمضة ولا في الاستنشاق؛ خشية إفساد الصوم، ولو كان الصوم صوم نفل وتخليل اللحية هو تفريق الشعر من جهة الأسفل إلى فوق، ويكون بعد غسل الوجه ثلاثاً بكف ماء فقوله: "بكف" متعلق بـ"يكون" المقدر. (مراقي الفلاح، حاشية الطحطاوي) الأصابع: وكيفيته في اليدين: إدخال بعضها في بعض، وفي الرجلين: بإصبع من يده، ويكفي عنه إدخالها في الماء الجاري ونحوه مراقي الفلاح (۷۱] وتثليث وفي البحر": السنة تكرار الغسلات المستوعبات لا الغرفات، والمرة الأولى فرض، والثنتان بعدها سنتان مؤكدتان على الصحيح [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧١] الغسل: قيد به؛ لأن المسح لا يسن تكراره عندنا (مراقي الفلاح واستيعاب الرأس إلخ وكيفيته: أن يضع من كل واحدة من اليدين ثلاث أصابع على مقدم رأسه، ولا يضع الإبهام والمسبحة، ويجافي كفيه ويمدهما إلى القفا، ثم يضع كفيه على مؤخر رأسه ويمدهما إلى المقدم، ثم يمسح ظاهر أذنيه بإبهاميه وباطنهما بمسبحتيه، كذا في "المستصفى" [العناية: ۲۹/۱] ومسح الأذنين بأن يمسح ظاهرهما بالإبهامين، وداخلهما بالسبابتين، وهو المختار كما في "المعراج"، ويدخل الخنصرين في جحريهما ويحركهما. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٢] والولاء هو بكسر الواو : المتابعة بغسل الأعضاء قبل جفاف السابق مع الاعتدال جسدا وزمانا ومكانا، فلو كان بدنه يتشرب الماء، أو كان الهواء شديداً، أو كان المكان حاراً يجفّف الماء سريعا، فلا يعدُّ تاركا له، ولو كان طرياً لا يجففه إلا في مدة مستطيلة وتأنى في الوضوء لا يكون آتياً بسنة الولاء [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ٧٢] القلب على الفعل، واصطلاحاً توجه القلب لإيجاد الفعل جزماً، ووقتها بعد الاستنجاء؛ فعله قربة، وكيفيتها: أن ينوي رفع الحدث أو إقامة الصلاة، أو ينوي الوضوء أو امتثال الأمر، والنية: وهي لغة عزم ومحلها القلب، فإن نطق بها ليجمع بين فعل القلب واللسان استحبه المشايخ. [مراقي الفلاح: ٧٣]
Section on the sunan of wudu. It is sunnah in wudu eighteen things: washing the hands up to the wrists, the tasmiyah at the beginning, at the beginning of wudu and the siwak at its beginning even with the finger in its absence, and rinsing the mouth three times even with one handful, and the manner of taking water with the hand once, and snuffing water up the nose with three handfuls, and exaggerating in rinsing the mouth and snuffing water for the non-fasting person, and passing the fingers through the thick beard with a palm of water from below it, and passing the fingers through the fingers, and triple washing, and covering all of the head with wiping once, and wiping the ears even with the water of the head, and rubbing, and continuity, and intention... like wiping over the splint and tayammum. And istinshaq linguistically is the inhalation: pulling water and the like with the wind of the nose to it, and terminologically: reaching water to the maran, which is the soft part of the nose, so it is understood that pulling with the wind of the nose is not a condition in it legally. [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 69] And exaggeration: Imam Khuwahar Zada said it is in mouth rinsing the gargling, which is causing water to move back and forth in the throat, and in istinshaq that he pulls water with his breath to the extent that his nose becomes intense. He said in 'al-Bahr': that is more appropriate. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 70] From 'for the non-fasting' is a qualification; for the fasting person does not exaggerate in mouth rinsing nor in istinshaq for fear of spoiling the fast, even if the fast is a supererogatory fast. And tahlil al-lihyah is separating the hair from the bottom upward, and it is after washing the face three times with a palm of water, so his statement 'with a palm' is associated with the implied 'it is'. (Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi) The fingers: its manner in the hands: inserting some into others, and in the feet: with a finger from his hand, and it suffices to insert them into running water etc. [Maraqi al-Falah 71] And triple [washing]: In al-Bahr: the sunnah is repeating the complete washings, not the handfuls, and the first time is fard, and the two after it are two emphatic sunnahs according to the correct. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 71] Washing: has been specified; because wiping is not sunnah to repeat according to us. (Maraqi al-Falah) And covering the head etc.: its manner: he places from each of his hands three fingers on the front of his head, and does not place the thumb and index finger, and separates his palms and extends them to the nape, then places his palms on the back of his head and extends them to the front, then wipes the outside of his ears with his thumbs and their insides with his index fingers, as in al-Mustasfa. [al-Inayah: 1/29] And wiping the ears: he wipes their outside with his thumbs, and their inside with his index fingers, and that is the chosen as in al-Mi'raj, and he inserts his little fingers into their openings and moves them. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 72] And al-wala' (continuity) is with kasr of the waw: following consecutively by washing the limbs before the drying of the previous one with moderation of body, time, and place; so if his body absorbs water, or the air is strong, or the place is hot and dries water quickly, then he is not considered to have abandoned it, and if it is moist not drying except in an extended period and he delays in wudu, he is not performing the sunnah of continuity. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah: 72] And intention: it is linguistically resolve of the heart for the action, and terminologically: turning of the heart to bring about the action decisively, and its time is after istinja; its doing is a qurba (act of drawing near to Allah), and its manner: he intends to lift the hadath or to perform the prayer, or he intends wudu or compliance of the command, and its place is the heart; if he pronounces it to combine between the act of the heart and the tongue, the mashayikh recommended it. [Maraqi al-Falah: 73]
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage presents the section on the sunan (recommended acts) of wudu. The author lists eighteen sunan, beginning with washing the hands up to the wrists, saying Bismillah at the start, using the miswak, rinsing the mouth, and so on. The commentary from 'Maraqi al-Falah' and 'Hashiyat al-Tahtawi' provides detailed definitions and rulings for each. For example, the sunnah of washing hands is emphasized for one waking from sleep. The tasmiyah is mentioned with its wording; if forgotten at the beginning and remembered later, the sunnah is not attained because wudu is a single act. The miswak is recommended at the start of wudu, and it can be done with the finger if no stick is available. Rinsing the mouth (madmadah) involves circulating water throughout the mouth, and it is sunnah to do it three times even with one handful. The text also covers istinshaq (sniffing water into the nose), with emphasis for the non-fasting person. It explains the manner of khilal (passing fingers through the beard and fingers), triple washing of limbs, complete wiping of the head, wiping the ears, dalk (rubbing), muwalat (continuity), and niyyah (intention). The commentary clarifies many subtle points, such as the recommendation to wipe the ears with new water or with the water from the head, and that muwalat is relative to climate and body type. The section ends with the definition of niyyah. This is a typical Hanafi treatment emphasizing practical details.

Key Terms
السواك (al-siwaak): The act of cleaning the teeth with a stick (miswak) or with the finger if no stick is available; it is sunnah at the beginning of wudu.
المضمضة (al-madmada): Rinsing the mouth by circulating water throughout the mouth; it is sunnah to do it three times.
الاستنشاق (al-istinshaq): Sniffing water up the nose; it is sunnah to do it three times, with exaggeration for non-fasting persons.
الولاء (al-wala'): Continuity in wudu: washing the next limb before the previous one dries, taking into account body, time, and place conditions.
النية (al-niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform the act of worship; its time is after istinja, and it is recommended to pronounce it verbally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many sunnah acts are there in wudu?
A) 10
B) 12
C) 18
D) 20

Key Takeaway
Wudu has 18 sunnah acts that perfect it; knowing them helps you perform a more complete wudu, but missing them does not invalidate the wudu.
